801 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Bank Bldg. & Equipment Corp. v. Architectural Examining Board


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


153 Conn. 121; 214 A.2d 377; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 409


October 14, 1965, Argued  
October 28, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiffs from certain orders of the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County where a plea in abatement was sustained, Gaffney, J., and judgment was rendered dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a bank and building association and three individuals (association), appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) in favor of defendant Architectural Examining Board of the State of Connecticut, sustaining the Board's plea in abatement on grounds that appeal was not served on the Board within 30 days of its order as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-289, as amended by 1961 Conn. Pub. Acts 335.


OVERVIEW: The association's original appeal from the Board's decision was dismissed because the association had erroneously served the state attorney general instead of the board. The association refiled the appeal under the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-592 and 52-593, which permitted refiling a civil action within one year if it was dismissed otherwise than on the merits. The trial court sustained the Board's plea in abatement to the second appeal. On review, the Board argued that the only statutory procedure for an administrative appeal was under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-289, as amended by 1961 Conn. Pub. Act 335. The court agreed and affirmed the judgment. The court found that the Board was a state-created administrative agency and that if the legislature wished to alter the procedural steps to perfect an administrative appeal it could have provided for them in § 20-289. The court noted that in an earlier ruling it had held that an administrative appeal was not an "action" subject to the refiling provisions for civil cases.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

 

802 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Taylor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


153 Conn. 72; 214 A.2d 362; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 401


June 3, 1965, Argued  
October 7, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of aiding and abetting the sale of narcotics to a minor, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Alcorn, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted him of the crime of aiding and abetting the sale of narcotics to a minor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-267.


OVERVIEW: A minor was arrested and charged with illegal possession of narcotics. The minor agreed to assist the police in apprehending the person who had been his source of narcotics. The minor testified that he was a user of narcotics, that he entered into a plan with the police to make a purchase of heroin, and that the transaction was executed between himself, as buyer, and defendant and his codefendant, as sellers. The minor testified that he placed his order over the telephone with defendant and shortly thereafter met defendant and his codefendant for the purchase. Police officers kept the minor under surveillance during the entire proceedings, and their testimony at the trial served to corroborate that of the minor. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. There was adequate corroborative evidence to support the inference that drugs found near where the sale took place had a common origin with the drugs sold to the minor and were connected to the crime charged. The court rejected defendant's argument that he was denied his constitutional right to a fair trial. There was no indication that the minor was influenced by promises into testifying against defendant and his codefendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aiding and abetting the sale of narcotics to a minor.

 

803 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spellman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


153 Conn. 65; 212 A.2d 413; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 400


June 1, 1965, Argued  
July 21, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of owning and keeping alcoholic liquor with intent to sell, brought to the Circuit Court in the sixth circuit and tried to the court, Williams, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court, which affirmed the judgment; from the judgment of the Appellate Division, the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court in the Sixth Circuit, Appellate Division (Connecticut), that affirmed his conviction of keeping alcoholic liquor with the intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-77, arguing that evidence obtained by a police officer in a search of defendant's automobile was improperly admitted where the officer had neither a search warrant nor a warrant for defendant's arrest.


OVERVIEW: The police officer observed defendant standing next to his car and talking with two people. At the conclusion of their conversation, defendant opened the truck of his car and removed two bottles of alcohol therefrom. As the officer approached, defendant replaced the bottles in the trunk and closed it. The officer asked defendant to open the trunk. Defendant complied, and the officer observed a dozen pints of wine and more than three dozen half-pints of whiskey. The officer arrested defendant, who was charged with keeping alcoholic liquor with the intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-77. Following his conviction and its affirmation on appeal, defendant sought further review. In finding error, the court concluded that the trial court erred in admitting the fruits of the search into evidence and that such error was prejudicial. That defendant complied with the officer's command that he open his trunk did not amount to consent, and the officer had no probable cause to believe that defendant was engaged in an illegal act. As such, no probable cause to execute the search existed, and the evidence was inadmissible against defendant.


OUTCOME: Because there was error, the judgment was set aside, and a new trial was ordered.

 

804 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Verraster v. Tynan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 645; 211 A.2d 150; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 535


May 6, 1965, Argued  
June 1, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining certain questions concerning a statute limiting the registration of new motor vehicles, for an injunction and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Dube, J.; judgment determining a portion of the statute invalid, and appeal by the defendants and by the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both plaintiff, a used car dealer, and defendant motor vehicles commissioner appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) in the used car dealer's declaratory judgment action. The trial court determined that a portion of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-1 (47) defining the phase "ultimate consumer" stifled competition in the automobile business by favoring new car dealers and was therefore unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The used car dealer sought an injunction prohibiting the commissioner from refusing to register used vehicles. The case was tried on a stipulation of facts, and the trial court rendered a judgment that was limited exclusively to a decree that the portion of § 14-1 (47) which defines the phrase "ultimate consumer" in the statute is invalid, null and void. All parties to the action appealed from the limited judgment as rendered. Among the assignments of error, one was directed at the failure of the trial court to determine the issues raised by the pleadings. On review, the court found that the judgment neither granted nor denied a requested injunction, and the issues were not found, nor was judgment rendered, for either party. The judgment did not even purport to answer the specific questions for the determination of which the suit was instituted. The court held that the judgment, as rendered, was clearly inadequate because any judgment, to be adequate, must conform to the pleadings, the issues and the prayers for relief.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the trial court's judgment and set it aside. The court ordered a new trial.

 

805 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kohlfuss


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 625; 211 A.2d 143; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 532


May 4, 1965, Argued  
June 1, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crime of breaking and entering and, in the second part, as a second offender, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County, where the issues under the first part of the information were tried to the court, Shapiro, J., which found the defendant guilty and, the defendant having pleaded guilty to the second part of the information, the court rendered judgment of guilty under both parts; from that judgment the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Fairfield County (Connecticut). An information charged him in the first part with breaking and entering, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-76, and in the second part as a second offender. He pleaded not guilty to the first part but he was found guilty as charged in a bench trial. He pleaded guilty to the second part. A judgment of guilty under both parts was entered.


OVERVIEW: Defendant essentially urged that the evidence was inadequate to support the adjudication of guilt. He was charged with breaking into a gas station. A gas station employee testified that on the night in question he locked all the doors and closed the window of the men's room. A police officer testified that during the night in question, he had seen two men, one of whom he recognized as defendant, coming from the front of the station carrying a large heavy object. The officer apprehended defendant and his companion and found the front door unlocked and ajar. Also the men's room window was open. The floor safe was found outside in the driveway. The court found no error in defendant's conviction and sentence, as the evidence warranted the adjudication of guilt of breaking and entering with intent to steal. Defendant and his companion were alone at the station during the time in question. The court concluded that the fact that no one saw defendant actually breaking into or out of the building, or even inside it, did not preclude a conviction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-76, as the circumstantial evidence was strong enough to prove guilt of the crime charged beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

806 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Zygmont v. Planning & Zoning Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 550; 210 A.2d 172; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 519


March 2, 1965, Argued  
April 27, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the denial of an application for a change of zone, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, Doherty, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal from a decision of defendant zoning commission denying his application to change the zoning classification of his property.


OVERVIEW: The owner applied to the zoning commission to change the classification of his property to allow development of 25 lots for single-family residences. The commission denied the application and the trial court dismissed the owner's appeal from that decision. The court found no error in the trial court's judgment. The commission's decision was supported by evidence showed that the factors of water supply and sewage disposal in the owner's development plan presented a definite public health question, and the commission's decision not to change the classification was not arbitrary, confiscatory, or an abuse of discretion. The court also rejected the owner's claim that the zoning classification of his property was unconstitutional because it had no relationship to health, safety, morals or the general welfare and was a taking of property without just compensation and without due process of law. The basis for the commission's denial of the application showed that the classification had a relationship to public health concerns, and the owner made no showing that the classification deprived him of the ability to put the property to any use.


OUTCOME: There was no error.

 

807 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Fredericks v. Reincke


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 501; 208 A.2d 756; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 509


February 3, 1965, Argued  
March 17, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging unlawful imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Pastore, J.; judgment for the plaintiff nisi, and appeal by him and by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant warden and plaintiff inmate sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which determined in the inmate's habeas corpus case, that the inmate had been denied his right to counsel to perfect his appeal and directed his discharge from prison unless, at his further request, counsel was appointed to pursue his appeal and necessary extensions of time in which to perfect the appeal were granted.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of the crime of robbery with violence. He was represented by a special public defender who, after trial, requested an extension of time to perfect the inmate's appeal. The special public defender notified the inmate that any grounds of appeal would be frivolous and took no other action. The inmate filed a motion for the appointment of counsel which was denied and the inmate's appeal was dismissed. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in habeas corpus. The court found that appointment of counsel was required to ensure the inmate's right to assistance of counsel on appeal was not violated. The court also found that the trial court did not exceed its power in conditioning the inmate's release on the appointment of appellate counsel and that the trial court had the power in a habeas corpus proceeding to dispose of the matter as law and justice required pursuant to 28 U.S.C.S. § 2243. The court also determined that while the trial court did not ordinarily have the authority to allow a late appeal, such authority was proper where on habeas corpus it had been properly determined that a right of appeal required by the federal constitution had been denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court to order the release of the inmate from incarceration unless a special counsel was appointed to represent the inmate on appeal and an extension of time was granted to perfect the inmate's appeal.

 

808 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Wadhams v. Torrington


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 454; 208 A.2d 549; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 502


December 3, 1964, Argued  
March 4, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendant city et al. from making certain pension payments, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Litchfield County and tried to the court, Parmelee, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in Litchfield County (Connecticut), which concluded that defendant city board of trustees was empowered to award pensions to the former mayor and superintendent of public welfare. Plaintiffs filed the action against the board and other defendants to enjoin the board from paying such pensions.


OVERVIEW: The former mayor of the city and the superintendent of public welfare were voted pensions by the board of trustees under 25 Conn. Spec. Laws 1075 § 6. The act provided that any employee who had been in the service of the city for 25 years and who had reached the age of 65 years should be retired. The board could likewise retire any employee who had been continuously in the service of the city for 20 years prior to reaching the age of 65, but such employees were to be paid a proportionate pension. Both the mayor and superintendent applied for pensions. Neither asked to be retired, and neither had reached the age of 65. Each applicant sought the pension under the second half of the statute. Plaintiffs filed suit to enjoin payment of the pensions and contended that the board acted illegally. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the board. Plaintiffs appealed, and the court found error, set aside the judgment, and remanded. The court held that the second part of the statute did not confer upon any 20-year employee who had not reached the age of 65 the right to voluntary retirement, as claimed by the mayor and superintendent.


OUTCOME: The court found error, set aside the judgment, and remanded the case with direction to render a declaratory judgment and a permanent injunction in accordance with the court's opinion.

 

809 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Patterson v. Dempsey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 431; 207 A.2d 739; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 500


January 7, 1965, Argued  
February 25, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Actions, one for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of the veto by the defendant governor of certain sections of an appropriations act, and for other relief, and the other in the nature of mandamus, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County by transfer from the Superior Court in New London County and tried to the court, Dube, J.; judgments in favor of the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgments directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenged the decisions of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which entered judgment in favor of defendants, the Governor, the Secretary of State, and the Comptroller, contending that the Governor's partial veto of a bill was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought unsuccessfully to have the trial court declare the Governor's partial veto of legislation invalid, and to issue a writ of mandamus requiring the Secretary of State and the Comptroller General to comply with the vetoed provisions. The court agreed that the Governor's veto was unconstitutional because (1) Conn. Const. art. IV, § 15 did not authorize the Governor to veto general legislation contained in appropriations bills, and (2) including such general legislation contrary to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2-35 merely repealed that statute by implication rather than making the general legislation illegal. The court found that two of the three vetoed provisions were consistent with legislative authority under Conn. Const. art. IV, § 23 to assign duties to the Comptroller. However, the court held that the third provision was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt because it infringed on the Comptroller's authority under § 23.


OUTCOME: By agreement of the parties, the court entered judgment in favor of the Secretary of State. However, the court modified the judgments against plaintiff to reflect that the Governor's veto was invalid, that two of the three vetoed measures were valid, and that the third measure unconstitutionally infringed on the duties of the Comptroller.

 

810 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 343; 206 A.2d 835; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 488


November 5, 1964, Argued  
January 26, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Shannon, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a residence where he had worked previously. Defendant repeatedly attacked a woman and her daughter. Defendant killed the woman, but the daughter survived. Defendant fled, but was eventually caught in Georgia. Detectives from Connecticut went to Georgia and discussed the case with defendant. While in Georgia, the detectives examined defendant's vehicle without a search warrant. Certain objects taken from the car were submitted to the state laboratory in Connecticut for examination. No search warrant was obtained. The daughter's blood and hair were found in defendant's car and introduced at trial over objection. The court held that the blood and hair were inadmissible because they were the result of an illegal search and seizure. No consent was given for the search. The search was not incident to a lawful arrest because the search occurred two days after the arrest and occurred in a different town from where defendant was being held. The error could not be regarded as harmless because it was impossible to say that admission of the evidence did not contribute to the verdict, especially since it was used to bolster the daughter's testimony.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial.

 

811 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Edward Balf Co. v. East Granby


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 319; 207 A.2d 58; 1965 Conn. LEXIS 484


October 13, 1964, Argued  
January 20, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining whether the plaintiff could lawfully operate a stone quarry and stone crushing plant on its land, and for an injunction, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Sidor, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant appealed a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County, Connecticut, which found in favor of defendants, a town and certain individuals, in an action by the applicant seeking a declaratory judgment determining whether the applicant could lawfully operate a stone quarry and stone crushing plant on its land and seeking an injunction.


OVERVIEW: The action was tried in conjunction with the applicant's appeal of the zoning commission's decision to deny his permit application. In that appeal, the applicant argued that the town did not comply with statutory procedural requirements in passing a new zoning ordinance. The trial court sustained that appeal but found in favor of defendants in the applicant's action for declaratory relief and an injunction, finding that the invalid ordinance had been cured by its readoption. The applicant's subsequent applications were denied. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the ordinance in effect at the time the applicant brought the action did not apply. In actions for injunctions and declaratory relief, where the relief was prospective, the law to be applied was the law that had developed at the time of trial. The court found that even the filing of an application for a permit did not restrict the right of a zoning commission to amend an ordinance by changing the grounds for approval of the permit. The court stated that the town's notice of the change in the zoning ordinance, upon its readoption, was sufficient to comply with the procedural requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

812 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


De Forest & Hotchkiss Co. v. Planning & Zoning Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 262; 205 A.2d 774; 1964 Conn. LEXIS 352


November 6, 1964, Argued  
December 15, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in the first case, from the refusal of the defendant to change the zonal classification of certain property, and, in the second case, action for a declaratory judgment, an injunction and other relief, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County and tried to the court, Doherty, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal in the first case and judgment for the defendants in the second case, and appeals by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of the judgment of the court of Common Pleas in New Haven County (Connecticut), which rendered judgments in favor of appellee planning and zoning commission (commission) in an action challenging the commission's refusal to change a portion of the company's property from residential to industrial and in a declaratory judgment action that alleged the zoning regulations were illegal and void.


OVERVIEW: The trial court rendered a judgment in favor of the planning and zoning commission (commission) in an action filed by the company challenging the commission's refusal to change a portion of the company's property from residential to industrial. The trial court also rendered a judgment in favor of the commission in a declaratory judgment action that had been filed by the company, which was seeking a declaration that the zoning regulations were illegal and void as to the company's property and also injunctive relief against the enforcement of the zoning regulation placing the company's property in a residential zone. The trial court's judgments were affirmed on appeal. The court found that the commission's denial of the application for a change of zone was reasonable because the granting of the request would not conform to the comprehensive plan. The court also found that the claim of unconstitutionality was without merit because, contrary to the company's contention, the company's land had not been confiscated and rendered unsalable. The court pointed out that the maximum possible enrichment of a particular landowner was not a controlling purpose of zoning.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

813 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Griffiths


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


152 Conn. 48; 203 A.2d 144; 1964 Conn. LEXIS 323


June 4, 1964, Argued  
July 14, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for an order for the support of beneficiaries of public assistance, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County and tried to the court, Armentano, J.; judgment for the state and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas in New Heaven County, (Connecticut), which found pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-90 that he was responsible for the contribution of a monthly amount of money to his daughter for her support.


OVERVIEW: The daughter applied for public assistance when she had one child and while the child's father was in the reformatory. The State granted assistance to the daughter. Her father offered to take her and her child into his home and to provide for them there because he did not want then to receive aid to dependent children assistance. The daughter was pregnant at the time. Conferences concerning the father's contribution for the daughter's support, but not for the support of her illegitimate children were held, but the father refused to contribute. The father was then notified by letter that he had been found to be a legally liable relative and pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-90, and was able to contribute a monthly amount for his daughter's support. The father's major assertion on appeal was that his daughter was ineligible for aid because of her refusal to live with him. The court found no error. The court held that the father's failure to take advantage of the hearing and appeal provided for in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-2a and 17-2b precluded him from raising, on appeal, issues which could and should have been raised in a hearing before a commissioner.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

814 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. De Witt School, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


151 Conn. 631; 201 A.2d 472; 1964 Conn. LEXIS 248


November 8, 1963, Argued  
May 20, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from using certain descriptive matter in the designation of the character of the defendant school, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County, where a demurrer to the substituted complaint was overruled, Longo, J., and, the defendants failing to plead further, judgment was rendered for the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school appealed an order of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which rendered judgment in favor of plaintiff State in the State's action for an injunction restraining the school from using certain descriptive matter in the designation of the character of the school after overruling a demurrer filed by the school.


OVERVIEW: The State filed an action to enjoin the school from operating a school in a manner alleged to be in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-6 (c). A temporary injunction was granted, following which a substituted complaint was filed. The substituted complaint alleged that the school was operated without a license or a certificate of accreditation from the state board of education and that it has no authority to grant degrees under any of the provisions of § 10-6. The trial court overruled a demurrer to the substituted complaint, and, upon the failure of the school to plead over, judgment was rendered for the State, from which the school appealed. The court set aside the judgment in favor of the State and remanded with direction to sustain the demurrer in favor of the school, holding that although it may be argued that schools created prior to a certain date would be less likely to mislead the public, such reason was not sufficient to sustain the discrimination. The court found § 10-6 unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment in favor of the State and remanded with direction to sustain the demurrer in favor of the school.

State v. Griswold


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


151 Conn. 544; 200 A.2d 479; 1964 Conn. LEXIS 231


November 12, 1963, Argued  
April 28, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations charging the defendants with the crime of assisting and abetting the use of drugs, medicinal articles and instruments for the purpose of preventing conception, brought to the Circuit Court in the sixth circuit and tried to the court, Lacey, J.; judgment of guilty in each case which, on appeal, the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court affirmed; from its judgment the defendants, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of judgments from the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court (Connecticut), convicting them of assisting and abetting the use of drugs, medicinal articles, and instruments for the purpose of preventing conception.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of assisting and abetting the use of drugs, medicinal articles, and instruments for the purpose of preventing conception. The court found no error in the convictions, holding that the every attack made on Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-32 by defendants had been made and already rejected by the courts. The court further held that courts were not permitted to interfere with the exercise by a state of the police power to conserve the public safety and welfare, including health and morals, where the law had a real and substantial relation to the accomplishment of those objects.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment convicting them of assisting and abetting the use of drugs, medicinal articles, and instruments for the purpose of preventing conception.

 

816 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Coyle v. Housing Authority of Danbury


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


151 Conn. 421; 198 A.2d 709; 1964 Conn. LEXIS 205


January 8, 1964, Argued  
February 25, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action seeking, in the first count, a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of an act concerning the city limits of Danbury, and other relief, and, in the second count, an injunction restraining the named defendant from carrying out its plans for the erection of a low-income housing project, and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Klau, J.; judgment dismissing the first count for lack of jurisdiction and finding the issues on the second count for the named defendant, and appeal by the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: Error in form of judgment; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) in favor of appellee city housing authority in the property owners' action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of an act concerning the limits of the city, and for an injunction restraining the housing authority from erecting a low-income housing project.


OVERVIEW: The property owners filed action challenging the constitutionality of 25 Conn. Spec. Laws 839, which authorized the city to expand its boundaries when the housing authority purchased land for the erection of low-income housing. The property owners all owned property within 1,600 feet of the proposed site, and also sought an injunction barring the low-income housing. The trial court found for the housing authority on the first count holding that it lacked jurisdiction to consider the constitutionality, and rendered judgment for the authority on the second count. The property owners appealed and on appeal the court held that the property owners had failed to show that any rights of theirs were endangered by the act, and that their mere status as taxpayers and residents of the community did not confer standing absent a showing of irreparable injury. The court therefore affirmed the trial court's judgment on the declaratory action, but directed that the trial court enter a judgment dismissing the injunction action for lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the declaratory action judgment, entering a judgment setting aside the trial court's judgment on the injunction action, directing that the trial court enter a judgment dismissing the action for lack of jurisdiction.

 

817 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Stapleton v. Lombardo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


151 Conn. 414; 198 A.2d 697; 1964 Conn. LEXIS 203


January 7, 1964, Argued  
February 25, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants Lombardo from operating a restaurant where liquor is sold, and for other relief, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Johnson, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers challenged a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut) denying their action for an injunction barring defendant restaurant owners from relocating their restaurant liquor permit to a new location.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, owners of real property in the forum town, filed suit for an injunction barring the restaurant owners from relocating their liquor permit to their newly relocated restaurant. The taxpayers also sought a finding that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-52 was unconstitutional. The trial court found for the restaurant owners, and the taxpayers appealed. On appeal the court held that while the record was unclear, the taxpayers were found to have failed to show that they would suffer an irreparable injury, necessary for an injunction to issue, and that the constitutionality of the statute was incidental to the injunctive action. The court held that the taxpayers' complaint merely alleged that they were aggrieved by the granting of the permit, which was not the equivalent of an irreparable injury. The court therefore held that the taxpayers had failed to meet their burden in the equitable action for an injunction. The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

818 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Dooley v. Town Plan & Zoning Com.


Nos. 78978, 79000, 79219, 79251


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


151 Conn. 304; 197 A.2d 770; 1964 Conn. LEXIS 186


October 2, 1963, Argued  
January 21, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals by the plaintiffs from the action of the defendant in changing the classification of their properties from residence B zone to flood plain district and from the defendant's subsequent action in amending the regulations for the flood plain district, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Johnson, J.; judgments dismissing the appeals, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of the decision from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal of appellee zoning commission's ruling that changed the classification of their properties from residence B zone to flood plain district.


OVERVIEW: The zoning commission amended the zoning regulations of Fairfield, Connecticut, by creating a flood plain district. The zoning of the landowners' property was thus changed from residence B zone to flood plain district. The landowners contended that the application of the new regulations to their property constituted the taking of property without compensation and without due process of law in violation of the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments and in violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 11. The trial court dismissed the landowners' appeals from the zoning commission's decision. In reversing on appeal, the court held that: (1) the uses permitted under Fairfield, Conn., Zoning Regulations § 22.2 (1960) placed such limitations on the use of the landowners' property that the enforcement of the regulation amounted to a practical confiscation of the property, for all practical purposes rendering the landowners' use of the property impossible and reducing its value by at least 75 percent; and (2) because the change in zoning, insofar as it affected the landowners' property, was unreasonable and confiscatory, it violated the Fourteenth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment from the trial court, which dismissed the landowners' appeals from the action of the zoning commission changing the classification of their properties to flood plain district. The court remanded the case to the trial court, holding that the regulations pertaining to the flood plain district could have no application to the landowners' property and directing the trial court to sustain their appeals.

 

819 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Horwitz v. Waterford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


151 Conn. 320; 197 A.2d 636; 1964 Conn. LEXIS 188


November 6, 1963, Argued  
January 21, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of an ordinance against building on a lot abutting an unaccepted street, and for an injunction and other relief, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New London County and tried to the court, Sidor, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs and appeal by the defendants.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a town and its building inspector, challenged a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in New London County (Connecticut), which was entered in favor of plaintiff applicants in a declaratory judgment proceeding, determining that an ordinance against building on a lot abutting an unaccepted street was unconstitutional and granting an injunction preventing its enforcement against the applicants.


OVERVIEW: The town enacted an ordinance the prohibited the erection of a building and the issuance of a building permit for the erection of a building on a lot abutting an unaccepted highway or street. The zoning and planning commission denied the applicants' petition for a variance to permit the construction of a home on their land and the building inspector denied the applicants' request for a building permit. The applicants brought an action seeking a declaration that the ordinance was unconstitutional as applied to their land. The trial court ruled that the ordinance was unconstitutional and issued an injunction restraining the enforcement of the ordinance against the applicants. On appeal, the court found no error. The town's zoning regulations limited the use of the applicants' land to residence purposes only. There was no land available to enable the applicants to satisfy the requirements for a town street. The application of the ordinance to the applicants' land was harsh in comparison with the trivial public benefit, if any, that might result from its enforcement. The ordinance was confiscatory as it prevented the effective use of the applicant's land for any purpose allowed by law.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the grant of an injunction to the applicants.

Lessner v. Zoning Board of Appeals


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


151 Conn. 165; 195 A.2d 437; 1963 Conn. LEXIS 325


October 10, 1963, Argued  
October 29, 1963, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant board in granting a variance of the zoning regulations to allow the construction of a house on an undersized lot, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Speziale, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed her appeal from a decision of defendant zoning board granting a variance to defendant developer to build a dwelling on a lot that had less frontage than required by zoning regulations for a building lot in the district in which the lot was located.


OVERVIEW: The developer purchased a lot relying on assurances from the planning and zoning office and the building inspector that a building permit could be issued and a dwelling could be built on the lot. These assurances were based on the then-most-recent opinion of the town counsel. The building inspector subsequently ordered construction stopped based on a more recent opinion of town counsel that did not allow construction of a dwelling on the property. The zoning board granted a variance. The owner, who owned an adjacent lot, appealed from a trial court judgment that upheld the board's decision. The court held that the trial court was not in error in concluding that the owner failed to prove that the action of the board was illegal, arbitrary, or in abuse of its discretion. The developer could not obtain additional frontage to meet the zoning requirement and application of the regulations to its property practically destroyed the property's value. When considered in the light of the fact that it was possible to build on smaller lots if they were mapped of record prior to 1945, the zoning requirement were in effect confiscatory or arbitrary as applied to the developer's lot.


OUTCOME: There was no error.

 

821 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Country Lands, Inc. v. Swinnerton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


151 Conn. 27; 193 A.2d 483; 1963 Conn. LEXIS 303


June 5, 1963, Argued  
July 18, 1963, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendant from taking steps to prevent the named plaintiff from removing earth materials from its property, and for a declaratory judgment and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Parmelee, J.; judgment ordering the issuance of a removal permit, and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; Judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city zoning enforcement officer appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Fairfield County (Connecticut) that ordered him to issue the permit for which plaintiff development corporations had applied. The permit applied for was to excavate and remove earth to create a lake on the excavation site. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6 applied.


OVERVIEW: The zoning officer contended on appeal that the failure of the corporations to exhaust the administrative remedy provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6 deprived them of the right to a judicial action. The court found that the corporations were in effect seeking a review of the officer's action. Per Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6(1), the city zoning board of appeals was vested with the power to hear and decide appeals where it was alleged that there was an error in any order, requirement, or decision made by the official charged with the enforcement of the zoning laws or any regulations adopted pursuant to them. An appeal could then be taken under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8 from the decision of the board to the Court of Common Pleas. When a party had a statutory right of appeal from the decision of an administrative officer or agency, he could not instead of appealing bring an independent action to test the very issue that the right of appeal had been given to test.


OUTCOME: The court wrote that there was error, and, acting against the development corporations, it set aside the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with a direction to render judgment for the city zoning enforcement officer on all counts of the complaint.

 

822 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Elm Buick Co. v. Moore


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


150 Conn. 631; 192 A.2d 638; 1963 Conn. LEXIS 250


June 6, 1963, Argued  
June 25, 1963, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover a deficiency alleged to be due on the purchase price of an automobile sold under a retail instalment contract, brought to the Circuit Court in the sixth circuit and tried to the court, Casale, J.; judgment for the defendant and appeal by the plaintiff to the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court, which affirmed the judgment, and thence, upon the granting of certification, to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a retail car dealership, appealed the judgment of the Appellate Division of the Circuit Court (Connecticut), which affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that entered judgment in favor of defendant buyer in the dealerships' action to recover a deficiency alleged to be due on the purchase price of an automobile sold under a retail installment contract.


OVERVIEW: The buyer purchased the car under a retail installment contract that was assigned to a sales finance company. When the buyer defaulted in the installment payments, the finance company repossessed the car. The finance company chose to resell the car under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-98(e) and sent the buyer by certified mail a written notice about the sale as required by § 42-98(d), but the buyer never received the notice. In the dealership's action for a deficiency judgment, the buyer argued that because he received no actual notice of the sale, he was not liable for any deficiency judgment. On appeal the court found that the disjunctive phrase "or by" in § 42-98(d) meant that there were two separate methods of giving the buyer notice of the proposed sale, which were by personal notice or by certified mail. The statute did not require actual notice, and to impose such a requirement would have allowed the buyer to thwart a valid sale. The finance company complied with the § 42-98(d), and the trial court and the lower appellate court erred to find to the contrary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the buyer and directed that the judgment should be entered in favor of the dealership.

Mack v. Saars


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


150 Conn. 290; 188 A.2d 863; 1963 Conn. LEXIS 201


November 7, 1962, Argued  
February 26, 1963, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition in the nature of an appeal from the action of the defendants in suspending the plaintiff's license to practice optometry, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Shannon, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensed optometrist appealed from an order of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which affirmed a decision by defendants, the state board of examiners in optometry and related individuals, to suspend the optometrist's license to practice optometry, and which denied the optometrist's petition for the restoration of his license.


OVERVIEW: The board concluded that the corporation which hired the optometrist to render optometrical services in one of its stores was essentially a retail jewelry store, and was not and could not be licensed to practice optometry. The board then concluded that the optometrist was an employee of the corporation and that the optometrist was guilty of abetting the corporation in the practice of optometry, and accordingly suspended his license to practice optometry. The optometrist petitioned for the restoration of his license, but the superior court sustained the order of the board. Upon review, the court found error, set aside the judgment, and remanded the case with directions to grant the optometrist's petition. The court held that chapter 380 of the Conn. Gen. Stat. could not be construed to prohibit an employment relationship between a corporation or any other unlicensed person, under any circumstances, and a licensed optometrist for a fixed salary, and that the board lacked the power and competence under the legislation to decide otherwise, as the power to prohibit such a relationship rested with the legislature and not with the board.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment which affirmed the board's determination, and remanded the case to the superior court with directions to grant the optometrist's petition for the restoration of his license.

Roan v. Connecticut Industrial Bldg. Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


150 Conn. 333; 189 A.2d 399; 1963 Conn. LEXIS 205


December 6, 1962, Argued  
February 26, 1963, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the act establishing the Connecticut industrial building commission, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Ryan, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of Public Act No. 542, adopted by the 1961 General Assembly, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 32-10 to 32-22, an act which created an administrative agency, the Connecticut Industrial Building Commission.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of the public act that created an administrative agency. Plaintiff challenged the constitutionality of this legislation on three grounds: (1) it authorized the use of public funds and the pledging of the faith and credit of the state for a private benefit which was not incidental to any public purpose. (2) it authorized the delegation of legislative power to the building commission without adequate standards to guide the commission. (3) it authorized the delegation of legislative power to a private corporation, and granted it an exclusive public emolument. The court concluded that the act sufficiently stated a public purpose and was not unconstitutional by reason of the fact that the purpose was not spelled out with clarion specificity. The court held that the act was not an illegal delegation of legislative authority to either the commission or the credit corporation.


OUTCOME: The court declared the act to be constitutional.

Peterson v. Norwalk


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


150 Conn. 366; 190 A.2d 33; 1963 Conn. LEXIS 209


December 5, 1962, Argued  
February 26, 1963, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the legality of a contract made by the defendant city, and other questions, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Bogdanski, J.; judgment answering certain of the questions, and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which determined several questions concerning the legality of a contract made between defendant City of Norwalk, a corporation, and a railroad. The taxpayer sought an injunction restraining the city from taking any action or making any expenditures in connection with the construction of a bridge across the right of way of the railroad.


OVERVIEW: The city had contracted with the corporation to allow the corporation to build a plant in a landlocked area; a new railroad bridge was required and electrical transmission wires had to be relocated. Pursuant to the contract, the city agreed to construct the bridge and pay one-half of its cost, to pay all the cost of relocating the wires, and to maintain the bridge or its replacement, while the railroad agreed to pay $ 25,000 of the cost and the corporation agreed to pay the difference. On review, the court found that the city charter gave it the power to lay out or extend any highway for public use and convenience, but that judicial review was available only to ascertain whether the city council's decision was made in bad faith, in clear abuse of power or in disregard of duty. The court found nothing to indicate bad faith and noted that private advantage did not defeat the public purpose of the project. The court ruled that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-98 required the railroad to pay one-half of the expense of the crossing, including the line relocation costs, and § 16-11 required the railroad to keep the crossing in repair. The court found error in part and remanded the action.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment in the taxpayer's action, and remanded with direction to render judgment as before but modified the judgment to state that the contract was not illegal and void except for the maintenance provisions and the provisions which required the city to pay more than one-half of the cost of relocating the transmission lines.

Levine v. Randolph Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


150 Conn. 232; 188 A.2d 59; 1963 Conn. LEXIS 194; 98 A.L.R.2d 349


November 7, 1962, Argued  
January 15, 1963, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the named defendant from issuing additional shares of its stock, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, House, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs and appeal by the defendants.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant directors appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which favored plaintiff share holders in their action for an injunction to restrain the directors from issuing additional shares of stock in the corporation.


OVERVIEW: A corporation was organized to deal in real estate. It originally issued 10 shares of capital stock, and each share was valued at $ 100. Six brothers and sisters, the parties in this action, held of the shares. Three purported to act as the directors of the corporation and voted to issue additional shares of stock. The remaining shareholders sought to enjoin the directors from issuing the stock certificates and from continuing to act as directors. They claimed the election was illegal, and that one of the certificates had been disenfranchised from voting in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 33-311. The lower court concluded that the voting of the certificate that was owned by multiple persons should have been in accord with how a majority of the holders in interest in that certificate voted, the proposed stock issue was not legally ratified, and that the directors were not legally elected. On review, the court held that since a corporation could not issue fractional shares, the stockholders could not divide their voting privileges. The majority in interest of the owners of the certificate determined the way it should be voted.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment of the trial court that enjoined the directors of a corporation from issuing additional stock certificates.

State v. Andrews


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


150 Conn. 92; 186 A.2d 546; 1962 Conn. LEXIS 258


June 8, 1962, Argued  
November 6, 1962, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of obscene literature and pictures, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County and tried to the court, Dube, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County (Connecticut), which convicted him following a bench trial of the crime of possession of obscene literature and pictures. Defendant was charged by information with two counts of violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-243, Connecticut's antiobscenity statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his partner operated a news store. A variety of magazines were exposed for sale, including so-called sex magazines, which were separately displayed. A plainclothes police officer purchased two such magazines from a large display. Defendant placed the magazines in a paper bag and was subsequently arrested on the obscenity charge. Defendant admitted that the magazines were not sent through the mail, but rather they were delivered to the store by railway express and personal delivery. Defendant claimed the antiobscenity statute was unconstitutional because it lacked a scienter requirement. The court, however, constructed the statute to incorporate scienter. The text and the accompanying photographs in the magazines were designed to appeal to the prurient interest of the average man. The magazines served no useful social purpose. Defendant knew the publications were obscene as evidenced by the way they were delivered, wrapped, and displayed. The scienter conclusion was buttressed by the unfavorable inference drawn from defendant's failure to testify.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of two counts of possession of obscene literature and pictures.

St. John's Roman Catholic Church Corp. v. Darien


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


149 Conn. 712; 184 A.2d 42; 1962 Conn. LEXIS 236


June 5, 1962, Argued  
July 27, 1962, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of the Darien zoning regulations governing the location of parochial schools, and for an injunction and other relief, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford and reserved by the court, Palmer, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff church brought a declaratory judgment action in the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut) against defendant town to determine the constitutionality of a zoning regulation that required a special permit for the construction of a parochial school in an area zoned for public schools. The trial court reserved the action for the court's advice.


OVERVIEW: The church owned property in an "R-2" residence zone on which it planned to build a school. Permitted uses in R-2 zones included residences and public schools, but required special permits for parochial schools. The town zoning commission denied the church's application for a special permit. The church brought a declaratory judgment action, arguing that the zoning ordinances were unconstitutional. The court declared that the ordinances were constitutional. The court found that in order to obtain a special permit the church had to submit a detailed plan of the proposed site, including the location of buildings, parking lots, traffic access and drives, and open areas. The court said there was a clear basis for these additional requirements because they encompassed the same requirements imposed on public schools at an earlier stage in the building process. The court pointed out that each public school building project required the approval of the planning commission or the municipal legislature and the filing of plans with the state before construction was begun. These requirements, the court said, tended to assure that the objectives of the zoning ordinance were safeguarded.


OUTCOME: The court held that a town's zoning ordinance, which required the church to obtain a special permit for the construction of a parochial school in an area zoned for public schools, did not violate the state or federal constitutions.

State v. Da Vila


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


150 Conn. 1; 183 A.2d 852; 1962 Conn. LEXIS 245


June 6, 1962, Argued  
July 27, 1962, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with violation of the Uniform State Narcotic Drug Act, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Thim, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for a violation of the Uniform State Narcotic Drug Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 19-246, from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that he was a drug addict, who had purchased narcotics for his own use on many occasions. After a discussion with a friend, defendant agreed to sell nine bags of heroin to an undercover officer. Defendant asserted that the friend induced him to sell drugs on several occasions and provided part of the purchase price. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court held that the trial court properly refused defendant's request to charge that if the jury found that the drug was in his possession or under his control for purposes of administration to himself or when he was addicted to the use of the drug, the jury should so indicate in their verdict. The court explained that the uniform statute, § 19-246, made no distinction between possession or control of the drug for sale and possession or control for self-administration or by one who is an addict. The court stated that another provision of the statute, criminalizing addiction, was of questionable constitutionality. The court also found that the trial court's instructions regarding entrapment were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Stonybrook, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


149 Conn. 492; 181 A.2d 601; 1962 Conn. LEXIS 207


April 3, 1962, Argued  
May 8, 1962, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of violating the building code of Stratford, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Leipner, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted him of the crime of violating the town of Stratford's building code upon a jury's verdict of guilty.


OVERVIEW: An information had charged defendant with committing the crime of permitting its dwelling units to be occupied by rent-paying tenants without obtaining the proper certificates as required by the town of Stratford's building code. A jury had found defendant guilty of this offense. Defendant argued that it was not bound by the requirements of the building code. Specifically, defendant argued that because the government had retained legal title to the property under a mortgage deed executed by the predecessor in title, the application of the building code to the property was contrary to the provisions of the federal constitution, and the Lanham Act, 1954 Conn. There was nothing in the finding or the record that indicated the government intended to retain ownership, possession, or control of the property, or that it had in any way attempted to do so. Finally, the court held that the law of estoppel did not prevent the town from exercising its right to prosecute a violation of the building code. The court, finding no error, affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court did not find any error in the trial court's judgment, and affirmed defendant's conviction for the crime of violating the town of Stratford's building code.

State v. Doe
