Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


149 Conn. 216; 178 A.2d 271; 1962 Conn. LEXIS 167


October 10, 1961, Argued  
February 6, 1962, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the statute under which the plaintiff proposes to remove the defendant to Vermont, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Cotter, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State government filed an action for declaratory judgment against defendant indigent out-of-state resident, claiming that it was authorized under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-273a to forcibly transfer the out-of-state resident to her home state, because she had applied for welfare benefits. The trial court reserved the case, seeking advice from the court.


OVERVIEW: An out-of-state resident moved to Connecticut and eventually applied for welfare benefits. The State attempted to forcibly transfer the out-of-state resident to her home state, so that she could receive public assistance there, but she refused to do so. The State then filed an action for declaratory judgment and the trial court reserved questions for the advice of the court. The court held that when a person applied for welfare assistance, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-273a provided that any person who belonged to another state and came to reside in the state and became chargeable or made application for aid or was admitted to a state humane institution as an indigent person or pauper or otherwise, that person may be transported to his home state. However, the court stated that the facts stipulated in this case were wholly inadequate to furnish a proper basis on which to consider the constitutionality of a statute which had such far-reaching consequences as § 17-273a. The court concluded that it would refuse to answer the questions reserved by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court refused to answer the questions reserved the trial court.

 

832 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Mott's Super Markets, Inc. v. Frassinelli


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


148 Conn. 481; 172 A.2d 381; 1961 Conn. LEXIS 206


April 6, 1961, Argued  
June 20, 1961, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the defendant requiring the plaintiff to desist from unfair sales practices, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Palmer, J.; judgment affirming the order in part and setting it aside in part, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff market owner appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas (Connecticut), which sustained an order of defendant commissioner of consumer protection issued pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-112, that the owner cease and desist from advertising and selling in its supermarkets two products, at less than "cost to the retailer."


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that § 42-112 was unconstitutional and that the finding that the owner had the intent to injure its competitors was unsupported by the evidence. The court found that, to be constitutionally valid, a statute like § 42-112, an exercise of the police power of the state, was required to meet a legitimate business purpose affecting the public health, safety, convenience, or welfare in a save and impartial way. The court found that § 42-112 met that requirement. The court found, however, that a violation of § 42-112 required a showing of the intent to harm competitors as a part of a prima facie case. Testimony taken by the commissioner that prices were lowered to attract customers into the owner's market was not sufficient to support a finding of intent to harm competitors or destroy competition, thus, the judgment finding that the owner violated § 42-112 was set aside.


OUTCOME: There is error, the judgment is set aside and the case is remanded with direction to render judgment setting aside the order of the defendant.

 

833 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Waterford v. Connecticut State Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


148 Conn. 238; 169 A.2d 891; 1961 Conn. LEXIS 171


January 4, 1961, Argued  
April 11, 1961, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the defendant requiring the plaintiff to furnish transportation to a school, brought to the Superior Court in New London County and tried to the court, Thim, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Town of Waterford appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, New London County (Connecticut), that dismissed its appeal from an order of defendant Connecticut State Board of Education that required the Town to provide transportation for certain pupils and that found for the Board on the question of the power of the Board to issue the order.


OVERVIEW: The Town claimed in effect that the failure of a town board of education to furnish transportation did not constitute a failure to furnish school accommodations under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-186. Certain parents had requested transportation for their school children although they lived within one mile of the school; the request was made on the basis of a lack of safe sidewalks and other precautionary measures. The court ruled that reading Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 10-186, 10-220 together, the failure of a town to provide the transportation that was reasonable and desirable as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-220 for the safety of the children attending the particular school they were required to attend constituted a failure to furnish school accommodations within Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-186, which section provided for an appeal to the Board. The court rejected the argument that § 10-186 was unconstitutional; the argument posited that § 10-186 failed to set standards for the proper guidance of the Board. The court also ruled that the Board's hearing had been lawfully held and that its order had been properly issued and that its action was not arbitrary and unreasonable.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the Board and against the Town, the court stated that there was no error.

 

834 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Heiberger v. Clark


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


148 Conn. 177; 169 A.2d 652; 1961 Conn. LEXIS 164


December 9, 1960, Argued  
March 21, 1961, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining whether the plaintiff is entitled to admission to the bar, and other questions, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County, where a demurrer to the complaint was sustained, Thim, J., and, the plaintiff failing to plead further, judgment was rendered for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, New Haven County (Connecticut), that sustained the demurrer of defendant members of the Connecticut Bar Examining Committee in the applicant's case that alleged that he had complied with the requirements for bar admission other than those set by subsections (5), (6), (7) of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Sup. Ct. § 4, and that he had fulfilled the requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-82.


OVERVIEW: The demurrer to the complaint was partly based on the contention that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-82 was unconstitutional. The court framed the issue as follows. Did the legislative branch of Connecticut's government possess the power to set the qualifications for admission to practice law such that the provisions of § 51-82 superceded the rules adopted by the superior court's judges? The court ruled that any attempt on the part of the legislative department to direct what the rules should be and to determine what qualifications applicants for admission had to possess exceeded the constitutional power of that department; the court held that § 51-82 was unconstitutional.The court's holding was based partly on history, which included the fact that 110 years before the adoption of the Connecticut Constitution of 1818 the General Assembly had assigned to the courts the business of admission of attorneys.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the bar-examining-committee members and against the applicant, the court wrote that there was no error.

 

835 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Crescent Dev. Corp. v. Planning Com. of New Canaan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


148 Conn. 145; 168 A.2d 547; 1961 Conn. LEXIS 159


January 3, 1961, Argued  
February 21, 1961, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant in partially rejecting a subdivision plan, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford and tried to the court, LaMacchia, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County at Stamford (Connecticut) that dismissed the landowner's appeal of a judgment of defendant planning commission, which modified the landowners' plan for a subdivision prior to approval.


OVERVIEW: The landowners sought approval of the proposed subdivision, which the commission approved subject to modifications in the plan regarding public roadways. The trial court dismissed the landowners' appeal. The court found no error, holding that the power of the planning commission to modify a plan before approving it was expressly provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-26. Thus, the planning commission had the power to modify and approve the landowners' plan prior to approval. As the modifications affected only the public roadway running through the subdivision at issue, the commission had the authority to modify the plan. The commission provided lengthy reasons for its judgment, which was predicated on the landowners' representations regarding an attached subdivision. The landowners failed to prove that the action of the zoning commission was illegal.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the dismissal of the appeal.

 

836 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Trubek v. Ullman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


147 Conn. 633; 165 A.2d 158; 1960 Conn. LEXIS 194


October 6, 1960, Argued  
November 1, 1960, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of legislation forbidding the use and prescription of contraceptive devices, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County, where a demurrer to the complaint was sustained, Ryan, J., and, the plaintiffs failing to plead further, judgment was rendered in favor of the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a husband and wife, appealed the decision of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which sustained defendant state's attorney's demurrer to plaintiffs' action for a declaratory judgment to determine unconstitutional legislation forbidding the use and prescription of contraceptive devices under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-32 and 54-196.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs consulted with a physician for information and advice on the manner and means of preventing conception. The physician refused on the ground that such action on his part may be claimed by the state's attorney to constitute a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-32 and 54-196. Plaintiff filed suit for declaratory relief. The state's attorney filed a demurrer, which the trial court sustained. On appeal, the court found no error. The court held that the issue had been previously decided in other litigation that raised essentially the same factual issues and that the one different fact, namely that plaintiffs did not claim that information relating to the employment of contraceptive measures was essential for the purpose of safeguarding the health of the wife, did not make raise a new issue.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the decision of the trial court, which had sustained the state's attorney's demurrer to plaintiffs' claim for declaratory relief against the state's laws against the use of contraceptives.

 

837 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Connecticut Theatrical Corp. v. New Britain


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


147 Conn. 546; 163 A.2d 548; 1960 Conn. LEXIS 185


May 5, 1960, Argued  
July 26, 1960, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of an ordinance of the defendant city concerning the stationing of policemen in theaters, and for an injunction and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Shapiro, J.; judgment finding the ordinance valid in part and invalid in part and enjoining the defendant from enforcing the invalid part, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, movie theater owners and operators, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which, in an action for a declaratory judgment, determined the validity of an ordinance of defendant city concerning the stationing of policemen in theaters.


OVERVIEW: The owners of all the movie theaters in a city contended that a city ordinance that required the presence and payment of police officers in their theaters was invalid. The owners' basic contentions were that the city charter conferred no power upon the city to enact an ordinance requiring the owners to pay for the services of policemen assigned to their theaters, that the ordinance was unconstitutional, and that Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 29-109 vested in the state police exclusive jurisdiction to regulate movie theaters with respect to all personal hazards. The trial court found the city ordinance to be valid. On review, the court found that the ordinance required, as the statute and the regulations promulgated by the state police did not, the presence of a police officer to see to it that all ordinances and statutes were complied with. It embraced the protection of theater patrons from hazards unrelated to those connected with fire or panic; that is, it embraced the general preservation of order under any and all circumstances. Thus, the court found that the trial court properly concluded that § 29-109 did not operate to supersede the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the city.

 

838 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


West Realty Co. v. Ennis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


147 Conn. 602; 164 A.2d 409; 1960 Conn. LEXIS 191


May 6, 1960, Argued  
July 26, 1960, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendant from enforcing an order for the demolition of a building, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, MacDonald, J.; judgment for the defendant and appeal by the plaintiff.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commercial building owner sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) that denied his request to enjoin defendant chief inspector of licenses and inspections from enforcing his order under the provisions of the Hartford building code, § 43-37, to demolish the building owner's building.


OVERVIEW: The building owner's building was damaged extensively in two separate fires. The chief inspector of licenses and inspections (chief inspector) ordered the demolition of the damaged building under the provisions of the Hartford building code, § 43-37. The building owner filed suit to enjoin the chief inspector from enforcing his order. The building owner was denied relief. In affirming the decision, the court held that the challenged portion of § 43-37 was not unconstitutional. Interpretation of § 43-37 in harmony with Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. §§ 19-378 and 19-391 led to the conclusion that damage to the building, to the extent of 50 percent, exclusive of the value of the foundation, was a sufficient standard for the guidance of the chief inspector. Otherwise, the unsightly remnants of a damaged building would remain until the ravages of time and the elements required common-law action to abate a nuisance. Further, the building owner did not take advantage of its right to appeal to the board of review. That appeal procedure, together with the building owner's right of recourse to the courts, satisfied the constitutional requirement of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that denied the building owner's request to enjoin the chief inspector of licenses and inspections from enforcing his order to demolish the building owner's building.

 

839 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Snyder v. Newtown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


147 Conn. 374; 161 A.2d 770; 1960 Conn. LEXIS 157


February 2, 1960, Argued  
May 31, 1960, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of legislation under which the defendant town transports children to a parochial school, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and reserved by the court, Healey, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, town citizens, challenged defendant town's payment of transportation expenses for children to attend private schools under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-281 as unconstitutional under the equal protection clause of Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 12, the freedom of religion clause of Conn. Const. art. VII, § 1, and the education "school fund" provision of Conn. Const. art. VIII, § 2.


OVERVIEW: After the passage of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-281, the town had a referendum on the public payment of private school transportation. The referendum was approved. The citizens filed suit for declaration that the payment under § 10-281 was unconstitutional. The court upheld the payment in part. The transportation of school children served a public purpose. Section 10-281was not violative of equal protection because of an incidental benefit to the private school. The real benefit was to the town's families. The payments were not in violation of guarantees of freedom of religion because § 10-281 served the public health, safety, and welfare. The aid was given to the parents, who were compelled by law to send their children to school, and the aid was not given to the private school. However, the use of monies from the "school fund" to pay for the transportation was unconstitutional because those funds were limited to expenditures to support and encourage public schools. Although the money from the town deposit fund was not governed by the "school fund" provision of Conn. Const. art. VIII, § 2, it was also limited to public school expenses under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-350, 7-353, 10-257.


OUTCOME: The court found that the town's provision of funds was constitutional, except for the use of funds derived from the school fund.

 

840 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Graham v. Houlihan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


147 Conn. 321; 160 A.2d 745; 1960 Conn. LEXIS 149


March 3, 1960, Argued  
May 10, 1960, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment on the validity of a redevelopment plan, brought to the Superior Court in Litchfield County and tried to the court, Alcorn, J.; judgment determining the plan to be valid, and appeal by the named plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the property owners and intervenors, sought review of the order of the Superior Court in Litchfield County (Connecticut), which determined a redevelopment plan concerning certain property in the city to be valid. Plaintiffs had filed an action for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against defendants, the city, redevelopment agency, and individual members of the agency.


OVERVIEW: On review of the declaratory judgment action, plaintiffs asserted that: (1) the agency acted arbitrarily, unreasonably and illegally in finding that the area was a "redevelopment area" within the scope of the Redevelopment Act, ch. 55 (1949), as amended by Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 130; and (2) the hearing held by the agency was in violation of the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the federal constitution and Conn. Const. art. I, § 12. The court held that: (1) the public policy of the Redevelopment Act was to be broadly and liberally construed to allow redevelopment of deteriorated property, and the agency's decision that the subject land was detrimental to the safety, health, and welfare of the community, was not arbitrary; and (2) plaintiffs were afforded a full opportunity to appear and oppose, and offer any evidence they had, during the proceedings by the agency, as well as a right of appeal to the courts on the issue of compensation, and therefore, there was no denial of due process. The court held that plaintiffs' motions for disclosure and production of agency documents was properly denied because plaintiffs were not hampered in preparation of their case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that found that the agency's redevelopment plan was valid.

 

841 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Buxton v. Ullman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


147 Conn. 48; 156 A.2d 508; 1959 Conn. LEXIS 251


October 7, 1959, Argued  
December 8, 1959, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Actions for declaratory judgments determining the constitutionality of legislation forbidding the use and prescription of contraceptive devices, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County, where demurrers to the complaints were sustained, Healey, J., and, the plaintiffs failing to plead further, judgments were rendered in favor of the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs doctor and patients challenged judgments of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) in favor of defendant state's attorney in the doctor and patients' declaratory judgment actions challenging the constitutionality of legislation.


OVERVIEW: The State of Connecticut passed Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-23 and 54-196, which prohibited the use of contraceptives. The doctor and patients brought declaratory judgment actions against the state's attorney challenging the legislation, and the trial court entered judgments in favor of the state's attorney. The doctor and patients sought review, and the court affirmed. The court held that the legislature had the power to pass the statutes under its police power and that the court could not have interfered because the statutes served the public health, safety, morals or welfare and did not deny or interfere with private rights. It was for the legislature to determine the policy of the law and the court was required to recognize and obey the legislature's will and not to usurp the legislature's power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments in favor of the state's attorney in the doctor and patients' declaratory judgment actions.

Karen v. East Haddam


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


146 Conn. 720; 155 A.2d 921; 1959 Conn. LEXIS 237


October 14, 1959, Argued  
November 17, 1959, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of an ordinance of the defendant town regulating trailer parks, and for an injunction and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Middlesex County and tried before Hon. William J. Shea, a judge of the Superior Court, on a motion for a temporary injunction; pursuant to stipulation that the decision on the motion should become the final judgment, the court rendered judgment finding the ordinance valid in part and invalid in part and enjoining the defendants from enforcing the invalid part, from which judgment the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in Middlesex County (Connecticut), which entered a judgment finding an ordinance of defendant town, which regulated trailer parks, to be valid in part and invalid in part, and enjoined the town from enforcing the invalid part of the ordinance. The landowners sought a declaratory judgment concerning the constitutionality of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The judgment was entered on a motion for a temporary injunction pursuant to a stipulation that the decision on the motion should become the final judgment. The landowners argued in part that the refusal of the trial court to incorporate in the finding 20 paragraphs of the draft was erroneous and that the ordinance violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. On appeal, the court concluded that the sections of the ordinance challenged by the landowners, with the exception of §§ 2 (C)(1) and 7 of An Ordinance to License and Regulate Trailer Parks and Mobile Home Parks in the Town of East Haddam, found invalid by the trial court, were valid exercises of the police power conferred under the statute. Further, the court determined that § 18 of the ordinance specifically provided for the separability of any sections that were declared invalid by the courts. The court also found that no corrections in the trial court's finding were warranted and the ordinance did not violate the U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment, which found that a town ordinance regulating trailer parks was valid in part and enjoined the town from enforcing the invalid part of the ordinance.

 

843 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Hartland v. Jensen's, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


146 Conn. 697; 155 A.2d 754; 1959 Conn. LEXIS 233


October 8, 1959, Argued  
November 3, 1959, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction against the use by the defendant of its premises as a trailer park, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Comley, J.; judgment for the named plaintiff and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowner challenged a decision from the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which granted the relief that plaintiff town sought in its action to enjoin the landowner from operating a mobile home park on its property.


OVERVIEW: The landowner determined that the injunction against operating a mobile home park violated its rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. The court affirmed the issuance of that injunction, finding that the ordinance on which the injunction relied represented a valid exercise of the town's police power. The court reasoned that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148 (Rev. 1958) empowered the town, which lacked a duly constituted local zoning or planning commission, to regulate and to provide for the licensing of parked trailers when located off the public highways, and trailer parks, or mobile home parks. The court also concluded that the record indicated that developing a park for the number of mobile homes that the landowner contemplated could have involved the town in civic problems that affected the public health, safety, and welfare in ways that exceeded the town's resources. The court further found that the town's power to regulate mobile home parks entailed a certain degree of prohibition and that ordinance's placement of mobile homes and trailers in the same classification could not have been said to have been unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in the town's favor in its action to enjoin the landowner from operating a mobile home park.

 

844 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Vartelas v. Water Resources Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


146 Conn. 650; 153 A.2d 822; 1959 Conn. LEXIS 226


June 5, 1959, Argued  
July 28, 1959, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant in establishing an encroachment line on land of the plaintiff's decedent, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the court, Dube, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant water resources commission sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff landowner's appeal of the imposition of a use restriction involving the landowner's property.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned real property, which contained five stores and six apartment buildings that was near the Naugatuck River. The river overflowed and destroyed the buildings and a bridge. A water resources commission, pursuant to Conn. Rev. Stat. § 25-3(c) (rev. 1958), established a line in the direction of the river, whereby no structure or encroachment could be placed unless the commission specifically authorized it. The only property unaffected by the commission's line gave the landowner 60 square feet to use. The commission denied the landowner's application to construct a 50 square foot retail market. The landowner sought judicial review, and the trial court sustained the landowner's appeal of the commission's decision. The court set aside and remanded, holding that the commission was justified in refusing to allow the construction of the proposed structure by way of regulation rather than by way of eminent domain because it was not shown that the landowner was finally deprived by the commission of the reasonable and proper use of the property. Other alternatives existed, and zoning was a valid method to exercise police power to protect the public interest.


OUTCOME: The court set aside and remanded the sustaining of the landowner's appeal of the imposition of a use restriction by the water resources commission, involving the landowner's property.

E. Ingraham Co. v. Town & City of Bristol


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


146 Conn. 403; 151 A.2d 700; 1959 Conn. LEXIS 177


March 4, 1959, Argued  
April 28, 1959, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for relief against the wrongful assessment of taxes upon personal property, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Barber, J., for the advice of this court.

The plaintiff filed a motion for reargument which was denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer and defendant town sought an answer to the question of whether the plaintiff was entitled to relief under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-119 (Rev. to 1997)(Rev. 1949, § 1801) by means of reservation before the court in the taxpayer's action for relief from the wrongful assessment of taxes upon personal property. The action had been brought before the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer owned real and personal property subject to taxation in the town. The town assessed the taxpayer's real property at 50 percent of its actual value, the personal property other than motor vehicles at 90 percent, and the motor vehicles at 100 per cent. The taxpayer brought a proceeding for relief against the wrongful assessment of taxes upon personal property. The taxpayer claimed that all of its property should have been assessed at a single uniform percentage of its actual value. The taxpayer argued that the proceeding was not an appeal from the doings of the board of tax review under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-118 (Rev. to 1958)(Rev. to 1949, § 1800), but was an application to the trial court for relief under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-119 (Rev. to 1997)(Rev. 1949, § 1801). The town brought a demurrer. The parties entered into a stipulation of reservation for the taxpayer's argument. The demurrer was not acted upon by the trial court. The reservation came before the court. The court held that the taxpayer failed to show that it was entitled to relief under § 119 because the taxpayer did not establish that the assessment on its personal property was "manifestly excessive."


OUTCOME: The court held against the taxpayer and answered the question in the reservation of whether the taxpayer was entitled to relief in the negative.

Bahr Corp. v. O'Brion


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


146 Conn. 237; 149 A.2d 691; 1959 Conn. LEXIS 151


February 3, 1959, Argued  
March 4, 1959, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction to restrain the members of the New Haven Redevelopment Agency from proceeding further with the taking of certain property, and for a declaratory judgment and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Bogdanski, J.; judgment in favor of the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.

Application for an order to put the New Haven Redevelopment Agency in peaceable possession of property, brought to Hon. Joseph W. Bogdanski, a judge of the Superior Court; from his order granting the application the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action plaintiff corporation appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which ruled in favor of defendant redevelopment agency in the corporation's action for injunctive and declaratory relief. The agency appealed from the order denying its application for an order for peaceable possession of the corporation's property.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was the owner of certain business property. Under the agency's redevelopment plan, the corporation's building was to be demolished. The corporation instituted an action against agency for a declaratory judgment determining whether the redevelopment plan was valid. The court held that the trial court erred in concluding that the corporation was barred by laches from asserting the claims set forth in its complaint. The court ruled that because an order directing the clerk of the Superior Court to issue an execution putting the agency into peaceable possession of the corporation's property could not be made if upon judicial review it was discovered that the taking of the property was illegal, the granting of the application for such an order constituted error. The court noted that the application should not be granted unless, upon judicial review, it was discovered that the taking of the property was legal.


OUTCOME: The court set the judgments aside and remanded the cases to be proceeded with in accordance with the court's opinion.

 

847 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sul


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


146 Conn. 78; 147 A.2d 686; 1958 Conn. LEXIS 270


November 4, 1958, Argued  
December 24, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of obscene literature, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County, where a demurrer to the information was overruled, Devlin, J., and the issues were tried to the court, Pastore, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted him of having in his possession with intent to sell, offer, and show certain booklets containing obscene and indecent language and also obscene and indecent pictures, against the peace and contrary to the form of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8567.


OVERVIEW: The information, in four counts, charged that defendant had violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8567 in that on four different days he did have in his possession with intent to sell, offer, and show certain booklets containing obscene and indecent language and also obscene and indecent pictures against the peace and contrary to the form of § 8567. Defendant demurred, alleging that § 8567 violated constitutional guarantees of freedom of speech and of the press because those were liberties protected from state action by the Fourteenth Amendment. The trial court overruled the demurrer, and defendant entered a plea of not guilty and elected to be tried to the court without a jury. The State withdrew two of the four counts. After a full hearing, the trial court found defendant guilty. Defendant sought review. On appeal, the court found no error. The court held that defendant's constitutional rights were not violated because § 8567 was sufficiently explicit to inform those subject to it what conduct on their part would render them liable to its penalties. The court ruled that obscenity was not protected by the unconditional language of the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

 

848 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Clark v. Town Council of West Hartford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


145 Conn. 476; 144 A.2d 327; 1958 Conn. LEXIS 214


June 6, 1958, Argued  
July 24, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the named defendant in approving a development plan for an integrated shopping center, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Bogdanski, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the named plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff neighbor appealed from the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut) that dismissed an appeal from the decision of defendant town council approving an application to rezone the land of defendant developer from residential uses to a special commercial zone subject to regulations peculiar to that zone.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought approval under West Hartford, Conn., Zoning Ordinance § 15, to build a shopping center in a largely residential area. The plan was approved with certain modifications, thereby creating a special commercial zone. The neighbor objected, but the common pleas court upheld the decision of the town council. He appealed. In affirming, the supreme court ruled that private property was held subject to the police power and the ordinance was not an invalid delegation of legislative power to the town's plan and zoning commission, which had recommended approval of the plan. The ordinance was valid because it adequately contained the legislative policy and specific qualifications for the exercise of zoning powers. The ordinance was within the power conferred by the enabling acts, 19 Conn. Spec. Laws 935 and 22 Conn. Spec. Laws 473. Also, the developer's plan complied with the comprehensive plan for the town, such that the creation of the new zone was not arbitrary and did not constitute spot zoning.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the neighbor's appeal from the rezoning decision was affirmed.

 

849 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shuster


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


145 Conn. 554; 145 A.2d 196; 1958 Conn. LEXIS 224; 35 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P71,867


May 9, 1958, Argued  
July 8, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of selling on Sunday in violation of statute, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County and tried to the jury before LaMacchia, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County (Connecticut), convicting defendant of selling on Sunday in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3302d (Supp. 1955) and denying defendant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of selling non-antique merchandise, to wit, candles, on Sunday in violation of § 3302d and appealed from the denial of a motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. Defendant alleged that the statute's classification violated the equal protection clause of both the Conn. Const. art. I, § 1, and the U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. Upon review, the court found no error. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3302d (Supp. 1955) did not violate the equal protection clause by reason of the fact that the statute permitted the sale of certain specified articles while prohibiting the sale of all others, as long as the statute accorded the same rights to all who engaged in the same business. None of defendant's competitors were granted privileges not accorded to defendant. Section 3302d was uniform in its operation. The court further held that the classification of antiques among the articles exempt from the operation of the statute rested upon fair distinctions and bore a substantial relation to the purposes of the legislation. There was no basis for holding invalid the addition of antiques to the class of articles exempt from the operation of § 3302d.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

850 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Wethersfield v. National Fire Ins. Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


145 Conn. 368; 143 A.2d 454; 1958 Conn. LEXIS 195


May 13, 1958, Argued  
June 17, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action upon an insurance policy to recover the amount paid by the plaintiff in settlement of a suit against it, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Devlin, J.; judgment for the defendant and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town sought review of decision, in the Superior Court of Hartford County (Connecticut), granting judgment for defendant insurance company, in action brought to recover amount paid by plaintiff in settlement of a suit against it. 1953 Conn. Spec. Acts 6.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff town sought review of decision granting judgment for defendant insurance company in action brought to recover amount plaintiff paid in settlement of a suit against it. The court held that plaintiff did not violate the cooperation clause of its insurance policy by waiving the defense of inadequacy of notice through the enactment of 1953 Conn. Spec. Acts 6 validating inadequate notice of injury provided plaintiff. Plaintiff did not legislatively enact the validating act, but it was the state which brought about the enactment of 1953 Conn. Spec. Acts 6. Instead, plaintiff attempted to prevent its enactment. The court held that 1953 Conn. Spec. Acts 6 was not an unconstitutional impairment of parties' insurance contract. 1953 Conn. Spec. Acts 6 did not purport to, nor did it, directly affect contract of insurance or any term of that contract. Furthermore, because both plaintiff and defendant had knowledge of and investigated victim's injuries within the statutory 10 days, the General Assembly could well have considered 1953 Conn. Spec. Acts 6 a reasonable exercise of legislative power.


OUTCOME: Court set aside judgment and remanded. Plaintiff did not violate the cooperation clause of its insurance policy by waiving the defense of inadequacy of notice through the enactment of special validating act in which the inadequate notice of injury provided plaintiff was declared legal. Plaintiff did not legislatively enact the validating act, but it was the state that brought about its enactment.

 

851 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Wilson Point Property Owners Asso. v. Connecticut Light & Power Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


145 Conn. 243; 140 A.2d 874; 1958 Conn. LEXIS 175


March 7, 1958, Argued  
April 15, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the defendant public utilities commission affirming an order of the Norwalk zoning commission approving Manresa Island as the location for a steam generating plant, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Mellitz, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.

The plaintiffs Nathan et al. filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners associations sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which dismissed an appeal from a decision by the public utility commission to affirm a zoning commission decision approving property for use as a steam generating plant by defendant power company.


OVERVIEW: The property owners associations owned property adjacent to an island. The power company applied, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5646, to develop a steam generating plant and received permission from the zoning commission. The public utility commission held a public hearing and affirmed the permission. The property owners association filed an appeal in the superior court, alleging that the public utility commission's decision did not comport with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5399. The appeal was dismissed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the decision rendered by the public utility commission was proper. The court reasoned that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5399, upon which the property owners' association relied, came into play only if the superior court were to have found that the commission had wrongfully excluded proper evidence or that the facts were insufficient for the proper disposal of the appeal. The court concluded that it was not the function of the public utilities commission to prepare a finding such as is required by court appeals and it was sufficient that the finding and conclusions set forth the basic facts upon which it predicated its decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the property owners associations' appeal from a zoning decision permitting the power company to build a steam plant on an island adjacent to the property owners associations' property.

 

852 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Benson v. Housing Authority of New Haven


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


145 Conn. 196; 140 A.2d 320; 1958 Conn. LEXIS 169


February 13, 1958, Submitted on Briefs  
March 25, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining whether the statutes under which the defendant proposes to erect a moderate rental housing project are constitutional, and for an injunction and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County, where the court, Phillips, J., sustained a demurrer to the complaint and, the plaintiffs having failed to plead further, judgment was rendered for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) in favor of defendant city housing authority in the landowners' action to enjoin the erection of a moderate rental housing development and for a declaratory judgment as to whether the Municipal Housing Authorities Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 52, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The housing authority began condemnation proceedings in the neighborhood of the landowners' properties in order to erect a moderate rental housing development, and it also purchased some land. The landowners filed an action against the housing authority to enjoin the development, and the trial court sustained the housing authority's demurrer. The landowners appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that there was no specific statutory provision allowing the landowners' recovery. Accordingly, because no land was physically taken from them, the prohibition in Conn. Const. art. 1, § 11 barred their action. The landowners' complaint did not set forth any facts entitling them to injunctive or declaratory relief on the ground of nuisance or under the Act by allegations that no emergency existed warranting the construction of the development, so it failed to state a cause of action for the relief claimed. Allegations of special irreparable injury and specifications of fact to support their claims were lacking. There was no authority for the landowners' assertions that zoning restrictions created a right in the nature of an easement in favor of their properties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining the housing authority's demurrer to the landowners' complaint for an injunction and declaratory relief.

 

853 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Avco Mfg. Corp. v. Connelly


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


145 Conn. 161; 140 A.2d 479; 1958 Conn. LEXIS 165


November 7, 1957, Argued  
March 25, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a deficiency assessment of sales and use taxes, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Thim, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court. 1


1 Subsequent to the appeal to this court, the Superior Court substituted John L. Sullivan as party defendant, he having succeeded William F. Connelly as tax commissioner of the state of Connecticut.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a judgment of a superior court (Connecticut), which affirmed a sales and use tax deficiency assessment levied by defendant state tax commissioner on facilities purchased for an aircraft manufacturing plant owned and operated by the United States government. The facilities, consisting principally of machinery, were purchased to fulfill a facilities contract with the government.


OVERVIEW: Under a facilities contract awarded to the taxpayer, the taxpayer could use machinery that had been purchased for use in manufacturing military aircraft engines and parts. The taxpayer received no profit on the purchase and installation of the facilities. The court held that not only the express language of the contracts but the surrounding circumstances, including controlling government regulations and conduct of the parties, indicated that the government was the owner of all facilities from the moment of shipment by the vendors. As the purchase orders specified that shipment was f.o.b. the vendor's plant, title passed from the vendor upon delivery of the facilities to the carrier as agent. It was also consistent with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6634 of the Sales and Use Tax Act that payment only be postponed and, if later inspection disclosed the facilities were not as ordered, the government could rescind and refuse payment. As the taxpayer's use was merely to accomplish the government's purpose, its use was not incident to ownership and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2095(2) did not apply. To allow imposition of the use tax regardless of ownership violated the government's immunity from state tax.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the superior court upholding the sales and use tax deficiency assessment levied by the state tax commissioner on facilities purchased by the taxpayer. The court remanded the case with directions to render judgment sustaining the appeal.

Edwards v. Hartford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


145 Conn. 141; 139 A.2d 599; 1958 Conn. LEXIS 162


February 5, 1958, Argued  
March 6, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for false arrest and imprisonment and for expenses incurred as the result of the impounding of the plaintiff's automobile, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Bogdanski, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut) in favor of defendants, the city and several police officers, in the owner's action to recover damages for false arrest and imprisonment and for expenses incurred as the result of the impounding of his automobile.


OVERVIEW: The owner parked his car at 4:45 p.m. within an area in which the parking of vehicles was prohibited from 4:30 p.m. to 6 p.m. because of heavy traffic conditions. An officer had placed a parking violation tag on the car and the car had been pushed about 50 feet by the tow truck employee when the owner caught up with the car, got into it, stopped the car, and attempted to order the other man out. As a crowd assembled, an officer was summoned, who refused to allow the owner to pay the fine and take his car, then arrested the owner for breach of the peace. The trial court dismissed the owner's suit for damages. In affirming, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict. The court rejected the owner's claim that the parking ordinance was unconstitutional because it provided for the removal of cars whether they were occupied or not. The court found that the car was not occupied when it was ticketed and towed, that the officer was not guilty false arrest, and that the officer did not violate the owner's right in having the car impounded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city and the police officers.

 

855 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walters


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


145 Conn. 60; 138 A.2d 786; 1958 Conn. LEXIS 148


January 8, 1958, Argued  
January 28, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree committed in perpetrating a robbery, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Shea, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield County, (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of the crime of murder in the first degree committed in perpetrating a robbery.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's trial the lower court gave the basic charge to which no exceptions were taken. The jury then deliberated until evening, at which time they were excused to go home. On the second day of deliberations the lower court gave the jury a portion of a charge that outlined the jurors' duty after it was reported that the jury was in hopeless disagreement. Counsel for defendant excepted to the lower court's failure to give the complete charge and also asked that the jury be dismissed based on the fact that they were in hopeless disagreement. The motion was denied. The lower court recalled the jury and not only gave them the omitted portion of the charge but emphasized that the rule enunciated in the charge applied whether the majority were for conviction or for acquittal. Defendant was found guilty. On appeal, the court found no error. The court held that it was not an abuse of discretion for the lower court to give the charge instead of treating the jury's first report of failure to reach a verdict as a final disagreement warranting an abandonment of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

856 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


United Interchange, Inc. v. Spellacy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


144 Conn. 647; 136 A.2d 801; 1957 Conn. LEXIS 153


October 9, 1957, Argued  
December 3, 1957, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining whether the act concerning the regulation and licensing of real estate salesmen and brokers is constitutionally applicable to the plaintiffs' operations, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Conway, J.; judgment in favor of the defendant and appeal by the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an advertiser and its employees, appealed from a judgment that the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) entered in favor of defendant insurance commissioner. Plaintiffs had instituted the action to obtain an injunction and a judgment declaring unconstitutional certain provisions in the regulation and licensing of real estate salesmen and brokers.


OVERVIEW: The advertiser, through its employees, solicited contracts from prospective sellers to advertise their businesses or properties in two printed media published by a publisher under agreement with the advertiser. The commissioner received complaints of fraudulent representations from those doing business with similar companies as the advertiser, so the commissioner sought and secured a legislative amendment, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2339d, in order to regulate such businesses. Plaintiffs argued that the amendment was unconstitutional as applied to them, but the trial court disagreed. Reversing, the court held that requiring plaintiffs to obtain real estate brokers' and salesmen's licenses was unnecessarily burdensome and discriminatory because their only business was advertising. The court, therefore, held that the provisions of the amendment that embraced plaintiffs' activities within the definition of "engaging in the real estate business" and the activities of a real estate broker or salesman violated the constitutional rights of plaintiffs and were null and void.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment and remanded with directions to render judgment in accordance with the court's opinion that the amendment was unconstitutional.

 

857 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Holloway


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


144 Conn. 295; 130 A.2d 562; 1957 Conn. LEXIS 96


February 6, 1957, Argued  
March 5, 1957, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with violation of the Uniform State Narcotic Drug Act, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Troland, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted under the Uniform State Narcotic Drug Act. The trial court reserved for advice.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially indicted in the trial court on an information charging him with violation of the Uniform State Narcotic Drug Act, third offense. Before the jury was sworn, the trial judge determined that because the penalty for which defendant was charged was life imprisonment, his trial could be had only upon an indictment by a grand jury. The grand jury returned an indictment against defendant charging him under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3962, as well as being a third offender under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 2103d, 2104d. The parties stipulated for reservation of advice from the court on various questions certain to enter into the decision of the case in the trial court. The major question was whether §§ 2103d, 2104d were applicable since defendant's convictions occurred prior to the effective date of their passage. The court ruled that offenses occurring prior to the passage of §§ 2103d, 2104d counted as offenses under the Act so as to authorize the imposition of the penalty for subsequent violations, such as life imprisonment. The court ruled that two statutory sections worked in tandem to ensure that prior convictions increased the penalties for subsequent convictions.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that defendant's prior convictions prior to the passage of certain statutory sections of the Uniform Narcotic Drug Act counted towards the imposition of increased penalties for subsequent violations.

 

858 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Pierce v. Albanese


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


144 Conn. 241; 129 A.2d 606; 1957 Conn. LEXIS 91


December 5, 1956, Argued  
February 13, 1957, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries, alleged to have been caused by the intoxication of a person to whom the defendant had sold intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Alcorn, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiffs and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tavern owner appealed the judgment in favor of plaintiff individuals in the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), in the individuals' action under the Dram Shop Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4307 (as amended, § 2172d Cum. Supp. 1955), to recover for personal injuries.


OVERVIEW: The individuals filed suit against the owner under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4307 for injuries sustained in a car collision with another party who received alcohol from the owner. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that § 4307 was not unconstitutional for imposing liability without proof of a causal relationship between the sale of intoxicating liquor and the intoxication which caused the injury. The Dram Shop Act was a valid exercise of the legislature's police power. Also, the trial court's jury instruction on causation adequately informed the jury that the individuals were required to prove a proximate causal relationship between the party's intoxication and the injuries, although the term "proximate cause" was not employed. Further, the court ruled that the trial court properly denied the owner's motions to set aside the verdict and for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The evidence was sufficient to allow the jury to find that there was a sale of alcohol to an intoxicated person within the terms of the statute and that the damages awarded by the jury were not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the individuals.

 

859 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Perrella


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


144 Conn. 228; 129 A.2d 226; 1957 Conn. LEXIS 89


January 2, 1957, Argued  
January 22, 1957, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations charging the defendants with the crime of attempted theft, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Meyers, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty in both cases, and appeal by the defendants.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted defendants of attempted theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with attempted theft. When the trial court indicated to defendants' attorney that, in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3326d (1955 Cum. Supp.), the trial was to be to a jury of six, defendants' attorney made the claim that his clients were entitled to a trial by a jury of 12. The trial court overruled defendants' claim. Defendants were tried by a jury of six, which returned a verdict of guilty as to both defendants. The trial court convicted defendants of attempted theft. Defendants appealed, contending that a trial by six jurors violated Conn. Const. art. 1, §§ 9, 21 and that defendants did not know that by failing to claim a jury of 12 they waived their right to it. On appeal, the court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3326d (1955 Cum. Supp.), in so far as it provided for a trial to a jury of six unless at the time defendants demanded a jury of 12, did not deprive defendants of their right of trial by jury and that there was no finding that defendants were ignorant of their rights and the way to protect them. So long as defendants' election stood as one for a trial by a jury of six, the trial court had no discretion but to deny them a trial by a jury of 12.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

 

860 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Burton v. Hartford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


144 Conn. 80; 127 A.2d 251; 1956 Conn. LEXIS 248


October 11, 1956, Argued  
November 20, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity and effect of an ordinance of the defendant city concerning controlled housing accommodations, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Conway, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs brought an action in the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) against defendants, City of Hartford, treasurer, and city housing rent commissioner, seeking a declaratory judgment to determine whether an ordinance relating to controlled housing was valid. The trial court reserved the case pending advice of the court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs owned property that was used for dwelling purposes and constituted controlled housing accommodations. They sought a declaration as to the validity of the city's ordinance, which forbid the use of summary process as a means of recovering possession due to a housing emergency, that was declared by the ordinance as a result of the second world war. The trial court reserved the question of the ordinance's validity. The court first addressed the issue of whether the city charter authorized the council to enact the ordinance limiting the use of summary process. The court found that temporary rent and eviction control legislation was within the police powers granted by the city charter. The court determined, however, that because the ordinance was in conflict with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 411, which authorized a landlord to evict a tenant by summary process, the ordinance was invalid. The court also ruled that the rent control provisions were so dependent upon the validity of the eviction controls that the invalid provision was not separable despite the city's inclusion of a separability clause in the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the city's ordinance was invalid in its entirety.

Moran v. Bens


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


144 Conn. 27; 127 A.2d 42; 1956 Conn. LEXIS 241


October 9, 1956, Argued  
November 6, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of an act establishing a police department in the town of Cheshire and other questions, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, House, J.; judgment declaring the act valid and constitutional and that the plaintiffs are barred from questioning the legality of the nomination and election of certain candidates for the police commission, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff taxpayers' action against defendant officials, the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) entered a judgment declaring an act valid and constitutional and barred plaintiff taxpayers from questioning the legality of the nomination and election of certain candidates for the police commission.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought a judgment declaring special legislation that established a police department in the town unconstitutional and void and that all action taken pursuant to it was illegal. The trial court rendered a judgment sustaining the legality of the legislation and the proceedings taken by reason of it. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. In enacting special legislation, the legislature did no more than empower the town, within its own territorial limits, to provide police protection in a special manner, and to make legal what had been done through mistake when the town acted pursuant to statutes that had been repealed. Its reasons for doing so were its own, and its legislative enactments could not be successfully challenged where they were not clearly beyond the grant of legislative power and were not so arbitrary and unreasonable as to constitute an abuse of the powers conferred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory judgment in favor of the city officials.

 

862 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gordon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


143 Conn. 698; 125 A.2d 477; 1956 Conn. LEXIS 228


June 14, 1956, Argued  
July 24, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of violating a town ordinance concerning auctions, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Swain, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of violating Stratford, Conn., Ordinance §§ 1-8 concerning auctions. Defendant challenged the conviction on the grounds that the ordinance was not legally adopted as set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 197c (1954) and Stratford, Conn., Charter § 1 and that the ordinance violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of selling merchandise at a public auction past the time specified by Stratford, Conn., Ordinance §§ 1-8. On appeal, defendant challenged the validity of the ordinance. The court held that the ordinance was legally adopted because the town council followed the procedures set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 197c (1954) and Stratford, Conn., Charter § 1. The court also held that the ordinance did not violate the due process and equal protection clauses of the United States and Connecticut Constitutions. The court found that in prohibiting public auctions after a certain time, the town council sought to protect the public from the dangers that could arise after dark. Moreover, the time fixed by the ordinance was not arbitrary and unreasonable because the town council was required to fix the time with certainty. In addition, the court rejected defendant's argument that the ordinance was discriminatory because an auctioneer licensed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 990b was permitted to sell beyond the time prescribed in the ordinance. The court held that the fact that the ordinance acted in a more comprehensive manner did not render it discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for violating a town ordinance concerning auctions.
