Calve Bros. Co. v. Norwalk


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


143 Conn. 609; 124 A.2d 881; 1956 Conn. LEXIS 215


June 13, 1956, Argued  
July 17, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction to restrain the defendant from enforcing an ordinance regarding soil removal, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Ryan, J.; judgment for the defendant and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, Fairfield County (Connecticut), which denied the contractor relief in its action for an injunction to restrain defendant City of Norwalk (Connecticut) from enforcing an ordinance regulating the removal of soil for sale or for use except on the premises and for a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was not constitutionally valid.


OVERVIEW: The contractor filed an application pursuant to Norwalk, Conn., Ordinance to Regulate the Removal of Soil for Sale or for Use Other Than on the Premises and Providing Penalties for the Violation Thereof (June 18, 1952) for permission to excavate and remove gravel from its land. After the completion of the proposed excavation, the contour of the land would be changed so that a slope would extend downhill from a public street. The contractor proposed to cover the slope with topsoil that would, unless properly seeded, wash off, leaving an unsightly condition. The city denied the application on the basis of evidence that the premises was located in a residential area, the excavation would reduce land values and produce health and safety hazards, the use of heavy equipment would create noise and dust and a traffic hazard, and the excavation would cause drainage problems and would leave a slope that was too steep to hold topsoil. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the requested injunction and declaring the ordinance to be constitutional. The ordinance was a valid exercise of the city's police power to preserve the public health, safety, and welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding there was no error.

 

864 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hurliman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


143 Conn. 502; 123 A.2d 767; 1956 Conn. LEXIS 197


May 3, 1956, Argued  
June 19, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of selling on Sunday in violation of statute, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County and tried to the court, LaMacchia, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An information charged defendant with the crime of selling on Sunday in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2492c (1953). The case was brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County (Connecticut), which adjudged defendant guilty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned a delicatessen and sold liverwurst to a customer on a Sunday. The sale was not one of necessity or mercy, nor was it an excepted sale. Defendant also was not excepted from the operation of the statute because of any religious beliefs. Defendant assigned as error the overruling of his claim that the statute was unconstitutional. The court found no error in defendant's conviction. Defendant's principal contention was that the statute was discriminatory because, although it prohibited the sale of goods, wares, and merchandise generally on Sunday, it permitted the sale of a considerable number of specified articles. The court found that the issue was whether the statute, by denying to retailers of most kinds of food the right to sell on Sunday and at the same time permitting the sale of some kinds of food, treated the one class of retailers differently from the other when there was no substantial difference between them germane to the subject matter and purpose of the legislation. The court found no equal protection violation because the items permitted to be sold were of a perishable nature and the legislative classification was not arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's conviction.

 

865 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


McAdams v. Barbieri


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


143 Conn. 405; 123 A.2d 182; 1956 Conn. LEXIS 184


March 7, 1956, Argued  
May 23, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an order in the nature of a mandamus directing the defendant to reinstate the plaintiff in his position and to restore his name to the city pay roll, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Thim, J.; judgment for the plaintiff and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Director of Public Works for the City of New Haven, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff employee's request for an order in the nature of a mandamus that required the director to reinstate the employee to a position from which the director had discharged him.


OVERVIEW: The employee was hired as a temporary clerk, and stayed in that position for eight years. The lower court issued a writ of mandamus that ordered the director to reinstated the employee to his position. The crux of the matter was whether the employee was, at the time of the adoption of New Haven, Conn., Charter § 9 "holding" a "permanent position" to which he had been "appointed." The section aptly described the employee's position as clerk in the department of public works. If the employee's case was embraced by the amendment at all, he must have met the qualifications prescribed by the first sentence, and that sentence must have been construed to express a legislative intent to include employees who had no civil service status. The court affirmed the lower court's conclusion that the place or employment to which the employee was assigned in 1946 was a permanent position.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that issued a writ of mandamus that ordered the director to reinstate the employee to his clerk position in the department of public works.

 

866 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Dempsey v. Tynan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


143 Conn. 202; 120 A.2d 700; 1956 Conn. LEXIS 150


January 5, 1956, Argued  
February 10, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the commissioner of motor vehicles in suspending the operator's license and automobile registration of the plaintiff, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, FitzGerald, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal and reversing the action of the commissioner, from which the defendant and the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in form of judgment; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1048c (Cum. Supp. 1953), plaintiff driver appealed the action of the Connecticut Commissioner of Motor Vehicles in suspending his operator's license and automobile registration. After a nonjury trial, the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut) reversed the commissioner's action. The commissioner appealed. The driver filed a cross appeal but failed to appear and urge it.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner acted under the financial responsibility provisions of the motor vehicle law. The driver was not insured or exempt under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1053c (Cum. Supp. 1953). The driver had not been required to furnish proof of financial responsibility under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1044c (Cum. Supp. 1953). After an accident, a pedestrian sued the driver for personal injuries and had an attachment filed against the driver's house. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1051c (Cum. Supp. 1953), the Commissioner requested the driver to deposit a specified sum in cash or its equivalent as security for the pedestrian's claim or suffer the suspension of his motor vehicle registration and operator's license. The Commissioner refused to accept evidence of the attachment as security unless the driver secured from the pedestrian or his attorney an affidavit that the attachment was satisfactory security. In conferring power upon the commissioner in such broad language, the court held that the legislature did not intend to allow the Commissioner to refuse to consider the existence of a substantial attachment. The court explained that the Commissioner mistook the law and abused his discretion.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment and remanded the proceeding with direction to render judgment in accordance with the opinion.

 

867 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Swanson v. Boschen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


143 Conn. 159; 120 A.2d 546; 1956 Conn. LEXIS 144


December 7, 1955, Argued  
January 27, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for violation of the Housing and Rent Act in making overcharges of rent, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County, where the defendant filed a counterclaim, a motion by the plaintiffs to strike the case from the jury docket was granted, Johnson, J., and the issues were tried to the court, LaMacchia, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs on the complaint and the counterclaim, and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landlord challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County (Connecticut), which, in plaintiff tenants' action to recover damages for violation of the Housing and Rent Act, 50 U.S.C.S. App. § 1895, in the landlord's overcharge of rent, granted the tenants' motion to strike the case from the jury docket and held in favor of the tenants.


OVERVIEW: The tenants filed a cause of action against the landlord to recover rent in excess of the amount fixed by the area rent director under the Act. The tenants also sought treble damages. The case was docketed as a jury case. The tenants moved to strike the case from the jury docket, and the trial court granted their motion. Judgment was rendered for the tenants. The court found that the underlying issue was whether the landlord was subject to a penalty in addition to the rent overcharge. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7936, as amended, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2387c, the present case was a civil action involving an issue which, prior to January 1, 1880, would not present a question properly cognizable in equity and therefore triable only to the court without a jury. The question, then, was whether the case was a "special statutory proceeding," which entitled the landlord to a jury trial. The court found that the trial court erred in striking the case from the jury docket. Actions for treble damages under the Act were triable to a jury in the federal courts.


OUTCOME: The court, finding lower court error, ordered a new trial between the tenants and landlord.

Proctor v. Sachner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


143 Conn. 9; 118 A.2d 621; 1955 Conn. LEXIS 120


October 11, 1955, Argued  
November 21, 1955, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for support, initiated in Ohio and brought by exemplified copy to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Swain, J.; judgment directing payments to be made for the support of the dependent named in the petition, and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiff mother, defendant father sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which directed him to pay $ 60 per month for the support of the parties' minor child.


OVERVIEW: The parties were divorced in Ohio. On appeal, the father argued that the judgment directing him to pay $ 60 per month was beyond the power of the trial court and void, and that the trial court did not have the power to order him to pay any sum greater than $ 5 weekly. Upon review, the court found the father's arguments without merit. By the terms of the separation agreement and the divorce decree, the amount of the payments made by the father was subject to change by a court having jurisdiction. The father was summoned to appear to show cause why the order for support prayed for by the mother should not have been made. He did not appear until after the time set and then only after an order had been made. Although he had the right to appear and show cause why the order for support prayed for should not have been granted, to file a verified denial of any of the material allegations of the petition, and to examine or cross-examine the wife and her witnesses by means of depositions or written interrogatories, as provided in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2451c, he failed to do so. The father was not denied due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment ordering the father to pay $ 60 per month in support for the parties' minor child.

 

869 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Cyphers v. Allyn


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


142 Conn. 699; 118 A.2d 318; 1955 Conn. LEXIS 226


October 5, 1955, Argued  
November 8, 1955, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the act concerning the regulation and licensing of real estate salesmen and brokers, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and reserved by the court, Molloy, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real estate broker filed a declaratory action against defendant state insurance commissioner in the Superior Court of New Haven (Connecticut), which challenged the constitutionality of an act concerning the regulation and licensing of real estate salesmen and brokers. The superior court reserved ruling for the advice of the court.


OVERVIEW: The broker filed a declaratory action on behalf of all Connecticut real estate salespersons and brokers seeking a declaration of rights regarding an act concerning the supervision, regulation, and licensing of realtors and brokers. The court found the legislation was within the State's police powers as a legitimate regulation for the public safety and welfare. The court noted that in other states, statutes requiring a license to engage in the business of real estate broker or salesman were generally held not to be violative of the equal protection and due process clauses of the federal Constitution. They were sustained as a lawful exercise of the police power of the state in the interest of the public welfare. The court further noted that the legislative department was the judge, within reasonable limits, of what the public welfare required, and the wisdom of its legislation was not the concern of the courts. Courts would not hold laws, ordinances, or regulations adopted under sanction of law to be unconstitutional unless they were clearly unreasonable, destructive, or confiscatory. These regulations were clearly for the public's safety and protection.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the licensing of real estate brokers and salesmen was within the legitimate exercise of the police power of the State when done in a reasonable manner.

Franklin Furniture Co. v. Bridgeport


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


142 Conn. 510; 115 A.2d 435; 1955 Conn. LEXIS 199


May 11, 1955, Argued  
June 27, 1955, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction against the enforcement of an ordinance concerning advertising signs and for a judgment declaring the ordinance void, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Thim, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff furniture company appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which denied a request to impose an injunction on defendants, the City of Bridgeport, Connecticut and others, to restrain the enforcement of Bridgeport, Conn., Ordinances of March 17, 1952, concerning advertising signs, and to declare the ordinance void.


OVERVIEW: The furniture company argued that the trial court erred in finding that the City had the power to prohibit the maintenance and erection of projecting advertising signs over sidewalks. On review, the court found that there was no error. The court concluded that the passage of the ordinance by the City's common council was not an arbitrary, unreasonable, or invalid exercise of the police power that deprived the company of its property without due process of law. The court rejected an argument that the ordinance contained discriminatory features rendering it unconstitutional. The furniture company failed to persuade the court that once having erected an expensive sign, it therefore was entitled to have the sign endure notwithstanding the valid city ordinance. The court also rejected the claim that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it compelled the removal of overhanging signs without any prior determination that such signs were hazardous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

871 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


First Federal Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Connelly


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


142 Conn. 483; 115 A.2d 455; 1955 Conn. LEXIS 196


May 10, 1955, Argued  
June 21, 1955, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an assessment of an additional corporation business tax, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, King, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Federal Savings and Loan Association sought review of a decision from the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) upholding an assessment by appellee Tax Commissioner of an additional corporation business tax upon the association's net income. The association contended that dividends paid to depositors were not in fact interest and could not be taxed under Conn. Cum. Sup. § 886c (1953).


OVERVIEW: A savings and loan association filed suit challenging an assessment of an additional corporation business tax upon the association's net income. The association contended that the assessment on dividends paid or credited to depositors on deposits or withdrawable accounts did not exist in the federal tax legislation and contended that the retroactive application of the state tax statute violated the due process clauses of the federal and statute constitutions. The court affirmed the superior court's order upholding the Tax Commissioner's assessment and concluded that the amount paid by the association as dividends or interest was interest paid within the meaning of the tax statute and thus, the amounts were properly taxable. Although the federal tax code allowed the deduction from gross income of dividends paid by banking corporations, the court held that the state legislature had the power to enact tax provisions different from those contained in the federal legislation. The court held the retroactive effect of the statute did not render it unconstitutional since the association would reasonably have anticipated either the nature or the amount of the tax it was expected to pay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order upholding the Tax Commissioner's assessment of an additional corporation business tax upon the savings and loan association's net income. The court concluded that the dividends paid or credited to depositors were properly taxed under the tax statute and held the statute was constitutional.

 

872 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Florentine v. Darien


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


142 Conn. 415; 115 A.2d 328; 1955 Conn. LEXIS 188


April 7, 1955, Argued  
June 7, 1955, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction against enforcement of a regulation rezoning a tract, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Shannon, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs and appeal by the defendants.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and its zoning commission (city), rezoned the area in which lands owned and controlled by plaintiff landowners were located. The landowners sought to have their property rezoned, but their petition was denied. They did not request a variance, but sought an injunction against enforcement of the rezoning regulation. The Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) awarded the landowners recovery, and the city sought review.


OVERVIEW: The city claimed that the lower court erroneously issued an injunction on the grounds that the regulation was unconstitutional. The court agreed, reversed the lower court's judgment, and entered judgment in favor of the city. The court found that zoning regulations were required to have a rational relation to the health, welfare, safety, and prosperity of the community and that if this police power was reasonably exercised, the regulations would be upheld. The court found that the city's urgent traffic problems justified the rezoning regulations and that they were valid. However, the court found that even valid zoning regulations were unconstitutional if they were applied in an arbitrary or confiscatory manner and that the zoning board of appeals existed to assure that the regulations were properly applied. Thus, the court held that the landowners were not entitled to seek injunctive relief until they were granted or denied a variance, and the action of the zoning authorities had thus become complete and final. Accordingly, because the landowners had not sought a variance or relief from the zoning board of appeals, the court held that the injunction was improperly issued.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded the case with directions for the lower court to enter judgment for the city.

West v. Egan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


142 Conn. 437; 115 A.2d 322; 1955 Conn. LEXIS 190; 28 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P69,288


May 5, 1955, Argued  
June 7, 1955, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from administrative regulations promulgated by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Thim, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employers sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal of its decision granting judgment for defendant labor commissioner in the business owners' challenge of the commissioner's establishment of a regulation under the minimum wage law, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 180.


OVERVIEW: The labor commissioner established a regulation fixing a minimum wage for waiters and waitresses under the minimum wage law, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 180. The employers challenged the labor commissioner's decision. The court affirmed the trial court's decision dismissing the employers' appeal. The court determined that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1527c was not an unconstitutionally invalid illegal delegation of legislative power to the labor commissioner. When the constitutionality of legislation was in question, it was the court's duty to sustain it unless its invalidity was beyond a reasonable doubt. Legislation designed to accomplish a particular purpose could authorize an administrative agency to provide the details of the operation of the statute through rules and regulations made and promulgated by the agency. The statute and the regulation acted in a field appropriate to the reasonable exercise of the police power by the state, and they did so in a manner that did not contravene constitutional principles of due process or equal protection of the laws. It was not the court's job to determine whether gratuities should have been included as part of the legal wage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision dismissing the employers' appeal of the trial court's decision granting judgment for defendant labor commissioner in the business owners' challenge of the commissioner's establishment of a regulation under the minimum wage law.

Cedar Island Improv. Asso. v. Clinton Electric Light & Power Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

142 Conn. 359; 114 A.2d 535; 1955 Conn. LEXIS 179


April 6, 1955, Argued

The plaintiffs and the defendant public utilities commission filed motions for reargument which were denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Middlesex County (Connecticut) reserved for the advice of the court plaintiff island association's action seeking review of defendant public utilities commission's denial of a petition seeking an order compelling the extension of electric service to the island by defendant electric companies.


OVERVIEW: The association filed a petition with the commission, seeking an order to compel the electric companies to extend electric service to the island. The commission denied the petition, and the association sought review. The trial court reserved to the court for the court's advice. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5673, the commission was required to order and direct the electric companies to distribute current in the state to extend their lines in their chartered territory to all "unserved areas" having a density of subscribers for electric service averaging at least two per mile. The court further found that, in fixing the rates, the commission was directed to exercise its statutory powers and to consider the expenses of the electric companies. The court determined that, under the statute, the trial court was only to require such extensions as the commission found reasonable under all circumstances. The court found that the factors that entered into the determination of reasonableness were the need and cost of the extension, the return to be expected, and the effect upon the electric companies' revenues. The court declined to answer the questions and remanded to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the action and declined to answer the questions asked by the trial court.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor appealed the decision of the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted him of making and fitting ophthalmic products without a license, operating an optical establishment without an optical license selling permit, and processing optical glasses and instruments without an optical license processing permit.

Romanov v. Dental Com. of State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


142 Conn. 44; 111 A.2d 9; 1955 Conn. LEXIS 136


October 15, 1954, Argued  
January 4, 1955, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from holding a hearing on charges against the plaintiff, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County by transfer from the Court of Common Pleas and tried to the court, Bordon, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dentist sought review of the decision from the of the Superior Court In Hartford County, (Connecticut), which granted judgment in favor of defendants, a state dental commission and its commissioners, in the dentist's action for an injunction to restrain defendant's from holding a hearing on charges against the dentist.


OVERVIEW: The commission, purporting to act under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4452, ordered a hearing on the charges contained in a complaint against the dentist that alleged that he had violated advertising restrictions placed on dentists by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1695. The dentist filed an action that sought an injunction to prevent defendants from holding a hearing. The trial court granted judgment in favor of defendants. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the fact that a grievance committee had not been organized, as provided for in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1697c, did not prevent the commission from taking action against the dentist. The court held that the two provisions were designed to accomplish different objectives; Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4452 was designed to discipline dentists, and the grievance committee provided for in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1697c had the purpose of policing the dental profession and provided a method to refer complaints to the committee. The court also held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4452 had not been repealed by the repeal of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4450. The court also concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4552 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of defendants.

State v. Donahue


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


141 Conn. 656; 109 A.2d 364; 1954 Conn. LEXIS 240


October 5, 1954, Argued  
November 9, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the jury before Troland, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found the trial court properly presented the issue of whether defendant was guilty of murder only in the second degree where the jury charge emphasized that proof of willfulness, deliberation, and premeditation, beyond a reasonable doubt, was indispensable to a conviction of murder in the first degree. The court determined that defendant did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1406b (Cum. Supp. 1951), where defendant was not harmed by application of the statute because the statute gave defendant a chance to receive a life sentence rather than a sentence of death, which was not an alternative prior to the passage of the statute. The court concluded that hypothetical questions presented to experts regarding defendant's mental capacity were properly excluded where the propounded questions sought to elicit an expression of opinion upon whether defendant acted in a wilful, deliberate, and premeditated manner, which were questions for the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of murder in the first degree.

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County (Connecticut), which dismissed its appeal of a decision by appellee city officials requiring the owner to make changes in its hotel and its request for an injunction restraining the city officials from proceeding with the orders.


OVERVIEW: The city officials notified the owner by letter that certain changes were to be made to its hotel for the fire safety of the building and provided it with a deadline to make the changes. It found that the statutes under consideration had as their purpose the reasonable safety from fire, smoke and panic, which was a legislative policy within the police power of the State of Connecticut. Further, the legislature could delegate to an administrative agency the power to fill in details of the legislation by prescribing rules and regulations for the operation and enforcement of the fire safety code. Finally, the court found that the fire safety code laid out standards from which to furnish a suitable guide to the adoption of regulations applicable to the code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed the owner's appeal of an order of the city officials requiring it to make certain changes to its hotel and its request for an injunction enjoining the city officials from enforcing the order.

Hoenig v. Connelly


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


141 Conn. 266; 105 A.2d 775; 1954 Conn. LEXIS 186


April 8, 1954, Argued  
May 18, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decree of the Probate Court for the district of Ridgefield determining the amount of a succession tax, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Cullinan, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal and affirming the decree, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executors sought review of a decree from the Superior Court of Fairfield County (Connecticut), which affirmed a judgment that determined the amount of a succession tax owed on a testator's estate in an action brought by the executors against defendant tax commissioner in which they challenged a tax assessment.


OVERVIEW: The executors of the testator's will filed an action against the tax commissioner alleging that a bequest made in a will to trustees of a fund was exempt from a succession tax. The probate court held that the bequest was not exempt from taxation and determined the amount of a succession tax owed on the testator's estate. A lower appellate court affirmed. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court held that the bequest was not subject to exemption where a trust company named in the bequest was not the entity that was to administer the charity pursuant to the terms of the will. The court noted the only function of the trust company named by the bequest was as the successor trustee so as to organize a foundation and turn over the residue over to it or, if the foundation was not organized, to turn the residues over to a set of trustees. The court determined the trial court properly held the bequest was not exempt under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 489c (Cum. Supp. 1935) where more than five years had elapsed between the death of the testator and the charitable corporation named under the bequest had not yet been organized. The court concluded that § 489c was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decree that upheld a judgment determining the amount of a succession tax owed on the testator's estate.

 

880 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Amsel v. Brooks


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


141 Conn. 288; 106 A.2d 152; 1954 Conn. LEXIS 189; 45 A.L.R.2d 1234


April 6, 1954, Argued  
May 18, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the 1953 act concerning the practice of dentistry, and for an injunction, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and reserved by the court, Conway, J., for the advice of this court.

The plaintiffs and the defendants filed motions for reargument which were denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, partners doing business as a dental laboratory (dental laboratory), filed an action against defendant, Dental Commission of the State of Connecticut (commission), in the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), asking for a judgment declaring unconstitutional Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 1696c, 1697c. (Cum. Supp. 1953), entitled: An Act concerning the Practice of Dentistry. The case was reserved for advice to the court.


OVERVIEW: The dental laboratory claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1696c was unconstitutional because it served only the interest of licensed dentists and failed to furnish the public with any protection and because it did not clearly define the act or acts which constituted a violation of its provisions. The court held that the portion of § 1696c that dealt with advertising was invalid but that the remaining portions were valid. The court determined that addressing the making, fitting, and repairing of artificial dentures constituted a calling intimately concerned with the public health and that one who pursued such activities was required to have an accurate knowledge of the physiology of the teeth and the parts of the human body associated with them as well as a high degree of technical skill. As such, the court found that the language of § 1696c addressing those activities was designed to serve the public health effectively and was not an unreasonable or arbitrary exercise of the police power. The court opined, however, that the portion of § 1696c that contained the prohibition against advertising was so sweeping in its effect that it was not a valid exercise of the state's police power.


OUTCOME: The court answered the questions propounded in the reservation by declaring that the statute was constitutionally valid except for the portion that contained the prohibition against advertising, which the court declared invalid.

Watrous v. Connelly


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


141 Conn. 257; 105 A.2d 654; 1954 Conn. LEXIS 185; 46 A.F.T.R. (P-H) 429


April 7, 1954, Argued  
May 12, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decree of the Probate Court for the district of New Haven approving the computation of a succession tax, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Alcorn, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal and affirming the decree, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the executors and the devisees and residuary legatees under the will of the testatrix, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), dismissing an appeal from and affirming a decree of the probate court that approved, as computed by defendant, the tax commissioner, the succession tax laid upon the estate of the testatrix and the order to pay it.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were ordered by the tax commissioner to pay the succession tax laid upon the estate of the testatrix and the probate court confirmed the decision. The trial court affirmed the decision of the probate court. The main question was whether the amount of the federal estate tax should have been deducted from the gross estate in the determination of the net estate by which the succession tax was measured. Plaintiffs claimed that the amount paid to the federal government for the federal estate tax should not have been included in the net estate upon which a Connecticut succession tax was payable. The court held there was no error in the decision. The succession tax was a tax upon the privilege of beneficial succession and was levied with regard to that portion of the estate that would have passed to the transferees. That the base chosen for the computation of the tax included the amount of the federal estate tax was not in conflict with the fundamental theory of the legislation. The probate court construed the statute correctly, and the statute was one within the constitutional powers of the legislature to enact.


OUTCOME: There was no error in the trial court's decision to affirm the judgment of the probate court that approved, as computed by the tax commissioner, the succession tax laid upon the estate of the testatrix.

Gibson v. Connecticut Medical Examining Board


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


141 Conn. 218; 104 A.2d 890; 1954 Conn. LEXIS 179


March 2, 1954, Argued  
April 20, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition in the nature of an appeal from the action of the named defendant recommending that the plaintiff's license to practice medicine be revoked and from the action of the defendant state department of health revoking it, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Roberts, J.; judgment for the defendants and dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctor sought review from a decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which awarded judgment to defendant state Medical Examining Board, in their action recommending that the doctor's license to practice medicine be revoked for improper professional conduct in the practice of his profession.


OVERVIEW: The doctor was charged with being guilty of unprofessional or incompetent conduct in failing to make necessary tests to corroborate the diagnosis of the ailments of his patient. The doctor contended that another physician, whom he called in as a consultant, made the diagnosis of the patient. The court disagreed. The consultant doctor suggested that the patient continue on her prescribed medication and that efforts should be made to confirm whether she suffered from myocarditis, possible nephritis, and a possible malignant bowel, by x-ray and other tests. The doctor did not perform any tests to confirm the consulting doctor's tentative diagnosis. The doctor did not secure nurses for the patient. Instead, the doctor's mother, who was in her late seventies and had no nursing experience, cared for the patient. The patient was not admitted to the hospital until a week before she died. The court held that the Board would be justified in concluding that the care that the patient received from the doctor fell far short of what professional standards required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Bassett v. Rose


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


141 Conn. 129; 104 A.2d 212; 1954 Conn. LEXIS 167


February 2, 1954, Argued  
March 30, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action by a taxpayer to enjoin the collection of taxes, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Quinlan, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which ruled in favor of defendant Acting Tax Collector of the Town of Milford in the taxpayer's action challenging the constitutionality of 1951 Conn. Acts 175 § 3 (Spec. Sess.), which changed the fiscal year for the Town.


OVERVIEW: The Town's council passed an ordinance and the General Assembly enacted a special act that provided that in 1951 the Town's fiscal period would run from October 1 to June 30, 1952, and thereafter the fiscal year would begin on July 1. The Town determined that for the 10-month change-over period, it would use the October 1950 tax list as the basis for the tax levy. The taxpayer filed an action challenging the constitutionality of the special act, arguing that it discriminated among taxpayers because it required those whose properties were assessed as of October 1950 to pay taxes on a valuation set as of that date, and freed from taxation entirely those whose properties were not on the list on October 1950. The trial court upheld the validity of the special act and the taxpayer appealed. The court stated an act was not discriminatory if it treated all persons who were in the same class on an equal basis and if there was a reasonable distinction between the members of that class and all other classes. The court concluded that the special act was not discriminatory because it treated equally all taxpayers whose property was listed on October 1950.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the trial court had rendered in favor of the Town in the taxpayer's challenge to the act changing the dates of the Town's fiscal period.

Gohld Realty Co. v. Hartford

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the Redevelopment Act, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Shapiro, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) that found in favor of defendant city in the taxpayer's action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the Redevelopment Act.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted the Redevelopment Act and created a redevelopment agency whereby if the taxpayer was not willing to sell its property, the city would have acquired it by condemnation proceedings. In affirming, the court held that the Redevelopment Act was constitutional in granting to the city the power of eminent domain. The court found that the grant of the power of eminent domain contained in the Redevelopment Act was not unconstitutional and that the city could acquire by eminent domain all property which the agency had determined to be essential to complete the acquisition and development of the area in question, including vacant and unimproved land and structures not in themselves substandard. The court further held that such power was not an unlawful delegation of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court and held that the Redevelopment Act was constitutional.

Jennings v. Connecticut Light & Power Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


140 Conn. 650; 103 A.2d 535; 1954 Conn. LEXIS 149


December 3, 1953, Argued  
February 9, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of a statute concerning location of power plants, and other questions, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County, where the named defendant filed a counterclaim and the case was reserved by the court, Cullinan, J., for the advice of this court.

The plaintiffs filed motions for reargument which were denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The action for declaratory judgment brought by plaintiff property owners, of land in Norwalk, and the counterclaim for declaratory judgment brought by defendants, electric company and members of Norwalk zoning commission, against defendant property owners, of land in Harbor View, were reserved by the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) for the advice of the court.


OVERVIEW: The property owners, who owned land in Norwalk, brought an action for declaratory judgment against the electric company and Norwalk Zoning Commission. The electric company and Commission brought a counterclaim against joined the property owners, of land in Harbor View. Both actions were reserved by the lower court for advice from the court. The court held that the Commission, in conducting its hearing and issuing its order regarding the electric company's proposed steam plant, acted as an agency of the state designated to fulfil a special function under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5646, and properly received the electric company's application with regard to the location of the plant, and was empowered to issue its order regulating and restricting its location. The Commission was in a position to appraise not only the welfare of its community, but also the larger welfare of the state as a whole. The court held that § 5646, as interpreted and applied by the Commission, complied with constitutional requirements, because its order was made in the interest of public health, safety, and welfare, and the public convenience and necessity.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant Norwalk zoning commission's order regulating and restricting the location of defendant electric company's proposed steam plant was valid.

Clapp v. Ulbrich


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


140 Conn. 637; 103 A.2d 195; 1954 Conn. LEXIS 146; 45 A.L.R.2d 1386


December 3, 1953, Argued  
February 9, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality and validity of a statute regulating the licensing of junk dealers, and for an injunction restraining the defendants from enforcing that statute against the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Daly, J.; judgment declaring the statute constitutional and valid and denying the injunction, and appeal by the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant junk dealer challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which found that a statute regulating the licensing of junk dealers was constitutional and denied his request for an injunction restraining appellee borough officials from enforcing the statute against the junk dealer.


OVERVIEW: The junk dealer operated a business on his premises. He entered the military and, upon his return to civilian life, he resumed his junk business. At no time had he obtained a license to engage in the junk business in the borough and continued operating his business, even though his applications for a junk dealer's license was denied. The junk dealer then brought a declaratory judgment action to determine the constitutionality of the statute requiring him to obtain a license and requested the borough officials be enjoined from enforcing the statute against him. The trial court found the statute was constitutional and denied the request for an injunction. The court affirmed, finding that the statute was constitutional. It held that it was permissible to regulate junk dealers in the interests of public safety and that the purpose of the statute was to assure that the junk business would be conducted in a legitimate manner. Further, the statute did not give the official any discretion once it was established that an applicant for a license was a suitable person and did not give the official any power over where the business was to be conducted under the license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which found that the statute regulating the licensing of junk dealers was constitutional and denied the junk dealer's request for an order restraining the enforcement of the statute against him.

 

887 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vachon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


140 Conn. 478; 101 A.2d 509; 1953 Conn. LEXIS 267


October 13, 1953, Argued  
December 8, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of operating a hospital and maintaining a home for the aged without a license, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New London County, where a demurrer to the information was overruled and the issues were tried to the court, Loiselle, J.; judgment of guilty on both counts and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in New London County (Connecticut), which convicted him of operating a hospital and maintaining a home for the aged without a license in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3823 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 579b (1951 Cum. Supp.).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that both statutes were an illegal and unconstitutional delegation of the legislative power of the General Assembly to an administrative board. The court determined that the power of the legislature to require a license for the transaction of business for the purpose of regulating its conduct was a proper exercise of police power. The court explained that the legislature's delegation of power was admissible if the statutes declared a legislative policy, established primary standards for carrying it out, or laid down an intelligible principle to which the administrative officer or body had to conform. The court noted that a sanitary code, authorized by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3800, provided safeguards and precautions for the care of patients in a hospital. The court concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3823 indicated a policy on the part of the legislature of preserving the public health by a sanitary code. The court determined that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 579b provided the standard for the age of the persons to be cared for, stated the minimum number of persons to be housed before the act became obligatory, and required that the person licensed be a suitable person.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

888 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Corthouts v. Newington


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


140 Conn. 284; 99 A.2d 112; 1953 Conn. LEXIS 238; 38 A.L.R.2d 1136


June 11, 1953, Argued  
August 4, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining whether an amendment to the zoning ordinance of Newington was a lawful and constitutional exercise of the powers vested in the zoning commission, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried to the court, Troland, J.; judgment declaring the amendment unconstitutional and void, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town and its zoning commission sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Hartford County (Connecticut), which found for plaintiff property owner in his action to enjoin defendants from the enforcement of an amendment to a zoning ordinance because the amendment was an unconstitutional exercise of the powers vested in defendants.


OVERVIEW: The amendment to the zoning ordinance prohibited the use of land for residential purposes in an industrial zone. The town was neither well-settled nor an industrial community. The owner purchased a tract of land for the purpose of erecting dwelling houses. There were several dwelling houses in the residence "B" zone adjacent to his land. The westerly portion of his lot was located in the residential district. When the owner purchased the land, the zoning ordinance permitted the use of land in the industrial district for residential purposes. The owner's land was adapted for residential use, for which there was a demand. Upon review, the court found that a residential use of the owner's land was the highest and best use to which it could have been put. There was no demand for an industrial use of the land, nor was there likely to be such a demand in the near future. The amendment was not a valid exercise of police power because there was no rational relationship to the public health, safety, welfare and prosperity of the community. Because the amendment prevented the owner from using his land for any feasible purpose, it was unreasonable and confiscatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the owner in his action to enjoin defendants from the enforcement of the amendment to the zoning ordinance.

Schwartz v. Kelly


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


140 Conn. 176; 99 A.2d 89; 1953 Conn. LEXIS 222


June 2, 1953, Argued  
July 21, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from imposing minimum consumer resale prices upon products sold by the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Mellitz, J.; judgment for the defendants and appeal by the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, package store permittees, challenged a judgment rendered in favor of defendant Liquor Control Commission in the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) in their action seeking an injunction restraining the Commission from enforcing the Liquor Control Act, 1951 Conn. Pub. Acts 200, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 904b-907b (Cum Supp. 1951).


OVERVIEW: The permittees sought to enjoin the Commission from imposing minimum consumer resale prices upon products they sold. They claimed that the Act was unconstitutional because it violated the due process clauses of both the federal and the State constitutions, it provided for an improper delegation of legislative power, and it contravened the interstate commerce clause of the federal constitution. The court held that the Act was not violative of the due process provisions of the federal and State constitutions because it was within the police power, and it was not discriminatory. The Act did make a differentiation between permittees for the retail sale of liquor not to be consumed on the premises and other retail permittees. There was no delegation of legislative powers to wholesalers. Even thought the Act imposed a condition upon the importation of alcoholic liquors into the State, it in no way contravened the interstate commerce clause of the United States Constitution. By virtue of the 21st Amendment, the states were free to enact laws prohibiting, restricting, or regulating the bringing of intoxicating liquors into their territories completely unfettered by the commerce clause.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment.

Beckanstin v. Liquor Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


140 Conn. 185; 99 A.2d 119; 1953 Conn. LEXIS 223


June 10, 1953, Argued  
July 21, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant in suspending the wholesaler liquor permit of the plaintiff, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Dwyer, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff permittee sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal from a decision of defendant liquor control commission to suspend his wholesaler's liquor permit for 45 days because of violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4306 and Conn. Agencies Regs. § 151-19 (1948).


OVERVIEW: An employee of the permittee's liquor company gave customers bonus bottles of liquor or paid them rebates and did not put the rebate on the customer's invoice. There was no direct evidence that the permittee authorized the employee to take such actions or that he was aware the employee was doing it. The committee concluded that each transaction was a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4306 and its regulation that required accurate invoices. The committee found that the permittee was an unsuitable person, which warranted the suspension of his permit. The permittee contended that the action of the commission was illegal and that § 4306 was unconstitutional. Upon review, the court found that the use of "allow" in § 4306 did not mean that the permittee had to have actual knowledge that the employee gave a rebate or free goods to its customer, the only question was whether the permittee was responsible for the employee's action in making the allowance. Under the circumstances, the permittee was responsible for the employee's conduct. Thus, the permittee violated § 4306. The statute was constitutional because the permit was a privilege, not a right, and did not constitute property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the permittee's appeal from the committee's decision that suspended his liquor permit.

Macy v. Cunningham


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


140 Conn. 124; 98 A.2d 800; 1953 Conn. LEXIS 214


May 7, 1953, Argued  
July 7, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decree of the Probate Court for the district of Hartford appointing certain parties successor trustees of a testamentary trust, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Cullinan, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an appeal by plaintiffs, the public works commissioner and the attorney general, the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) certified questions concerning the issue of a probate court's appointment of defendant successor trustees to administer a testamentary trust.


OVERVIEW: The deceased created a testamentary trust to construct a memorial to her father. The provision stated that the memorial was to be artistic in design and that the state commission of sculpture, later the commission on fine arts, was the trustee. The state then abolished the fine arts commission and created a public works department. The public works commissioner asked the probate court to appoint him as successor trustee, but the probate court refused and appointed members of the commission on fine arts at the time it was abolished as trustees. In responding to certified questions, the court found that the probate court did not abuse its discretion in appointing the successor trustees. While the powers formerly granted to the commission on fine arts were transferred to the public works commissioner, so far as trusts were concerned, the only thing transferred was the power to act as trustee. No specific trusteeship was granted to the public works department. The court also found that the deceased's will did not contain any direction that public officials be named as the trustees.


OUTCOME: The court found that the probate court did not abuse its discretion in appointing the successor trustees of the testamentary trust.

Barnes v. New Haven


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


140 Conn. 8; 98 A.2d 523; 1953 Conn. LEXIS 199


April 8, 1953, Argued  
June 2, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the legality of the creation and maintenance by the named defendant of a parking authority, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and reserved by the court, Murphy, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This action was brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) and reserved by the superior court for the advice of the court. The case involved an action for a declaratory judgment determining the legality of the creation and maintenance, by defendant city, of a parking authority.


OVERVIEW: The issue in this case was whether the parking project, for which the act in question provided, was a legitimate public purpose. The court held that the aggravated nature of the traffic problem on city streets and the serious effect which it had upon a very large part of the public in such localities were matters of common knowledge of which courts could take judicial notice. The court held that the broad provision in Conn. Const. art. III, § 1, which vested the legislative power in the General Assembly, was subject to the limitation that an act which served no other purpose than individual gain or profit goes beyond the power of that body to enact and was necessarily void. However, the court held that the very substantial weight of authority supported the conclusion that the use in question, the parking project, was a legitimate public use. The court held that since the development and operation of parking facilities was a proper municipal function devoted to a public purpose, public property of all kinds, as well as public funds in the manner provided in the act, could be used for the purpose.


OUTCOME: The court held that the development and operation of parking facilities was a proper municipal function devoted to a public purpose and that public property of all kinds, as well as public funds in the manner provided in the act, could be used for the purpose.

 

893 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Weidlich v. First Nat'l Bank & Trust Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


139 Conn. 652; 96 A.2d 547; 1953 Conn. LEXIS 180


March 4, 1953, Argued  
April 21, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decree of the Probate Court for the district of Fairfield awarding a further monthly allowance for the support of the widow, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Molloy, J.; judgment confirming the order and dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant remainderman challenged an order of a Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which affirmed a probate court order that granted a widow a further allowance upon petition by appellee executors.


OVERVIEW: Stating that settlement of the estate would take some more time, the executors petitioned the probate court for a further widow's allowance. The superior court affirmed, stating that the remainderman was not aggrieved by the decision. In affirming, the court noted that a clause in decedent's will directed the executors to apply for an allowance for the widow's support while the estate was in the process of settlement and further directed that if, for any reason, allowance was not made, the executors were to pay the widow, for her support and maintenance, a monthly sum while the estate was in the process of settlement. Giving effect to the decedent's intention to provide liberally for his widow, the court stated that the widow was to receive the stated monthly sum either as an allowance or as a bequest. In reality, the clause was a pecuniary bequest made on condition. As such, even if the remainderman prevailed and the order for further allowance failed, the widow would have received the same sum by bequest. The remaindermen's pecuniary position would be the same.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

894 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Warner v. Gabb


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


139 Conn. 310; 93 A.2d 487; 1952 Conn. LEXIS 194


October 14, 1952, Argued  
December 9, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of a special act concerning retirement credit for veterans in the employ of the city of Hartford, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Cullinan, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff veteran brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant in the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), seeking a determination of his retirement benefits under Conn. Spec. Act No. 281 (1949) (1949 Act), based on his service to the city and on his service in World War I and World War II. The trial court reserved for advice from the court the issue of whether the 1949 Act was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The veteran became a firefighter for the City of Hartford after his service in World War I. He was then called to serve in World War II after which he returned to the fire department. Upon retirement, he was entitled to add to the term of his service in World War I and World War II to his actual service for the city by virtue of Conn. Spec. Act No. 394 (1945). The veteran claimed that by reason of the 1949 Act, he was entitled to an additional credit of one month for each month of his service in the armed forces during World War II. Defendant asserted that the 1949 Act was invalid because it constituted exclusive emoluments to a group of policemen and firemen based upon no reasonable classification. The 1949 Act gave the extra benefits only to policemen and firemen who served the city prior to serving in World War II. The court held that the 1949 Act was unconstitutional because the preference of World War II veterans who were members of the police and fire departments before they entered military service over World War II veterans who were new to the departments after World War II was too nebulous to afford a reasonable basis for the difference in their treatment.


OUTCOME: The court held that the 1949 Act was unconstitutional.

 

895 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Rourke v. Barbieri


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


139 Conn. 203; 91 A.2d 773; 1952 Conn. LEXIS 178


October 7, 1952, Argued  
October 15, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an order in the nature of a mandamus directing the defendant to place the question of a council-manager charter for the city of New Haven on the voting machines at the general election of November 4, 1952, and for an injunction, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County, where a demurrer was sustained as to the plaintiff's claim for a mandamus and was overruled as to his claim for an injunction, and, upon stipulation of the parties, the court, FitzGerald, J., rendered judgment from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city elector filed an action in the Court of Common Pleas in New Haven County (Connecticut) for an order in the nature of a mandamus directing defendant town clerk to place the question of a council-manager charter for the city on the voting machines at a general election, and for an injunction. The trial court sustained the clerk's demurrer, overruled the elector's claim for an injunction, and rendered judgment. The elector appealed.


OVERVIEW: The clerk did not intend to comply with the petitioners' request made in a petition that the proposed charter be acted upon at a general election, but had determined to give warning of a special election in accordance with an order of the board of aldermen. The trial court held that the Home Rule Act of 1951, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 118b, 119b (1951), did not empower the town clerk or the signers of the petition to set the election day on the referendum. On appeal, the clerk argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 118b vested in the board of aldermen the discretion of deciding whether the proposed change should be submitted at either a special or a general election. The court found that the board of aldermen had no power to intervene where the petitioners sought to have their proposal acted upon at a general election. The town clerk was under the duty of incorporating the question in the warning for the general election because the proposed change in the charter was initiated by a petition filed with the town clerk and because the petition requested the submission of the question to the electorate at the general election.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to overrule the demurrer and for further proceedings.
