Bridgeport Hydraulic Co. v. Pearson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


139 Conn. 186; 91 A.2d 778; 1952 Conn. LEXIS 177


June 10, 1952, Argued  
July 29, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendant from further prosecuting an action against the plaintiff, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County, where a temporary injunction was granted, Shea, J., a motion to dissolve was denied, Quinlan, J., and the issues were tried to the court, Bordon, J.; judgment for the plaintiff and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In eminent domain proceedings, defendant property owner appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) in favor of plaintiff water company, which denied the property owner's motion to dissolve a temporary injunction granted to the water company and denied the property owner's motion for reargument. The property owner contended that it was error to conclude that the water company was entitled to relief.


OVERVIEW: The water company instituted proceedings to condemn a property containing a forge, and a property containing a schoolhouse. The property owner instituted actions to stop the condemnations or became a party defendant in actions where the water company sought to condemn the lands. She later reinstituted proceedings as to the two properties. The court held that there was no error. The trial court's finding that the litigation was the result of malice had to be stricken because there was nothing in her conduct which would justify an inference of the existence of malice. Although the remedies sought as to the school house property were somewhat different, the cause of action of wrongful ejectment was the same. In addition it was of no consequence whether she was bound by the prior adjudication because it was sufficient that she had an interest in the subject matter and participated in the litigation. Although the order striking the forge property case from the docket was not a judgment on the merits, her acceptance of the monetary judgment in an action over the same set of facts was conclusive.


OUTCOME: In the eminent domain action, the court held that there was no error in the judgment for the water company or in the denial of the property owners' motions for reargument and to dissolve the temporary injunction.

 

897 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Higgins v. Civil Service Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


139 Conn. 102; 90 A.2d 862; 1952 Conn. LEXIS 166


May 13, 1952, Argued  
July 8, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action claiming a writ of mandamus requiring the defendant commission and defendant personnel director to add points to the final earned rating of the plaintiffs on an examination for promotion in the police department, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and reserved by the court, Cullinan, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff veteran police officers filed suit in the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), seeking a writ of mandamus requiring defendant civil service commission and defendant personnel director to add points to their final earned ratings on an examination for promotion in the police department. The trial court reserved the action for the advice of the court.


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed a special act requiring the commission to add five points to the earned rating received by an honorably discharged war veteran taking an examination with the city and later amended the act to add similar points on promotional examinations. After the commission added points to the veteran officers' ratings on a promotional examination, defendant nonveteran officers challenged the constitutionality of the amendment. The court held that the amendment was valid because: (1) the legislature could reasonably have believed that extending preferential treatment to veterans taking civil service examinations served the genuine public purpose of encouraging patriotism; and (2) there was a natural and substantial difference between veterans and other citizens, and the difference was logically related to the purpose of the amendment, which was to encourage veterans to bring the qualities developed by military service to the service of the city. The court further held that the commission improperly applied the additional points only to the veteran officers' ratings on the written part of the examination, rather than to their final grades on the entire examination.


OUTCOME: The court held that the amendment was constitutional and that the "earned rating" to which the additional points were to be applied was the final rating attained by candidates on all subjects of examination.

 

898 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Northeastern Gas Transmission Co. v. Benedict


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


139 Conn. 36; 89 A.2d 379; 1952 Conn. LEXIS 155; 1 Oil & Gas Rep. 1094


May 6, 1952, Argued  
May 22, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by the defendants that an order terminating a stay of execution on appeal made by a judge of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Murphy, J.) be reviewed and set aside.



DISPOSITION: Motion that order be set aside denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners filed a motion to set aside an order of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which terminated a stay of execution on appeal in their appeal of a judgment obtained by plaintiff gas company for the condemnation of rights of way for a natural gas pipeline.


OVERVIEW: The gas company obtained a judgment in condemnation proceedings for condemnation of rights of way for a natural gas pipeline. The property owners appealed that judgment and execution of the order for immediate possession was automatically stayed. The gas company filed a motion for termination of the stay, which the trial court granted. The property owners filed a motion to set aside the order terminating the stay. The court denied the motion, concluding that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in coming to the opinion that the due administration of justice required a termination of the stay of execution. The property owners' claim that the trial court's conclusion that public interest would be prejudiced by further delay was not warranted. Whether the claim was valid was a question which would have to be determined upon the appeal from the order for immediate possession. That the claim was made was not of controlling moment in the determination of the motion. The fact that practical difficulties could arise to obstruct the execution of a public work did not necessarily postpone all proceedings until those obstacles were overcome.


OUTCOME: The court denied the property owners' motion to set aside the trial court's order terminating the stay of execution of a judgment in favor of the gas company. The gas company had obtained a judgment for condemnation of rights of way for a natural gas pipeline.

 

899 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Ruppert v. Liquor Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


138 Conn. 669; 88 A.2d 388; 1952 Conn. LEXIS 141


March 5, 1952, Argued  
April 22, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the denial of a renewal application for an out-of-state shipper's permit, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Dwyer, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff importers challenged a decision from the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which dismissed the importers' appeal from defendant Liquor Control Commission's decision to deny their permit to ship beer.


OVERVIEW: The importers filed an application with the Commission, which sought the renewal of an out-of-state beer permit. Under the terms of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4266, a backer was required. The Commission objected to the backer chosen because it owned a controlling interest in a corporation that already backed other permits. The importers' appeal was dismissed by the trial court. The importers contended that § 4266 violated the Fourteenth Amendment, as applied to out-of-state permit applications. In affirming the trial court's decision, the court determined that § 4266 was a constitutional exercise of legislative power. The states were given broad police power to regulate alcoholic beverages under the Twenty-First Amendment. As such, they were permitted to adopt reasonably appropriate measures. A classification recognized by the Twenty-First Amendment was not forbidden by the Fourteenth Amendment. Moreover, there was no illegal discrimination were there was a natural and substantial difference, germane to the purpose of legislation, between those in one distinct class who were dealt with in one way and those in a separate class who were dealt with in another fashion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the importers' appeal from the denial of their application for a permit to ship beer.

 

900 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Northeastern Gas Transmission Co. v. Collins


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


138 Conn. 582; 87 A.2d 139; 1952 Conn. LEXIS 127; 1 Oil & Gas Rep. 278


February 7, 1952, Argued  
March 6, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for an order permitting the plaintiff to enter upon the defendants' land to make a survey of easements and rights of way necessary for the construction and operation of its pipe line, and for the appointment of a committee to assess damages, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Quinlan, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners challenged the constitutionality of An Act concerning Natural Gas Pipe Line Companies (Act), Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 1072b-1078b (Cum. Sup. 1951), after plaintiff corporation petitioned for an order permitting it to enter upon the land to make a survey of easements and rights of way necessary for the construction and operation of its pipeline.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was engaged in the business of supplying natural gas by pipeline. It held a certificate of public convenience and necessity issued by the Federal Power Commission pursuant to the provisions of the Natural Gas Act of 1938. The court found that the Act was not unconstitutional because ample provision was made to insure the payment of just compensation for the taking, and due process, though not questioned by the landowner, was thoroughly provided for. The court construed the Act to authorize by implication the taking of a temporary interest in land which was reasonably necessary to carry out the purposes for which the taking of permanent easements was authorized. The property which the corporation was privileged to take was restricted to that which reasonably served the public use; more than that would have, in effect, been a taking for a private use and, hence, illegal as an abuse of power.


OUTCOME: In an eminent domain case, the court found for the corporation and against the landowners in holding that the Act, which allowed for the taking of land for building of a pipeline, was constitutional.

 

901 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Cotter v. Leipner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


138 Conn. 153; 83 A.2d 169; 1951 Conn. LEXIS 198


July 21, 1951, Argued  
July 30, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action of quo warranto to determine whether the plaintiffs or the defendants are entitled to hold office as judges of the City Court of Bridgeport, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Molloy, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, new judges, brought a quo warranto action to the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) to determine whether they or defendants, old judges, were entitled to hold office as judges of the city court. The superior court reserved the case for the advice of the court.


OVERVIEW: The question reserved was whether defendants or plaintiffs had been the de jure judges of the city court since July 1, 1951. The question turned upon whether Conn. Const. amend. XX and the statutes adopted thereunder operated to fix the terms of office of city court judges or whether they had been superseded by Conn. Const. amend. XLVII. The term of office, a vacancy in which defendants were appointed to fill, was for two years from July 1, 1949. Conn. Const. amend. XX was in effect at the time of their appointment and remained in effect until Conn. Const. amend. XLVII received the requisite implementation by act of the General Assembly. Conn. Const. amend. XX imposed a constitutional restraint upon any extension of the term of office of a municipal court judge beyond the period of two years. No legislative or executive act was able to override that restraint. Accordingly, the court concluded that defendants' terms of office expired on June 30, 1951. On July 1, 1951, there were vacancies in the terms of the offices which it was incumbent upon the governor to fill pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 92. He had filled those vacancies by the appointment of plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court advised the superior court that plaintiffs held the offices of city court judges.

Legat v. Adorno

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought a declaratory judgment in regard to expenditures by defendant state treasurer pursuant to a bond issue.


OVERVIEW: A bond issued was released, and the requisite regulations as to expenditures were voted into place. It was decided that an expenditure would be made for improvements to a hospital that met the definitions of a hospital and of a not-for-profit organization. Based on the definitions set forth in § 3 of the Institutional Building Bonds Act (Act) the hospital also qualified as being partially maintained by the state. The court determined that the contract for improvements was valid. The court found that the Act was not violative of Conn. Const. art I, § 1because the hospital was partially maintained by the state, and there was no violation of the prohibition of public funds being used to support private enterprise. The court ruled in favor of the treasurer.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the expenditure was appropriate and ruled in favor of the action taken by the state treasurer.

 

903 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Gionfriddo v. Windsor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


137 Conn. 701; 81 A.2d 266; 1951 Conn. LEXIS 175


April 4, 1951, Argued  
May 22, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining whether an amendment to the building zone regulations passed by the zoning commission of the defendant town forbidding the sale or display of motor vehicles in any open lot was a violation of the plaintiffs' constitutional rights, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Comley, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut) reserved questions to the court regarding an action brought by plaintiffs, an owner and a lessee, for a declaratory judgment determining whether an amendment to the building zone regulations passed by defendant zoning commission of defendant town forbidding the sale or display of motor vehicles in any open lot was a violation of plaintiffs' constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The superior court requested the court to decide if plaintiffs were proper parties and whether an amendment to Windsor, Conn., Building Zone Regs. § 6 was unconstitutional. The court found that plaintiffs were proper parties and that the amendment, which did not allow a permit to be issued for the sale or display of new or used motor vehicles in any open lot or portion thereof, or for the business of a motor vehicle junk yard, in any zone, was unconstitutional. The lessee had applied for and was granted permission to erect a gasoline station and store. His application for permission to convert and use the filling station for the sale and repair of motor vehicles was granted subject to the condition of the amendment to § 6. The court found that plaintiffs were proper parties because the lessee sought a permit under the ordinance and the owner was subject to a fine and possible imprisonment. The amendment to § 6 was unconstitutional because it was an unwarranted and arbitrary interference with the constitutional rights to carry on a lawful business.


OUTCOME: The court determined that plaintiffs were proper parties and that the amendment to the regulation in question was unconstitutional and void.

 

904 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Hartford-Connecticut Trust Co. v. O'Connor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


137 Conn. 267; 76 A.2d 9; 1950 Conn. LEXIS 216


April 4, 1950, Argued  
July 25, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the assessment of a penalty tax on the estate of the plaintiffs' decedent, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Daly, J., for the advice of this court.

The plaintiffs filed a motion for reargument which was denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executors of decedent's estate sought review of the decision of defendant tax commissioner which assessed a penalty tax on the estate.


OVERVIEW: Three sisters entered into a contract to sell their property to an insurance company. The sisters were entitled to remain in the property until their death. The deed was escrowed with a bank with directions to deliver the deed on the payment of the balance of the purchase price on the death of the surviving sister. The sisters were required to pay all property taxes. The executors of the will of the last surviving sister filed an inventory and appraisal with the probate court. The tax commissioner assessed a penalty tax on the estate pursuant to the contract on the property. The penalty was based on the fact that the sister failed to pay the tax during the year preceding her death. The executors sought review of the legality of the tax. The trial court certified certain questions to the court. The court found that the contract was a credit or chose in action that was liable to taxation under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§1745, 2083. Thus, the court found that the assessment was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the assessment and denied the executors' motion for a rehearing.

 

905 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Hagerty v. Administrator, Unemployment Compensation Act


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


137 Conn. 129; 75 A.2d 406; 1950 Conn. LEXIS 194; 20 A.L.R.2d 960


May 2, 1950, Argued  
July 18, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from a decision of the unemployment commissioner for the third district that the plaintiffs are ineligible to receive unemployment compensation, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and tried to the court, Wynne, J.; judgment dismissing the appeals, from which the named plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut), which upheld a decision of an unemployment commissioner denying the employee's application for renewal of unemployment benefits. That decision was based on a determination that the employee had not received sufficient wages during the preceding base period to qualify as a beneficiary under the Connecticut Unemployment Compensation Act.


OVERVIEW: The employee would have qualified for renewal benefits if the Act had not been amended to require under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1389i (Supp. 1947) that the wage amount an unemployed person had to receive during his base period must have been paid in at least two different quarters of that period. Thus, the employee argued that he had a vested property right in benefits under the Act as it existed at the time of his discharge which could not constitutionally be affected by subsequent legislative action. On appeal, the court disagreed and affirmed. A right was not vested unless it became a legal or equitable title to the present or future enjoyment of property. A savings clause in the original Act provided that the Connecticut General Assembly reserved the right to amend any part of the Act and that no vested private right prevented such an amendment. As a result, the employee's right to benefits at the time of his discharge was subject to the contingency of an amendment. As such, his right was conditional, and the reservation of power to amend justified as constitutional the changes made to benefit eligibility. Therefore, the employee's renewal application was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Strain v. Zoning Board of Appeals


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


137 Conn. 36; 74 A.2d 462; 1950 Conn. LEXIS 180


April 4, 1950, Argued  
June 20, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant board in denying the plaintiffs' application for authorization to erect a garage on their property, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, McNiff, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal and ordering the defendant board to vacate its order, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Greenwich, Connecticut sought review of a judgment by the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which sustained an appeal of the Board's action of denying plaintiff landowners' application for authorization to erect a garage on their property.


OVERVIEW: The owners had been conducting for some time a gasoline filling station, automobile repair business, and general store. Their property was located in what was described under the building zone regulations of the Town as a local business zone. The Board denied the application upon the ground that the granting of it would aggravate an unsightly and noisy condition and that the denial of it would be in accord with the public interest and the appropriate development of the neighborhood and in harmony with the purpose and intent of the zoning regulations. The trial court on appeal held that the zoning ordinances under which the Board purported to act were unconstitutional and void because they did not contain any rule or standard to guide or restrain the discretion of the Board, nor any comprehensive plan for uniformity, and, therefore, were illegal and an improper delegations of legislative power. The owners had utilized the regulations previously when they obtained permission to open their business. Therefore, the court concluded that the ordinances could not later be challenged on the issue of their constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

907 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Ruttenberg v. Dine


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


137 Conn. 17; 74 A.2d 211; 1950 Conn. LEXIS 175


April 5, 1950, Argued  
June 6, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of error from a judgment for the defendant in error in a summary process action brought to the City Court of New Haven, where the court, Henchel, J., denied the motion of the plaintiff in error for a jury trial and the issues were tried to the court, Damiani, J. 



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error tenant sought review of the judgment of the City Court of New Haven (Connecticut) in favor of defendant in error landlord, in the landlord's summary process action against the tenant to recover possession of the leased premises.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the tenant argued that the trial court erred in denying her motion for a jury trial. In particular, the tenant claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 664a (1949 Cum. Supp.), which repealed Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8246, providing for a right in either a lessor or a lessee in moving for a jury trial, was unconstitutional. The court rejected the tenant's argument. In so ruling, the court noted that the issue of the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 664a (1949 Cum. Supp.) was not properly presented by the record. The court explained that if the Connecticut Legislature could have deprived litigants of a jury trial in a summary process, then the trial court's denial of the tenant's motion for a jury would not have presented an appellate issue. The court further observed that, on the other hand, if the right was guaranteed by the Connecticut Constitution, then the action of the Connecticut Legislature repealing the statute would have been void and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8276 (repealed) would have been controlling. Under § 8276, a lessor or a lessee was required to request by motion a jury trial on or before the return day. The tenant, however, failed to make such a request.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

908 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Cusano v. Dunn


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


137 Conn. 20; 74 A.2d 477; 1950 Conn. LEXIS 176


April 5, 1950, Argued  
June 6, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the denial by the liquor control commission of the plaintiff's application for a package store liquor permit, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, Pickett, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal and sustaining the action of the commission, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff store owner's son challenged a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County (Connecticut), which affirmed the decision of defendant Liquor Control Commission. The Commission denied the son's application for a package store liquor permit.


OVERVIEW: A third party had been operating a package store as a tenant of the father. The son wanted to obtain the permit and the third party was removed from the business by a judgment in summary process. The third party obtained a permit at a different location. The son claimed that since the father's premises had been used as a legal liquor outlet for more than 12 years, and since this use was not violative of the zoning ordinance, it constituted an existing "permit premise," and the action in granting the third party's permit for his new location, when it knew that the son was going to apply for a permit for the old, was arbitrary and unreasonable. Only one of the two permits could have been awarded unless the number of outlets in the neighborhood was to be increased. The court found that if the Commission had reasonable cause to believe that granting a new permit would prove detrimental to the public interest, it was its duty under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4263(3) to refuse to do so. Permits to sell liquor in given vicinity were not necessarily mutually exclusive either in fact or law. Accordingly, the court found that the son had no vested interest in a liquor permit issued to his tenant.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the decision of the Commission or the judgment of the trial court.

 

909 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Mills v. Gaynor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


136 Conn. 632; 73 A.2d 823; 1950 Conn. LEXIS 164


February 10, 1950, Argued  
May 16, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition alleging that the plaintiff was elected registrar of voters in Norwalk and seeking a certificate that he is entitled to hold that office, brought to Hon. James E. Murphy, a judge of the Superior Court, in Fairfield County, where the defendants filed cross petitions and the cause was reserved for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff republican party member (republican) filed a petition in the Superior Court of Fairfield County (Connecticut), alleging that he was elected registrar of voters in Norwalk and sought a certificate that he was entitled to hold the office. Defendants, democratic party member (democrat) and socialist party member (socialist), filed answers and cross petitions, and the cause was reserved for the advice of the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: Two registrars of voters were elected every two years at the city's general election, with one from each of the two major political parties who had the largest and next to the largest number of votes at the previous election. The democrat and the republican were nominated pursuant to the charter. The socialist filed a rule to show cause with the superior court as to why his name was not on the voting machines, and it was agreed that it would be added. The republican lost the election and filed a petition requesting a certificate entitling him to hold and exercise the duties and powers of the office. The democrat and the socialist filed answers and cross petitions. By agreement, the case was reserved for the advice of the court as to whether the charter provisions were constitutional and who the registrars were. The court held that the provisions were not unreasonable and were constitutional because the registrars were not party officials, and that the legislature might have believed that a multiplicity of such officials would tend toward confusion and inefficiency. The court concluded that the republican and the democrat were the registrars.


OUTCOME: The court advised that the statute in question was constitutional and that the republican and the democrat were elected the registrars of voters.

 

910 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Du Pont v. Liquor Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


136 Conn. 286; 71 A.2d 84; 1949 Conn. LEXIS 237


November 8, 1949, Argued  
December 14, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the action of the defendant commission in denying the application of the plaintiffs for a package store permit, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County and tried to the court, FitzGerald, J., judgment sustaining the appeal and directing the commission to issue the permit, from which the defendant town of Stratford appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner filed an application for a package store permit, which defendant commission denied. The owner appealed to the Court of Common Pleas in Fairfield County (Conn.). Defendant town joined the action as a party defendant. The trial court sustained the appeal and directed the commission to issue the permit. Defendant town appealed.


OVERVIEW: Stratford was not a "no-permit" town. The premises were located in a business zone. Issuance of the permit was prohibited by no statute, ordinance, or regulation aside from Stratford, Conn., Zoning Ordinance §§ 7 K and 20 J. The owners were unable to obtain from other owners the number of signatures approving their use of the premises as a package store, which §§ 7 K and 20 J required. The ground of the commission's refusal to grant the application was unsuitability of place because the premises did not comply with the requirements of the zoning regulations. The court held that the consent requirement was unconstitutional. If the existence of a law depended upon the vote or act of the people, it was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power; but if the law was complete in and of itself, the fact that it provided for the removal or modification of its prohibition by the act of those most affected thereby did not make it a delegation of legislative power. An absolute prohibition under an ordinance was essential to render the consent provision valid as providing for waiver of an existing restriction. The ordinance could not be construed as containing such a prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

911 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Parlato v. McCarthy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


136 Conn. 126; 69 A.2d 648; 1949 Conn. LEXIS 210


June 8, 1949, Argued  
October 25, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decree of the Probate Court for the district of Derby prorating the federal estate tax, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County where a demurrer of the named defendant and the defendant Griffin Hospital to the reasons of appeal was sustained, O'Sullivan, J., and, the plaintiff failing to plead further, judgment was rendered, Murphy, J., dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

The appellees filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff distributee sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of New Haven County (Connecticut) that sustained the demurrer of defendants, executor and trust beneficiary, and dismissed the distributee's appeal from the probate court that had decreed that the distributee was required to pay a prorated estate tax under 1949 Conn. Gen. Stats. § 2076.


OVERVIEW: The distributee claimed that the retroactive provision of 1949 Conn. Gen. Stats. § 2081, when read in connection with the remainder of the statute, as applied to the federal estate tax upon the transfer of property of a testator who died before passage of the act, was unconstitutional, because it impaired the distributee's vested right to the legacy under the testator's will and violated the due process. The court set aside the judgment of the lower court and remanded to the lower court to proceed consistent with the court's opinion, holding that 1949 Conn. Gen. Stats. § 2076 was not a taxing statute, because it only allocated the federal taxes that were to be charged to the estate, and the retroactive application violated due process by impairing the distributee's right to the legacy from the estate, which was vested when the testator died. The court held that § 2076 was unconstitutional, as applied through 1949 Conn. Gen. Stats. § 2081.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the lower court's judgment that had dismissed the distributee's appeal from the probate court that had required the distributee to pay a prorated amount of the estate tax and remanded to the lower court to proceed consistent with the court's opinion after determining that the estate tax proration statute was unconstitutional.

 

912 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Carroll v. Socony-Vacuum Oil Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


136 Conn. 49; 68 A.2d 299; 1949 Conn. LEXIS 202


March 8, 1949, Argued  
August 23, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover an amount retained by the defendant from the tax due from it for the sale of gasoline, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and reserved by the court, Murphy, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After plaintiff state treasurer filed a complaint against defendant oil company to recover tax due from the sale of gasoline, and while the case was pending on demurrer, the case came before the court on reservation.


OVERVIEW: After an oil company denied liability in the state's action to recover taxes from the sale of gasoline, the general assembly enacted Conn. Gen. Stat. § 400i (Supp. 1947). The oil company amended its answer to include the special defense that § 400i authorized it to retain one percent of the tax on all gasoline. The state demurred, and the case was reserved to the court. The court advised the trial court that the demurrer should be overruled. The first ground of demurrer, namely, that the general assembly improperly gave money belonging to the state to the distributors and gave them exclusive privileges, was unsound. The distributors, in collecting the tax, were acting as agents for the state; allowing them to retain a reasonable sum for their services was proper. The general assembly could also grant compensation retrospectively for equitable reasons. The general assembly could properly consider that it was unfair to the distributors, after state officials and the distributors had assumed for ten years that the distributors had the statutory right to retain the one percent, to require them to pay back the money to the state. The statute on its face was not discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The court, having taken the case under reservation, advised the trial court that the state's demurrer to the oil company's special statutory defense should be overruled on both grounds.

 

913 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Old Colony Gardens, Inc. v. Cheney


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


136 Conn. 18; 68 A.2d 132; 1949 Conn. LEXIS 197


June 15, 1949, Argued  
August 9, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of error from a judgment for the defendant in error in a summary process action before the City Court of Stamford, Reback, J. 



DISPOSITION: Error and new trial ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessor appealed from a judgment of the City Court of Stamford (Connecticut) that dismissed its complaint for a summary process action to reclaim possession of an apartment building which it intended to withdraw from the rental market.


OVERVIEW: The lessor filed a summary process action against defendant lessee to regain possession of an apartment building that it intended to withdraw from the rental market. The trial court dismissed the action on the ground that under 1949 Conn. Pub. Acts no. 5 summary process could not be used to recover possession of any apartment in a building. The lessor appealed, and the court set the trial court's judgment aside and ordered a new trial. The trial court erred when it interpreted the enactment as barring the filing of the lessor's action. The enactment applied only to the bringing of actions, not to maintaining them, and the present action was filed before the enactment was made.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment and ordered a new trial.

 

914 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Rundbaken v. Watrous


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


135 Conn. 638; 68 A.2d 289; 1949 Conn. LEXIS 184


July 25, 1949, Argued  
August 1, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Actions of quo warranto to determine the validity of appointments by the governor of judges to fill claimed vacancies in the minor courts, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford and New Haven Counties and reserved by the court, Molloy, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reserved determination of cases originally heard in the Superior Court in Hartford and New Haven Counties (Connecticut), which sought resolution of quo warranto actions to determine whether plaintiff successor judges or defendant appointed judges had the right to remain in office.


OVERVIEW: The successor judges were appointed by the General Assembly to hold office for two years. The appointed judges were appointed by the governor to replace the successor judges. The court held that the appointed judges had the right to hold the offices. The court held that Conn. Const. amend. XX established a constitutional limitation on the term of appointed judges for a period of two years. One appointed to fill a vacancy held office only until the expiration of the term established for the person whose place he took. Because the successor judges were appointed for a period of two years, their terms of office expired after two years. Furthermore, the amendments extending prior appointments were passed after the successor judges were appointed and statutes affecting substantial changes in the law were not to be construed to have retroactive effect unless the intent was clear. The governor's appointment of the appointed judges was valid because the senate had adjourned sine die, giving the governor the power to make vacancy appointments.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the appointed judges were properly appointed by the governor and that the successor judges did not have the right to continue in office.

 

915 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Zoning Com. of Bridgeport


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


135 Conn. 405; 65 A.2d 577; 1949 Conn. LEXIS 144; 9 A.L.R.2d 873


January 7, 1949, Argued  
March 15, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of certain zoning regulations as applied to the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, O'Sullivan, J.; judgment for the defendant and appeal by the plaintiffs.

The plaintiffs filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff restaurant owners sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut) entered in favor of defendant Zoning Commission of the City of Bridgeport, Connecticut. The owners had filed an action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of certain zoning regulations as applied to them.


OVERVIEW: The owners desired to change their liquor permit so that they could dispense alcoholic liquor without limitation as to kind under a full or all-alcoholic restaurant permit. The change was prohibited because it was found to have been against the zoning regulations of the City of Bridgeport, Connecticut. Bridgeport, Conn., Zoning Regulations § 6(B)(2) and (3) were at issue. Section 6(B)(2) had been previously held valid in another case. Finding no error in the trial court's judgment, the court found that the power of the Commission as a subdivision of the State was to regulate and restrict the business of the sale of liquor. Its power was far broader than a power to regulate or restrict ordinary lawful business. The use of property for the sale of liquor was deemed by the legislative authority to have a far more harmful effect upon the health and welfare of the community than an ordinary business. The only places for the sale of liquor which would have been a conforming use would have been those which were so situated that there was not another place for the sale of liquor within the 1500-foot radius.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

State ex rel. La Voie v. Building Com. of Trumbull


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


135 Conn. 415; 65 A.2d 165; 1948 Conn. LEXIS 218


October 14, 1948, Argued  
December 22, 1948, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus to compel the defendant to issue a building permit, brought to the Superior Court in Fairfield County and tried to the court, Quinlan, J.; judgment for the defendant and appeal by the plaintiff.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was granted.



DISPOSITION: Error in part and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield County (Connecticut), which entered judgment in favor of defendant building commission in the landowner's suit in mandamus to compel the commission to issue a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The commission denied the landowner's building applications on the ground that the proposed plan would have violated requirements of the zoning regulations as to the size of lots and as to the dimensions of rear and side yards. The landowner brought an action to secure an order to compel the building commission to issue to him certain permits for the erection of houses upon lots he owned. The court held that the landowner was entitled to a permit for the construction of the house upon the lot the dimensions of which were unchanged from those on the original layout, but found that the building commission did not exceed its powers in denying the applications for permits as regards the other lots on the ground that the proposed use of them would have violated the zoning regulations.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was error in part of the lower court's decision, set the judgment aside and remanded the case with direction to enter judgment finding that the landowner was entitled to a permit for the construction of a house upon the lot, the dimensions of which were unchanged from those on the original layout.

 

917 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Walsh v. Jenks


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


135 Conn. 210; 62 A.2d 773; 1948 Conn. LEXIS 206


October 15, 1948, Argued  
November 23, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining whether the defendant has the right to grant tax exemptions to veterans not domiciled in this state at the time of induction, and other questions, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County at Waterbury and reserved by the court, Inglis, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in New Haven County at Waterbury (Connecticut) brought questions in plaintiff Connecticut Tax Commissioner's suit for a declaratory judgment to determine whether defendant Assessor of the City of Waterbury had the right to grant tax exemptions to veterans not domiciled in Connecticut at the time of induction.


OVERVIEW: State tax statutes granted limited exemptions from the Connecticut property tax to those in the armed services, those who had served, or their dependents. The Commissioner claimed that the statutes had to be interpreted as restricted to those who were serving or had served as a portion of a quota for Connecticut. Answering the first question, the court said that exemptions from the Connecticut property tax for those who were not state residents at the time of their enlistment or induction and who did not serve as a part of the Connecticut quota were within the meaning of statutes and were valid. It was not the legislative intent in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 158f (Supp. 1941) to restrict the grant to persons who served as a part of the Connecticut quota. Nothing in the statute suggested such a limitation, and the court could not read such a provision into it. The terms of the statute permitted no severance, which would have to be made between two groups that fell within the broad language of the law. If taxes could be laid to show gratitude for meritorious military service, veterans could properly be exempted from the payment of a portion of the taxes levied on the people of a state.


OUTCOME: The court answered the question.

 

918 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Spector Motor Service, Inc. v. Walsh


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


135 Conn. 37; 61 A.2d 89; 1948 Conn. LEXIS 184


May 6, 1948, Argued  
July 21, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment as to whether or not the assessments made against the plaintiff under the Corporation Business Tax Act of 1935 were illegal and void, brought to the Superior Court in Hartford County and tried by the court, Comley, J.; judgment determining the issues and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error in part and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tax commissioner appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in Hartford County (Connecticut), which held that plaintiff corporation was within the terms of the Corporation Business Tax Act of 1935 (Act), Cum. Supp. 1935, Chap. 66b, § 416c et seq., that the Act did not as applied violate the state constitution, but that the Act as applied to the corporation was unconstitutional under the U.S. Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was a foreign corporation engaged in the transportation of freight in interstate commerce. The commissioner assessed a certain tax against it under the Act, which imposed a tax upon the franchise or privilege of a corporation to do business within the state. The tax was to be upon a base that reasonably represented the proportion of the trade or business carried on within the state. The corporation brought an action seeking a declaratory judgment as to whether assessments made against it were illegal and void. The court found that the corporation was doing business within the state, though that business was interstate in character. Its business was within the purview of the Act. The corporation argued that the Act was unconstitutional because it did not impose a tax upon partnerships or individuals engaged in the same business. The court held that the tax was upon the privilege which existed in conducting business with the advantages which inhered in the corporate capacity of those taxed. Those advantages created a distinct privilege. The classification was not unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious and was not, therefore, violative of the state unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court erred in deciding the issue of whether the Act was in violation of the U.S. Constitution but that its conclusions that the Act did not violate the state constitution and that the assessments were not illegal were correct. It directed the trial court to enter judgment as on file except that the provisions that the Act was violative of the U.S. Constitution was to be eliminated.

Regional High Sch. Dist. No. 3 v. Town of Newtown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


134 Conn. 613; 59 A.2d 527; 1948 Conn. LEXIS 161


April 9, 1948, Argued  
May 19, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment concerning the legal existence, rights, powers and duties of the plaintiff Regional High School District, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven County and reserved by the court, O'Sullivan, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court's advice was sought in an action for declaratory judgment brought in, and reserved by, the Superior Court in New Haven County (Connecticut) concerning the legal existence, rights, powers, and duties of plaintiff regional high school district and defendant towns.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 196h, three adjacent towns formed a regional high school with the approval of the state board of education and another town joined their regional district shortly thereafter. The regional school district, acting through its board, incurred substantial indebtedness in undertaking to establish the high school and later two towns sought to withdraw from the district. The district, towns, and their creditors sought declarations from the court regarding the legal validity, powers, and obligations of the regional school district. The court concluded that pursuant to the state's plenary power to establish school districts and as recognized by a special act of the state general assembly, the regional school district, had a legal existence as a quasi-municipal corporation established by the state to carry out its governmental purposes. The court reasoned that as such, none of the towns had the power to withdraw or dissolve the school district without legislative authority. The court also advised that the creditors' claims were not suitable for determination in the declaratory judgment action, and should be pursued as contract actions.


OUTCOME: The court gave a declaration answering specific questions concerning the legal existence, powers, and obligations of the regional school district.

Downer v. Liquor Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Errors of Connecticut


134 Conn. 555; 59 A.2d 290; 1948 Conn. LEXIS 151


March 4, 1948, Argued  
April 22, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the denial by the defendant of a wholesaler beer permit, brought to the Court of Common Pleas in Hartford County and tried to the court, FitzGerald, J.; judgment for the defendant dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought review of an order from the Hartford County Court of Common Pleas (Connecticut), which entered judgment in favor of defendant liquor control commission (commission), in the applicant's appeal of the commission's denial of a wholesaler beer permit.


OVERVIEW: The applicant filed an application for a wholesaler permit which showed that the proposed backer was a New York corporation which was also a backer on a Connecticut out-of-state shipper's permit for beer only. The commission denied the application because the permit already held by the backer was in a different class from the one for which the application was made. The trial court sustained the commission's decision. On appeal, the court determined that the Liquor Control Act did not expressly or by implication exclude that application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 968e (Sup. 1939), which prohibited the backer or permittee of one class of permit from being the backer or permittee of another class, to an out-of-state shipper's permit. The court found that it was not permitted to read an exception into that section to avoid consequences so absurd or unreasonable that the legislature must have been presumed not to have intended them and that the denial of the permit in question was mandatory under the statute. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court.

In re Shyliesh H.


(AC 19433)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


56 Conn. App. 167; 743 A.2d 165; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 499

December 21, 1999, Officially Released

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed from the judgment of the Child Protection Session at Middletown (Connecticut) terminating his parental rights for failure to show sufficient rehabilitation within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112 (c) (3) (B).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner Commissioner of Children and Families obtained an ex parte order for custody of respondents' minor child. The trial court set forth specific steps for respondents to take to facilitate the minor child's return. State v. Butler


(AC 17753)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


55 Conn. App. 502; 739 A.2d 732; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 423


June 8, 1999, Argued  
November 2, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder as an accessory and conspiracy to commit murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before McMahon, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment of conviction of murder as an accessory and conspiracy to commit murder entered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: The defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction of murder as an accessory and conspiracy to commit murder. The defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motions for a mistrial that were based on the existence of egregious prosecutorial misconduct. The court held that the prosecutor's comment was improper where the state neither claimed, nor did the record disclose, any legitimate justification for informing the jury of the outcomes of the codefendants' trials. After careful examination of the specific circumstances of the instant case and despite the trial court's use of a curative instruction, the court held, on the basis of the severity of the misconduct, its centrality to the critical issues in the case, and the weakness of the state's case, that the prosecutor's misconduct deprived the defendant of his due process right to a fair trial. Conviction was reversed.


OUTCOME: Conviction reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial; the prosecutor's misconduct deprived the defendant of his due process right to a fair trial.

State v. Bell


(AC 17999)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


55 Conn. App. 475; 739 A.2d 714; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 406


June 8, 1999, Argued  
October 26, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crime of harassment in the second degree and information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crime of criminal trespass in the first degree and information, in the third case, charging the defendant with the crime of falsely reporting an incident, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, geographical area number eleven, where the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the defendant was tried to the court, Quinn, J.; judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the guilty judgments of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Windham (Connecticut) for harassment in the second degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(3); criminal trespass in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-107; and falsely reporting an incident, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-180.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made criticizing and threatening telephone calls to various employees of a family preservation program in which his children were enrolled. A court order enjoined defendant from entering his ex-lover's apartment building, nevertheless defendant stood near the building. Defendant called the police to report that his ex-lover's failure to give their children an antibiotic was a medical emergency. The court held that: (1) defendant's telephone calls were not protected speech under the U.S. Const. amend. I; (2) the harassment statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant's conduct; (3) evidence was sufficient to prove that defendant intended to harass or annoy the employees of the program; (4) because the court's order only prevented defendant from entering the building, but not from being on the property, defendant did not violate it and could not have criminally trespassed; and (5) evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of falsely reporting an incident.


OUTCOME: Criminal trespass conviction reversed because court order only prevented defendant from entering building, but not being on property. Remaining convictions affirmed because defendant's telephone calls were not constitutionally protected speech and there was sufficient evidence for the harassment and falsely reporting an incident convictions.

OVERVIEW: Petitioner prisoner was convicted of kidnapping, sexual assault, robbery, assault, and larceny and his petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as to the determination of personal jurisdiction and award for alimony, but reversed the judgment as to the order requiring defendant to obtain life insurance. Further, the court remanded the case to determine the reasonableness of the attorney's fees.

State v. Story


(AC 17763)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


53 Conn. App. 733; 732 A.2d 785; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 247


December 14, 1998, Argued  
June 15, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell and possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Maloney, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the state issued a nolle as to the charge of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, and the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charge of possession of narcotics with intent to sell; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him, after a conditional plea of nolo contendere pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a, of possession of narcotics with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a). Defendant alleged the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding. When defendant was given the citation, he was asked to step out of his vehicle. Defendant complied and was then asked for permission to search the vehicle. Defendant consented and cocaine was found in a bag in the trunk. Defendant then volunteered there were more drugs in the console between the seats. Defendant was arrested and the police searched the vehicle, finding the other drugs. Defendant entered a conditional nolo contendere plea under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a to possession of narcotics with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a). Defendant appealed alleging the trial court improperly concluded that his detention by police following a traffic stop was not unjustifiably prolonged and that he had voluntarily consented to a search of his vehicle. The court affirmed, finding that defendant was free to leave at the time he was asked to exit his vehicle. The court held that whether a restraint of freedom of movement existed was a factual determination not to be overturned unless clearly erroneous. The court found defendant's will was not overborne and his consent was not an unconstrained choice.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed on the basis that the trial court's finding that defendant voluntarily consented to a search of his vehicle was not clearly erroneous. There was no evidence the police employed coercive or deceptive procedure to obtain defendant's consent nor that defendant did not feel free to leave after he was given a traffic citation.

State v. Vasquez


(AC 17951)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


53 Conn. App. 661; 733 A.2d 856; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 234


March 23, 1999, Argued  
June 8, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics, sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and sale of narcotics within 1500 of a school, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of narcotics, sale of narcotics as a lesser included offense and sale of narcotics within 1500 of a school, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for possession of narcotics in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a), for the sale of narcotics in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a), and for the sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278a(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for the possession of narcotics, the sale of narcotics, and the sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that the issue of identification was a question of fact for the jury which had sufficient evidence in the form of in court identification of the defendant by an undercover police officer. The court rejected defendant's argument that his admission to being a drug addict lessened the prosecution's burden of proof because being drug dependent was not the same as being in possession of drugs at the time of his arrest. Defendant's claim that prosecuting him for both the possession and the sale of narcotics was double jeopardy was rejected because the two offenses had different elements. Defendant's claim that his sentence was an abuse of discretion was also denied because the sentences imposed were within the statutory limits for the offenses.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for the possession of and the sale of narcotics and the sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school were affirmed because the jury had sufficient evidence to identify defendant and defendant's testimony as to his drug dependency did not unconstitutionally dilute the prosecution's burden of proof. The court also held that there was no double jeopardy violation.

 

930 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ryan


(AC 16865)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


53 Conn. App. 606; 733 A.2d 273; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 220


January 25, 1999, Argued  
June 1, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the third degree and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Spada, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction of robbery in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136, and assault in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61, rendered after a jury trial, in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of robbery in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136 and assault in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61. Defendant appealed, claiming, inter alia, that the trial court improperly instructed the jury regarding the law of reasonable doubt and the presumption of innocence, thereby depriving him of his rights under the state and federal constitutions. Specifically, he raised six claims regarding the jury instructions. The appellate court addressed each claim. Defendant sought review under Golding on three unpreserved claims. The appellate court found that two of the claims were not entitled to review because the instructions at issue did not constitute constitutional violations; nor did either involve plain error. Defendant's claim concerning the presumption of innocence was reviewable because it alleged the violation of a constitutional right, but it failed the third prong of Golding. Under the third prong, defendant could have prevailed on an unpreserved constitutional claim of instructional error only if from the substance of the charge rather than its form, it was reasonably possible that the jury was misled. Judgment affirmed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of conviction of robbery in the third degree and assault in the third degree. Defendant's the claims underlying the claim that the trial court improperly instructed the jury regarding the law of reasonable doubt and the presumption of innocence either failed or were not reviewable by the appellate court. The appellate court disagreed with the other claim regarding the filing of the substitute information.

Burnham v. Carr


(AC 17694)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


53 Conn. App. 425; 730 A.2d 643; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 213

May 25, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to confirm an arbitration award, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven at Meriden and tried to the court, Silbert, J.; judgment confirming the award, from which the defendant appealed to this court; thereafter, the court, DiPentima, J., granted the plaintiff's application for a prejudgment attachment of certain of the defendant's real and personal property; subsequently, this court affirmed the judgment of the trial court; thereafter, the court, Gaffney, J., ordered the defendant to make certain payments and granted the plaintiff's motion for attorney's fees; subsequently, the court, Dunnell, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to find the defendant in contempt, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant builder appealed a judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven at Meriden (Connecticut) that affirmed an arbitration award in favor of the plaintiff contractor in a contract dispute.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contractor and defendant builder entered into a construction contract for excavation and site work for the construction of a house. The contract was terminated after a dispute arose as to the value of services rendered by the plaintiff. The parties submitted their dispute to arbitration. The arbitrator found in favor of the plaintiff, awarding him the balance due on the contract, interest, and fees. The defendant refused to pay the plaintiff the award. The plaintiff filed an application to confirm the award and the defendant filed an application to vacate it. The trial court affirmed the award. The defendant again refused to pay the plaintiff. On appeal, the defendant claimed that the plaintiff's filing of a prejudgment remedy violated his due process rights. The court concluded that the defendant had seven days to file an appeal concerning the remedy, but did not take action until nine months later. Therefore, the claim concerning the remedy was untimely. The defendant also claimed that the trial court improperly found him to be in contempt. The court found this claim to be without merit and declined further review. Therefore, the lower court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The lower court's judgment for plaintiff contractor was affirmed because the defendant builder's appeal of the prejudgment remedy was untimely and there was no merit in the defendant's claim that the trial court improperly found him to be in contempt.

Anguish v. TLM, Inc.


(AC 18076)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


53 Conn. App. 241; 728 A.2d 1165; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 174


February 3, 1999, Argued  
May 11, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the seventh district reinstating the plaintiff's temporary total disability benefits, brought to the compensation review board, which dismissed the appeal, and the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed a judgment from the workers' compensation review board (Connecticut), which dismissed an appeal from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner reinstating plaintiff's temporary total disability benefits.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee appealed from the dismissal of his appeal to the workers' compensation review board (board). Plaintiff contended that the board improperly approved defendant employer's notice to discontinue his temporary total disability benefits because, he argued, there should have been a formal hearing for the workers' compensation commissioner (commissioner) to approve the discontinuance. Moreover, plaintiff urged that the failure to have such a hearing was a violation of his due process rights guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed the dismissal finding that this was not a case requiring a review of what would otherwise be moot. It further found that plaintiff could not be afforded any further practical relief at this time as his benefits had been reinstated. Finally, plaintiff had a formal hearing after the board agreed with him in his first appeal that his due process rights entitled him to a formal hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff employee's appeal to a workers' compensation review board because the case was not one requiring review of what would otherwise be moot. In addition, further relief was not available because disability benefits had been reinstated.

 

933 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Valinski


(AC 17466)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


53 Conn. App. 23; 731 A.2d 311; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 150


November 30, 1998, Argued  
April 28, 1999, Officially Released *


* April 28, 1999, the date that this decision was re-released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended May 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts of the crime of operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension, with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and with the infraction of failure to drive on the right and, in the second part, with having previously been convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, geographical area number eighteen, and tried to the jury before Kocay, J., on the first part of the information on the charges of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension verdict of guilty; thereafter, the defendant was tried to the court on the charge of failure to drive on the right; subsequently, the court granted the defendant's motion to set aside the verdict on one count of operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the second part of [***2] the information; judgment of guilty of failure to drive on the right, operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant appealed his conviction by the Litchfield Superior Court (Connecticut) for operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension, operating a motor vehicle while under the influence, and failure to drive on the right. The defendant alleged that he could not be convicted of operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension because he possessed a work permit license.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence, operating a vehicle with a suspended license, and failure to drive on the right. At the time the defendant was stopped by the police for erratic driving while returning from a fishing trip, he was in possession of a work permit, a conditional driver's license permitting the defendant to drive for work purposes only. At trial, the defendant asserted that he could not be convicted of driving on a suspended license in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215 because he was in possession of a valid work permit. The lower court rejected his argument and instructed the jury to find the defendant guilty if he had not proved by a "preponderance" of the evidence that he was driving within the context of the work permit. The appellate court found that the lower court mis-instructed the jury by inferring that some part of the burden of proof was on the defendant, rather than emphasizing the fact that the defendant was innocent until proven guilty. The court therefore reversed the lower court as to the suspended license charge only and remanded for new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found the defendant's assertion that he could not be convicted of driving on a suspended license because he held a work permit license to be without merit. However, the court agreed with the defendant's allegation that the court mis-instructed the jury as to the defendant's burden of proof and therefore remanded for new trial.

 

934 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Kostrzewski v. Commissioner of Motor Vehicles


(AC 17359)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


52 Conn. App. 326; 727 A.2d 233; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 94


September 17, 1998, Argued  
March 23, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant suspending the plaintiff's license to operate a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Maloney, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), in which the court affirmed defendant's decision suspending plaintiff's driver's license under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-111c as a result of her conviction in Florida for driving under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Defendant suspended plaintiff's Connecticut license to operate a motor vehicle pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-111c as a result of plaintiff's conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol. The lower court affirmed defendant's decision and plaintiff appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that defendant did not commit error in admitting her conviction and that the driver's license compact did not violate the double jeopardy clause. According to the appeals court, administrative tribunals were not strictly bound by the rules of evidence and they could consider evidence which would normally be incompetent in a judicial proceeding, so long as the evidence was reliable and probative. The appeals court held that the evidence concerning plaintiff's conviction in Florida was reliable and probative and was admissible. Next, the appeals court held that plaintiff's one year license suspension did not violate the double jeopardy clause because a civil or administrative sanction that served a legitimate remedial purpose and was related rationally to that purpose did not give rise to a double jeopardy violation even if the sanction had some deterrent effect.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the suspension of plaintiff's driver's license as a result of her conviction for driving under the influence in another state because defendant's conviction was admissible where it was reliable and because the suspension did not violate the double jeopardy clause.
