State v. Kung


(AC 17841)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


52 Conn. App. 121; 726 A.2d 130; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 66


January 19, 1999, Argued  
March 2, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motor vehicle infraction complaint charging the defendant with speeding, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the court, Tobin, J.; judgment of guilty from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from Superior Court, District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), judgment convicting him of speeding in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-219, alleging improper shifting of burden of proof and factual errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of speeding in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-219. Defendant appealed, alleging that lower court improperly shifted the burden of proof to require him to prove that he was not guilty of the offense. The court held that given the state trooper's testimony that defendant was driving at seventy-four miles per hour in a posted fifty-five miles per hour zone and defendant's testimony that did not include the speed at which he was traveling, lower court's statement that there was absolutely no evidence of defendant's not speeding was an observation that there was no evidence contradicting the trooper's testimony rather than a shifting of the burden of proof. Further, the court held that defendant's remaining claims all raised issues of fact, which were matters for the lower court rather than for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court, holding that the factual issues raised by defendant were matters for the lower court, and further holding that since defendant had failed to contradict the testimony alleging that he was speeding, the lower court's observation to that regard was not improper shifting of burden of proof to defendant.

State v. McMillan


(AC 16731)

51 Conn. App. 676; 725 A.2d 342; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 37

February 5, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics, conspiracy to possess narcotics, sale of narcotics, possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school and conspiracy to possess narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the court, Clark, J., rendered judgment dismissing the information; thereafter, the court denied the state's request for permission to appeal, and the state filed a motion for review with this court, which granted the state permission to file a late appeal to this court.

State v. Latorre


(AC 16869)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


51 Conn. App. 541; 723 A.2d 1166; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 28


September 16, 1998, Argued  
January 26, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree and with the crimes of commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions on a jury verdict in the Superior Court (Connecticut) for armed robbery and carrying a pistol without a permit. Defendant claimed the trial court improperly failed to instruct the jury on the essential elements of robbery, improperly determined that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, and improperly failed to find prosecutorial misconduct in the prosecutor's final summation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed he was entitled to have his two first-degree robbery convictions reversed because the trial court failed to instruct the jury on the statutory elements of robbery. Although defendant failed to preserve the error for review, the trial court was constitutionally required to instruct the jury properly on every essential element of the crime charged and the court reversed and remanded. It could not be considered harmless error for a jury to find an accused guilty without knowing what the essential elements of the crimes charged were. The trial court's failure to instruct the jury on the intent requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-133 was harmful error mandating reversal. Further, even if the conviction had been upheld, defendant was incorrectly sentenced under § 53-202k, which was intended to serve as a sentence enhancement provision, not as a separate crime under which a defendant could be convicted. However, defendant's claim that the trial court incorrectly instructed the jury on attempted robbery failed because an unsuccessful robbery was not the same as an attempted robbery and the evidence was sufficient to prove defendant acted as a principal in the robbery.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for first-degree robbery were reversed and remanded because the lower court failed to properly instruct the jury as to the statutory elements of the crime charged and he was erroneously convicted under a sentencing enhancement provision for committing a felony with a firearm. Defendant's conviction as a principal was affirmed because the evidence was sufficient to prove defendant threatened the immediate use of force.

Golden Hill Paugussett Tribe of Indians v. Weicker


(AC 17460)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


51 Conn. App. 552; 723 A.2d 348; 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 24


September 23, 1998, Argued  
January 26, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for a writ of mandamus to compel the defendant to negotiate a trust agreement with the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and referred to Hon. Mary R. Hennessey, judge trial referee; judgment denying the application from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a tribe of Native Americans, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut). The trial court refused plaintiff's request for a writ of mandamus to compel defendant governor to enter into trust agreements with Indian tribes pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-66h(a).


OVERVIEW: An Indian Affairs task force submitted several reports to the general assembly. After the submission of the 1991 report, plaintiff, a tribe of Native Americans, brought a mandamus action to compel defendant governor to enter into trust agreements with Indian tribes pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-66h(a). The trial court denied plaintiff's request. The court affirmed. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-66h specifically required that a trust agreement be consistent with recommendations contained in the final report of the task force. The trial court properly concluded that the 1991 report constituted the final report of the task force, and that this report did not contain trust agreement recommendations as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-66h. Even if all of the reports collectively constituted the final report, the task force nonetheless failed to issue a final report that contained trust agreement recommendations. In the absence of such recommendations, no trust agreements could be entered into and a writ of mandamus could not issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied a writ of mandamus to plaintiff, a tribe of Native Americans, to compel defendant governor to enter into trust agreements with Indian tribes. The trust agreements could not be entered into because an Indian Affairs task force had failed to issue a final report that contained trust agreement recommendations.

State Library v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n


(AC 14415), (14416)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


50 Conn. App. 491; 717 A.2d 842; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 392


December 15, 1997, Argued  
September 22, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in each case, from the decision by the named defendant ordering access to certain records of an investigatory subcommittee of the city of Norwich, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at Norwich, where the court, Teller, J., granted the named defendant's motion to consolidate the appeals; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Hurley, J.; judgments sustaining the appeals, from which the named defendant and the defendant Maria T. Hileman et al. filed separate appeals to this court, which consolidated the appeals, reversed the judgments of the trial court and remanded the case to that court with direction to dismiss the appeals, and, on the granting of certification, the plaintiffs filed separate appeals to the Supreme Court, which reversed this court's judgment and remanded the case to this court for further proceedings.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, reporter and newspaper, complained to the Connecticut Freedom of Information Commission which ordered disclosure with some redaction of documents held by plaintiff library. The library and plaintiffs, city and individuals, appealed to the trial court which reversed. The reporter, paper, and commission appealed to the appellate court which reversed. On appeal, the supreme court reversed and remanded to the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: Hearings were conducted in 1964 on the city's police department. In 1973, the city and library contracted that the transcripts be retained at the library as historical records, but that they be sealed for 50 years. The reporter and paper argued that the trial court improperly substituted its judgment for the commission's. On remand, the appellate court held that although the trial court found that the commission made no finding as to the 1964 investigation's legality, the trial court itself did not purport to make such related findings. The trial court was not required to defer to the commission's legal conclusions in that the commission's construction of the federal contract clause had not previously undergone judicial scrutiny. The paper failed to adequately brief the issue whether the contract clause was limited to property interests cases. Exchange of promises was sufficient consideration. Applying the Freedom of Information Act in the case would have definitely impaired the contractual relationship. Reasonable minds could have differed whether disclosure, even with redaction, would have affected reputations. Open government would not have been advanced by disclosure.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court were affirmed.

State v. Tucker


(AC 16427)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


50 Conn. App. 506; 718 A.2d 979; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 391


May 28, 1998, Argued  
September 22, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of risk of injury to a child and unlawful restraint in the second degree, and information, in the second case, charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the cases were consolidated and the first case was tried to the jury before Hartmere, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of risk of injury to a child; thereafter, the court rendered judgment of guilty of violation of probation, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) for risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, and from the judgment of violation of probation in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-96.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with one count of risk of injury to a child and one count of unlawful restraint in the second degree after he pushed his minor daughter down to the ground, and made several unsuccessful attempts to force his tongue into her mouth. At the time of his arrest, defendant was on probation for a conviction of sexual assault. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court considered the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 in relation to defendant's claims that § 53-21 was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of his case. The court found that defendant had fair warning that his actions toward the victim violated the second prong of § 53-21, and therefore his challenge failed. The court reasoned that prior case law on this issue, in conjunction with the exercise of common sense, constituted fair warning to defendant that his actions were in violation of § 53-21. The court further held that the Pickering standard meant that while a defendant who deliberately and improperly touched the private parts of a minor was clearly a hard-core violator of § 53-21, such conduct was not necessarily the only type of conduct that was proscribed under the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for risk of injury to a child and violation of probation.

State v. Snyder


(AC 16898)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


49 Conn. App. 617; 717 A.2d 240; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 333


May 5, 1998, Argued  
August 4, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations charging the defendant with five counts of the crime of harassment in the second degree and five counts of the crime of disorderly conduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, where the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the court, Keller, J., granted the defendant's motions to dismiss the informations and rendered judgments thereon, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court, which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to that court for further proceedings; on remand, the court, Damiani, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the informations; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to three counts of harassment in the second degree; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) that denied his motion to dismiss and convicted him of harassment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(2) after the entry of a nolo contendere plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the harassment statute as violating his First Amendment rights and being vague and overbroad. In particular, defendant argued that his conduct did not fit within the criminal conduct proscribed by the vague terms of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(2). The state claimed that defendant clearly intended to harass victims by communicating with a third party by mail in an effort to cause such harassment. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss. Defendant was convicted, and he appealed. The court held that: (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(2) was not unconstitutionally overbroad because it prohibited intentional harassment by means of mail and did not seek to regulate the content of such mailings, which would encumber freedom of speech; (2) a person of ordinary intelligence would have fair warning that defendant's outrageous conduct was prohibited under § 53a-183(a)(2); and (3) defendant failed to meet the burden of proof that § 53a-183 (a) (2) was unconstitutionally void for vagueness beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying defendant's motion to dismiss and convicting defendant.

 

944 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Otero


(AC 17381)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


49 Conn. App. 459; 715 A.2d 782; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 311


March 24, 1998, Argued  
July 21, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder as an accessory, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Norko, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder as an accessory in the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, Connecticut. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen to pull out a shiny object before gunshots were heard, and the victim was fatally shot. He was alleged to have been wearing a ponytail at the time. He went to talk to police, and before his photo was taken, he took down his ponytail, explaining that he did not want to be mistaken for a man named "Green Eyes." The trial court charged the jurors that they could consider his taking down his ponytail as consciousness of guilt, and did not advise them of his innocent explanation for doing so. On appeal, he argued that this violated his due process rights. The appellate court disagreed. The instruction was proper, and the trial court was not obliged to enumerate the innocent explanations defendant offered. He was not entitled to an instruction that the jury had find facts proved by circumstantial evidence, or any logical inferences from the evidence, beyond a reasonable doubt; the State needed to prove only that the cumulative impact of the facts proved beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant acted intentionally. The jury charge on reasonable doubt was proper, as it followed United States Supreme Court's recommendation for such an instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Provost


(AC 15651)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


49 Conn. App. 56; 713 A.2d 879; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 262


January 12, 1998, Argued  
June 9, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Procedural History

Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) for sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the trial court of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child. On appeal, the court affirmed his convictions. The court held that the trial court properly restricted defendant's cross-examination of the witness to whom the victim first revealed the sexual abuse. The court determined that defendant failed to lay the required evidentiary foundation before raising the issue of third party culpability and failed to establish how the issue was relevant to the witness's credibility. Therefore, the court ruled that defendant was not denied his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation. The court held that alleged prosecutorial misconduct did not deprive defendant of his due process right to a fair trial. The court determined that defendant failed to preserve his objections to the conduct and that statements by the prosecutor during his closing argument were not so egregious as to implicate defendant's right to due process. The court ruled that the prosecutor did not impermissibly shift the burden of proof to defendant to prove that the victim had fabricated the charge of sexual abuse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child.

Amica Mut. Ins. Co. v. Woods


(AC 17150)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


48 Conn. App. 690; 711 A.2d 1208; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 210


February 26, 1998, Argued  
May 19, 1998, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover the amount of basic reparations benefits paid to the named defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and referred to Irving B. Shurberg, attorney trial referee, who filed a report recommending judgment for the defendants; thereafter, the court Norko, J., rendered judgment in accordance with the referee's report, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurer brought an action against defendant insured and others, seeking to recover the amount of basic reparations benefits paid to the insured. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) entered judgment, upon a referee's report, in favor of the insured. The insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insurer provided a policy of automobile insurance to the insured. On July 4, 1994 the insured was injured in an automobile accident. Subsequently, the insurer paid certain funds for medical costs and other benefits pursuant to the basic reparations benefits portion of the policy. The insured later reached a settlement with a third-party tortfeasor. The insurer then sought to recover the reparations benefits paid. The referee determined the insurer was not entitled to recover reparations benefits paid, and recommended judgment for the insured. The trial court accepted the referee's report over the insurer's objections. On appeal, the insurer claimed the trial court improperly concluded the right to recover basic reparations benefits was extinguished when 1993 Conn. Acts 297 repealed Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-369. The insurer also claimed the application of the changes mandated in 1993 Conn. Acts 297 violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 (contracts clause). The court affirmed the judgment because the insurer did not have a vested right to recover the benefits as of the date of the accident and the insurer failed to demonstrate a substantial impairment of its contractual rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the insured in the action brought by the insurer to recover benefits paid to the insured.

 

947 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Dumont v. Commissioner of Motor Vehicles


(AC 16761)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


48 Conn. App. 635; 712 A.2d 427; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 203


February 19, 1998, Argued  
May 12, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the suspension by the defendant of the plaintiff's license to operate a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Maloney, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal from the suspension by appellee commissioner of the driver's license to operate a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: The driver's license was suspended because he failed a blood alcohol breath test after he had been pulled over by a trooper. On review, the driver claimed that there was no probable cause for his arrest, the commissioner's decision was not supported by substantial evidence, and the criminal statutes under which his license was suspended were unconstitutional. The court affirmed. The court found that the trial court had properly found that there was ample evidence to support the hearing officer's determination that there was probable cause to arrest the driver. Given the trooper's testimony and the certification of the testing equipment by the health department, the court determined that the trial court had ample evidence to conclude that the machine was functioning properly. The court rejected the driver's claims that the statutes did not give fair warning because an ordinary person had no ascertainable means of measuring his or her own blood alcohol content. The court found that those who drank a substantial amount of alcohol within a relatively short period of time were given clear warning that to avoid possible criminal behavior they had to refrain from driving.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the appeal from the suspension of the driver's license was affirmed.

 

948 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Cotto v. United Techs. Corp., Sikorsky Aircraft Div.


(AC 16670)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


48 Conn. App. 618; 711 A.2d 1180; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 205; 13 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1732


January 12, 1998, Argued  
May 12, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the defendant's termination of the plaintiff's employment for the exercise of rights allegedly protected by the state and federal constitutions, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Fracasse, J., granted the defendant's motion to strike the complaint; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiff's motion for judgment and rendered judgment in favor of the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged the decision of the Superior Court of New Haven (Connecticut), which rendered judgment in favor of appellee former employer on the granting of its motion to strike the former employee's two count complaint. The former employee filed suit to recover damages for the termination of his employment for the exercise of rights allegedly protected by the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The issue to be resolved was whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-51q provided the former employee with a cause of action for monetary damages against the former employer after he was discharged from his employment for an alleged exercise by the former employee of his federal or state constitutional right of free speech when the speech took place at the site of the workplace. The former employer claimed that a cause of action based on § 31-51q was unavailable to an employee whose alleged expressive activity occurred exclusively on the private property of his employer, and the former employee's words and actions as alleged were not constitutionally protected. The court concluded that § 31-51q applied to some activities and speech that occurred at the workplace because there were no words in the statute limiting the place at which the constitutionally protected activity occurred, there was no prohibition that prevented a legislature from protecting employee speech wherever it occurred, and other legislation governing the same general subject matter included speech occurring at the workplace. The court further held that on the facts as alleged, the former employee had no cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the former employer.

Settani v. Commissioner of Motor Vehicles

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

State v. Kimber


(AC 15800)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


48 Conn. App. 234; 709 A.2d 570; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 116


December 15, 1997, Argued  
March 24, 1998, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the second degree, larceny in the third degree and perjury, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the court, Lager, J., granted the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal of larceny in the second degree; verdict and judgment of guilty of larceny in the third degree and perjury, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for larceny in the third degree and perjury, which were entered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: Defendant worked at a funeral home. He withdrew money that was in an irrevocable funeral trust bank account. The client who paid the funds demanded their return. Defendant refused to return the funds. Defendant argued that his testimony to the jury that he did not know the meaning of irrevocable funeral trust negated any evidence of intent presented by the State. The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that that sufficient evidence was presented from which a jury reasonably could have concluded that the cumulative force of the evidence established guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that (1) defendant withdrew the funds from the account held by the funeral home for the benefit of a client using a certificate marked irrevocable funeral trust for the benefit of the client, (2) demand was made on defendant for a return of the funds, (3) defendant failed to return the moneys and ignored the request. The court stated that from these facts alone, sufficient evidence was presented from which the jury reasonably could have inferred that defendant intended to take funds from the client's account without her permission, and that he refused to return them.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for larceny in the third degree and perjury were affirmed.

State v. Ryan


(AC 15840)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


48 Conn. App. 148; 709 A.2d 21; 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 112


November 7, 1997, Argued  
March 17, 1998, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit murder and inciting injury to persons, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of inciting injury to persons, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her conviction for inciting injury to persons in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut). On appeal, defendant claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-179a was vague and overbroad and that the trial court abused its discretion by improperly refusing to admit into evidence a police informant's criminal history.


OVERVIEW: Defendant wanted her ex-husband killed because she suspected that he or his roommate were victimizing her children. A police informant arranged for a hit man, who was actually a police officer, to meet with defendant to perform the killing. A jury found defendant guilty of inciting injury to persons and property, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-179a, but acquitted her of attempted murder. On appeal, defendant asserted that the language in § 53a-179a was vague on its face because it lacked a common core meaning and prohibited speech protected by the First Amendment. The court disagreed and affirmed. The court held that the statute required an intent to cause injury in addition to the proscribed language. The court also rejected defendant's First Amendment challenge. The court held that the statute did not allow a person to be prosecuted for a mere expression of opinion without any criminal intent or criminal act. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in declining to admit as evidence the police informant's prior drug-related arrest and criminal history.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for inciting injury to persons.

Stat. § 53-202k vacated because the statute was a sentence enhancement provision and not a separate crime. The court remanded the case for correction.

DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of four counts of kidnapping in the first degree, one count of robbery in the first degree, two counts of robbery in the second degree, and one count of commission of a class A, B, or C felony with a firearm. The convictions arose out of defendant's robbery of a fast food restaurant.


OVERVIEW: The police arrived at the scene and saw defendant run and drop a vest that contained the keys to his apartment. Defendant claimed on appeal that the trial court improperly refused to suppress out-of-court identifications of him made by witnesses and that remarks made by the prosecutor during the state's closing argument impermissibly infringed on his constitutional right to testify. The court disagreed and affirmed defendant's conviction holding that the on-the-scene identification procedure used by the police was reasonably necessary because it allowed the witnesses to view the suspect while their memories of the incident were still fresh. The court further held that the prosecutor's remarks on defendant's credibility were proper and did not invite the jury to draw an inference adverse to defendant solely on account of defendant's assertion of his right to testify as defendant opened up the issue of his credibility. The court vacated defendant's conviction, however, to permit resentencing as the trial court erred by treating an enhancement provision of one of defendant's crimes as a separate offense in calculating prison time.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, in part, the trial court's conviction of defendant with regard to committing a class A, B, or C felony with a firearm and remanded the case with direction to vacate defendant's conviction for committing a class A, B, or C felony with a firearm and to resentence defendant to a total effective term of imprisonment of 20 years.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of larceny in the sixth degree and credit card theft and with the crimes of assault in the second degree, forgery in the second degree and attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of larceny in the sixth degree, two counts of credit card theft, the lesser included offense of assault in the third degree, forgery in the second degree and attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Henderson, 37 Conn. App. 733, 658 A.2d 585, 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 234 (May 9, 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which was entered on a verdict convicting him of larceny under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125b, assault under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61, credit card theft under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-128c(a), forgery under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-139(a)(1), and attempted kidnapping under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49(a)(2) and 53a-94(a).

The court found no error in denying defendant's motion for a mistrial arguing that the state violated an order in limine because the jury's use of evidence that the detective watched defendant in the store because he bought high-ticket items the previous day was limited by a proper curative instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of two counts of larceny in the sixth degree, one count of assault in the third degree, two counts of credit card theft, one count of forgery in the second degree, and one count of criminal attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree.

State v. Shinn


(AC 15928)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


47 Conn. App. 401; 704 A.2d 816; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 573


October 1, 1997, Argued  
December 30, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit murder, attempt to commit assault in the first degree and carrying a dangerous weapon without a permit, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crime of threatening, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of attempt to commit murder and carrying a dangerous weapon without a permit in the first case, and verdict and judgment of guilty of threatening in the second case, from which the defendant filed a joint appeal to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part in the first case, new trial; affirmed in the second case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Haven (Connecticut) after he was convicted of attempt to commit murder, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stats. §§ 53a-49(a)(2), 53a-54a, carrying a dangerous weapon without a permit, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-206(a), and threatening, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-62.


OVERVIEW: In a confrontation with a police officer, defendant moved quickly towards the officer while holding a knife. On appeal from his convictions, the court rejected defendant's argument that the State was required, in order to convict defendant of attempt to commit murder, to prove that defendant "planned" to murder the officer on the roof. Instead, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction for attempt to commit murder because the jury could have found that defendant's act of advancing towards the officer while holding the knife in a menacing manner was a substantial step in a course of conduct that was planned to culminate in the murder of the officer. Upon considering the State's comment that defendant chose to testify because he believed the State's evidence against him was strong, the court found that the comment amounted to a denial of defendant's due process rights. Moreover, the State had not proven that the comment was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the critical question in the case was whether the officer or defendant, the only eyewitnesses to the events, was telling the truth.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in part, reversing defendant's conviction for attempt to commit murder. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), where he was convicted of murder as an accessory and conspiracy to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: Witnesses implicated defendant in a shooting. Tests of the truck defendant had been driving revealed elements characteristic of gunshot residue. Defendant made some statements to police. State v. Oliphant


(AC 15393)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


47 Conn. App. 271; 702 A.2d 1206; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 555


September 16, 1997, Argued  
December 9, 1997, officially released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Oliphant, 244 Conn. 904, 714 A.2d 3, 1998 Conn. LEXIS 81 (1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Oliphant v. Warden, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3652 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 20, 2000)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of larceny in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, and tried to the jury before Gaffney, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Oliphant, 1995 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2372 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 15, 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), for larceny in the first degree. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to conduct an adequate canvass prior to accepting his waiver of the right to counsel, that he was denied effective assistance of standby counsel, and that the evidence was insufficient.


OVERVIEW: Defendant applied for and received duplicate welfare benefits using his own name and an alias. Defendant was arraigned, and a public defender was appointed to represent him. The public defender had represented defendant previously in other criminal matters in which defendant was found guilty. Defendant requested a different public defender, but the trial court denied the request after which defendant expressed a desire to represent himself. The trial court allowed defendant to represent himself, but it required the public defender to serve as standby counsel. Defendant was convicted of larceny, and he appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court was properly satisfied that defendant's waiver of counsel was knowing and intelligently made in conformity with Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 961. There was no merit to defendant's claim that standby counsel was ineffective. Defendant did not have a constitutional right to standby counsel, and the requirements of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book §§ 962 through 964 were met. The evidence was sufficient to prove defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, so the court would not disturb the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for larceny in the first degree.

 

958 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Eason


(AC 16062)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


47 Conn. App. 117; 703 A.2d 130; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 516


September 16, 1997, Argued  
November 11, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Norko, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1) and unlawful restraint in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-95(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court's failure to give limiting instructions concerning the use of prior conviction and misconduct evidence, coupled with improper statements made by the prosecutor, constituted plain error. Because defendant failed to preserve the claim for review, he argued that he was entitled to plain error review. The court rejected defendant's claim and affirmed his conviction, finding that plain error review was reserved for truly extraordinary situations where the existence of the error was so obvious that it affected the fairness and integrity of, and public confidence in, the judicial proceedings. The court determined that the claimed error was not such an "obvious" error. Further, the court failed to see how the prosecutor's remarks were so abusive or prejudicial as to deprive defendant of a fair trial and, therefore, concluded that defendant had waived his right to raise the claim of prosecutorial misconduct. Finally, the court found that convictions for sexual assault and unlawful restraint did not violate defendant's right against double jeopardy because the two crimes each required proof of a fact not required for conviction of the other.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of sexual assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree.

In re Michael A.


(AC 16531)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


47 Conn. App. 105; 703 A.2d 1146; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 514


September 16, 1997, Argued  
November 11, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to remove the respondent mother as guardian of the parties' minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, Juvenile Matters at Middletown, and tried to the court, Foley, J.; judgment granting the petition, from which the respondent appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middelsex, Juvenile Matters at Middletown (Connecticut), which granted petitioner father's request to remove the mother as guardian of the parties' minor child and granted him sole guardianship and custody pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-610.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the mother contended that the superior court should have addressed the alleged impropriety of a prior order of temporary custody before considering the petition for removal of guardianship. The court concluded, however, that any issues involving the order of temporary custody were moot because that order was subsumed by the order appealed from, which granted sole custody and guardianship to the father. The mother also claimed that the trial court improperly applied only the best interests of the child standard of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-605 instead of finding a statutory basis for removing her as guardian as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-610. The court disagreed and found that the record amply supported the trial court's conclusion that the evidence satisfied the clear and convincing standard of § 45a-610 as well as the best interests of the child standard of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-605. Finally, the court found that the mother's claim that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 45a-607, 45a-610 was unconstitutional was untimely and that the mother failed to demonstrate any exceptional circumstances that would allow the court to consider the claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

960 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jason B.


(AC 15323)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


47 Conn. App. 68; 702 A.2d 895; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 475


May 1, 1997, Argued  
October 28, 1997, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with being a youthful offender for having committed the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the court, Barry, J.; judgment of guilty of being a youthful offender for committing the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which found him guilty of being a youthful offender in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-76b, for committing the crime of sexual assault in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(1), and injury or risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21.


OVERVIEW: The victim and defendant were students at the same high school. Defendant was accused of sexually assaulting the victim. At the time, the victim was 14 years old, and defendant was 16 years old. Defendant was found guilty of being a youthful offender, for committing the crime of sexual assault in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(1), and injury or risk of injury to a child. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(1) was not unconstitutionally vague. The statute made it unlawful for any person to have sexual intercourse with a youth age 13-15 when the difference between their ages exceeded two years. The difference between the age of defendant and the victim was two years, three months, and seven days. The court found that the statute did not discriminate against 16 year olds because it did not single out all 16 year olds for adverse treatment. The court further found that the restriction placed by the statute did not impinge on defendant's fundamental right to have sexual relations with consenting partners because the restriction was justified and the state had a compelling interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of being guilty as a youthful offender for committing the crime of sexual assault in the second degree, and injury or risk of injury to a child.

State v. Lindstrom


(AC 16023)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


46 Conn. App. 810; 702 A.2d 410; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 471


January 16, 1997, Argued  
September 23, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, attempted sexual assault in the first degree, and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Spada, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's victim identified him from his picture in a photo lineup. The lineup contained the pictures of seven other people that the victim knew. Defendant contended that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress the victim's pretrial identification and in subsequently allowing her to identify him in court. He also contended that the trial court denied him access to the victim's drug and psychiatric records for impeachment purposes. The court held that the trial court correctly denied the motion to suppress and allowed the in-court identification despite the fact that the photographic array was unnecessarily suggestive, because the victim had observed defendant for a period of hours during the assault and there was not a risk that the original identification procedure was suggestive as to be conducive to irreparable misidentification. The court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant access to portions of the victim's medical records because he was able to question the victim on all of the subjects that he proposed to the trial court as necessary fields of inquiry for impeachment purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

962 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Associates Fin. Servs. of Am. v. Sorenson


(AC 16187)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


46 Conn. App. 721; 700 A.2d 107; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 462


May 30, 1997, Argued  
September 16, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage on certain real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, West, J., granted the motion filed by Ford Consumer Finance Company, Inc., to be substituted as plaintiff; thereafter, the court granted the motion for summary judgment filed by the defendant Northern State Financial, LLC, and rendered judgment thereon, from which the substitute plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgage owner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which granted the motion for summary judgment filed by defendant purchaser in the mortgage owner's action to foreclose a mortgage on real property under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-157 (1993).


OVERVIEW: The purchaser's grantor acquired the real property through a tax foreclosure sale. The mortgage owner's predecessor owned the mortgage at the time of the foreclosure sale. The predecessor originally brought a foreclosure action against the purchaser and the mortgage owner was substituted as plaintiff. The trial court granted the purchaser's motion for summary judgment, holding that the tax foreclosure sale extinguished the mortgage on the property. Upon review, the court affirmed, holding that § 12-157 was not unconstitutional because it provided the mortgage holder's predecessor with proper notice and an opportunity to be heard. The court held that the deprivation of the mortgage owner's property interest did not occur without due process of law. The court held that a hearing or judicial review of the valuation and sale of the property was not required because no findings of fact were required by the tax collector. The court held that the trial court properly granted summary judgment because the mortgage owner failed to prove that its predecessor did not have notice or actual notice of the sale, and thus, it did not overcome the prima facie evidence of unencumbered title.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the purchaser's motion for summary judgment in the mortgage owner's foreclosure action.

 

963 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cummings


(AC 14275)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


46 Conn. App. 661; 701 A.2d 663; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 452


April 22, 1997, Argued  
September 9, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of harassment in the second degree and with the crimes of stalking in the first degree, stalking in the second degree, disorderly conduct and criminal violation of a protective order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Tierney, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of stalking in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181d, harassment in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(3), and disorderly conduct in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: After he was romantically involved with the victim, defendant telephoned her, called and visited her friends and family, and followed her. The trial court convicted him of stalking, harassment, disorderly conduct, and criminal violation of the victim's protective order. On appeal, defendant claimed that three of the statutes were unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The stalking in the second degree statute was not unconstitutionally vague because its ambiguities were not so significant to render it void for vagueness and it provided sufficient guidelines to prevent arbitrary enforcement. The disorderly conduct statute was unconstitutional on its face because the terms "annoy, offensive, and disorderly" were vague. Although judicial gloss had been applied to those terms, defendant's conviction occurred before the gloss was applied. The harassment statute was not unconstitutionally vague although it contained the term "annoy" because judicial gloss was previously applied, nor was the statute unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant's conduct because he previously violated the statute and was on notice of the proscribed conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for stalking in the second degree and harassment in the second degree. The court reversed defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct.

Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-119 and 53a-123. Defendant claimed that the classification of this crime violated his right to equal protection.

In re Jonathan M.


(AC 14693)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


46 Conn. App. 545; 700 A.2d 1370; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 449


May 30, 1997, Argued  
September 2, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to adjudicate the respondent minor a delinquent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, Juvenile Matters at Willimantic, where the court, McWeeny, J., granted the state's motion to transfer the case to the regular criminal docket of the Superior Court, and the respondent appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent minor appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham (Connecticut), which granted the state's motion to transfer his case to the regular criminal docket in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-127 (Rev. to 1993).


OVERVIEW: The minor was 15 years old and accused of murder. The trial court granted the state's petition to transfer the minor to the regular criminal docket. The court affirmed the trial court, holding that the police were not required to inform him that he could be tried as an adult before accepting his confession. The court held that the confession was voluntary and knowing, where the minor and his mother acknowledged in writing that they had received and understood the Miranda warnings. The court found that the mother was given ample time to talk privately with her son, but chose not to, and that the confession was taken in the mother's presence even though, at her request, she was sitting in the hallway and did not have eye contact with her son. The court found that the mother chose this arrangement after it became apparent to her that her son had murdered her mother, and she could no longer tolerate looking at him. The court held that the failure to record the reading of his rights was not a due process violation, and that statements made to a friend were admissible even though they were made without the presence of a parent. The court found no violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-133.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment to transfer the minor to the regular criminal docket.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut) granting defendant's amended motion to suppress certain evidence and his motion to dismiss the arson charges against him.


OVERVIEW: Flooring samples were seized incident to an investigation to determine the cause and origin of a fire that caused substantial damage to defendant's home. The samples were then tested in the laboratory without first obtaining a search warrant. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress the test results. The court affirmed this decision, holding that: (1) defendant had an expectation of privacy in the samples and that expectation was reasonable; (2) the testing was a search within the meaning of Conn. Const. art. I, § 7; and (3) the search did not fall within the recognized exception to the warrant requirement for exigent circumstances .


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the arson charges against defendant was affirmed.

August 26, 1997, officially released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 5, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6155.

Appeal denied by State v. Connelly, 244 Conn. 908, 713 A.2d 829, 1998 Conn. LEXIS 102 (1998)
Writ of certiorari denied Connelly v. Connecticut, 525 U.S. 907, 119 S. Ct. 245, 142 L. Ed. 2d 201, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6155 (1998)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Summary judgment granted by Connelly v. Lantz, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 82171 (D. Conn., Nov. 2, 2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at State v. Connelly, 129 Conn. App. 373, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 325 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of kidnapping in the second degree and assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, and tried to the jury before Scheinblum, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Connelly v. Solnit, 1994 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2051 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 16, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which, on retrial after a verdict of not guilty by reason of insanity, entered judgment on the jury's verdict that found defendant guilty of two counts each of the crimes of kidnapping in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94, and assault in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-60.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found not guilty by reason of insanity and was committed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-13, 17a-580-17a-603. Defendant did not appeal from either his acquittal or his commitment, but filed a habeas corpus petition. The habeas court, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-493, ordered a new trial. The court held that the habeas court properly relied on defendant's claim that his constitutional right to a trial by jury was violated, that the habeas court had the authority to order a new trial, and that defendant had met the cause of prejudice standard to allow the habeas proceeding in the absence of taking a direct appeal. Regarding the retrial, the court ruled that (1) there was sufficient evidence to charge the jury on kidnapping and unlawful restraint and that it was up to the jury to determine which, if either, defendant had committed; (2) the trial court properly considered the pre-sentence investigation when determining defendant's sentence; and (3) defendant was not denied effective representation under the Sixth Amendment by the conduct of his stand-by counsel because defendant waived his right to counsel when he chose to proceed pro se.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Chapman


(AC 15426)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


46 Conn. App. 24; 698 A.2d 347; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 375


April 29, 1997, Argued  
July 29, 1997, officially released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied April 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2370.


PRIOR HISTORY: (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of risk of injury to a child and assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, and tried to the court, Sylvester, J.; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal of assault in the second degree and rendered judgment of guilty of risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which found him guilty of risk of injury to a child, upon a substitute information charging him with the crimes of risk of injury to a child and assault in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that, among other things, his conviction was fatally flawed because the trial court permitted him to be tried when he had not properly waived his constitutional right to a trial by jury, and that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction for risk of injury to a child. Viewing the totality of circumstances, the court concluded that defendant waived his right to a jury trial, and that the waiver was knowing, voluntary, and intelligent. The court further concluded that defendant's claim that the trial court improperly enlarged the charge against him was meritless. The trial court's finding that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant employed a weapon or instrument did not affect the sufficiency of the evidence required to support defendant's conviction for risk of injury to a child. The evidence presented at trial was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for risk of injury to a child, and defendant's claim to the contrary was without merit. Defendant's claim of inconsistent determinations was also without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him after a jury trial of two counts of felony murder, attempt to commit robbery in the first degree, and two counts of robbery in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54c; 53a-134(a)(1), (2), (4); 53a-49(a)(2); 53a-134(a)(2), (4).


OVERVIEW: After an employee gave a man a job application, she made a telephone call. A man with the same rolled up blue shirt sleeves and voice came up behind her, put a gun to her head, and demanded money. The robber demanded money from another employee and the owner of the company and shot and killed them both. The court found that the affidavit accompanying the arrest warrant presented a substantial factual basis to support the issuing judge's conclusion that probable cause for the lineup and the voice sample existed based on the surviving employee's description of the gunman. The identification procedure was not unnecessarily suggestive, even though the employee was shown photographs of defendant in arrays on several occasions. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding expert testimony on the subject of eyewitness identification after concluding that the proffered testimony was within the general knowledge of the jurors. The trial court properly admitted evidence of prior robbery convictions because it was relevant to prove identity and to show a common scheme of criminal activity as the characteristics of the four robberies were sufficiently distinctive and unique.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

State v. Morales


AC 14765


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


45 Conn. App. 116; 694 A.2d 1356; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 236


January 13, 1997, Argued  
May 13, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child and with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and sexual assault in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Freed, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which entered a jury verdict that convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(2) (1991), two counts of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, and sexual assault in the fourth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-73a(a)(1)(A).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife operated a day care in their home. Defendant allegedly penetrated a child's vagina with his finger and asked her to touch his penis. He was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree, two counts of risk of injury to a child, and sexual assault in the fourth degree. The court reversed defendant's conviction for sexual assault in the first degree and remanded with direction to render a judgment of not guilty on that charge and guilty of sexual assault in the second degree. The evidence did not support a conclusion that the acts occurred after the effective date of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(2) (1991). Defendant failed to sustain his burden of establishing even an inference that the victim's prior allegation of sexual abuse was false in order to question her about other allegations of abuse. Defendant was not deprived of the opportunity to cross-examine a videotaped interview of the victim before trial and before her testimony. He had the opportunity to cross-examine the victim regarding any claimed inconsistencies. The prosecutor's comments regarding defendant's use of alcohol did not deny him a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for sexual assault in the first degree and remanded with direction to render a judgment of not guilty on that charge and guilty of sexual assault in the second degree and to resentence defendant. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for risk of injury to a child and sexual assault in the fourth degree.

State v. Casey


(AC 15847)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


45 Conn. App. 32; 692 A.2d 1312; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 201


January 21, 1997, Argued  
April 29, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, murder and conspiracy to commit murder, and information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, larceny in the second degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the cases were consolidated, and the court, Kaplan, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere on the charges of felony murder and robbery in the first degree; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut), which convicted defendant after a conditional plea of nolo contendere of felony murder and robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of felony murder and robbery in the first degree, she appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress witnesses' out-of-court identifications of her on the basis that they were unnecessarily suggestive and unreliable. The show-up identification was conducted while defendant and other suspects were standing in a line-up, handcuffed, surrounded by police officers, and next to the car in which they were stopped. The court determined that the identification process was suggestive but not unnecessarily so. The identification procedure did not give rise to a very substantial likelihood of irreparable misidentification. The court stated that the exigencies of the situation justified the procedure that was followed. Furthermore, the court found that the identification was reliable. The court considered the witnesses' degree of attention during roadside show-up, the accuracy of their prior descriptions, their levels of certainty, and the length of time between the crimes and the identifications in determining the reliability of the identifications.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Bouier


(15917)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


44 Conn. App. 548; 690 A.2d 889; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 110


January 23, 1997, Argued  
March 25, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Parker, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which had convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court improperly instructed the jury (1) by failing to instruct on compulsion, an essential element of the crime, (2) by shifting the burden to defendant to prove consent, and (3) on the use of force and the threat of the use of force. Defendant failed to preserve his compulsion claim at trial, and sought review under the theory that (1) the record was adequate to review the alleged claim of error; (2) the claim was of constitutional magnitude alleging the violation of a fundamental right; (3) the alleged constitutional violation clearly existed and clearly deprived the defendant of a fair trial; and (4) if subject to harmless error analysis, the State failed to demonstrate harmlessness of the alleged constitutional violation beyond a reasonable doubt. The court, which was free to dispose of the claim by focusing on whichever condition was most relevant in the particular circumstances, held that defendant failed to prove that a constitutional violation clearly existed that deprived him of a fair trial because the trial court charged the jury on compulsion. The State's burden never shifted, and trial evidence was sufficient to support the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

974 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Fleet Credit Corp. v. Miller


(15515), (15516), (15517)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


44 Conn. App. 529; 690 A.2d 423; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 95


November 12, 1996, Argued  
March 18, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in each case, from the assessment of interest on the plaintiffs' estimated corporate tax payments, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Tax Session at Hartford, where the court, Aronson, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion to consolidate the appeals; thereafter, the court, Blue, J., granted the plaintiffs' motions for summary judgment, denied the defendant's cross motions for summary judgment, and rendered judgments sustaining the plaintiffs' appeals, from which the defendant filed separate appeals to this court which were consolidated.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three consolidated cases, defendant, the commissioner of revenue services, challenged an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Tax Session at Hartford (Connecticut), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff taxpayers in their actions seeking a refund of interest paid by the taxpayers on amounts calculated by the commissioner to be due because of alleged underpayments of estimated corporate tax.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner claimed that the trial court improperly ordered him to refund the interest on the alleged underpayments. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment. In so ruling, the court noted that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-242b(a) provided that it was the taxpayer's responsibility to make declarations of estimated tax each quarter. In turn, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-242b(b) provided that the estimated tax stated in the declaration was the amount of money that the company estimated would equal the total tax that it would be required to pay. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-242c required payments of estimated tax. Because § 12-242c had been complied with, § 12-242d, entitled "interest on unpaid installments" was not called into play. Indeed, the only way that a corporate taxpayer could fall within the purview of § 12-242d was if it made an unreasonable estimate or if it did not pay the requisite percentages set forth in § 12-242c.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court.

State v. Villanueva


(15112)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


44 Conn. App. 457; 689 A.2d 1141; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 91


January 22, 1997, Argued  
March 11, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Fasano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him upon a jury verdict of two counts of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(2) and two counts of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21.


OVERVIEW: The victim was a 12-year-old girl with mild mental retardation. Because of defendant's continuous assertion of innocence, defendant requested the trial court to instruct the jury that this fact was consistent with his supposed innocence. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court violated his constitutional right to equal protection and due process when it denied his requested instruction. Defendant contended that the constancy of accusation doctrine was unconstitutional and unfair and that the constancy of denial instruction was constitutionally required to offset the harmful impact of the constancy of accusation instruction. The court affirmed the judgment. Because the court found that the constancy of accusation doctrine did not violate an accused's constitutional rights, the court found it unnecessary to required the trial court to deliver a constancy of denial instruction as a counterweight. The court also rejected defendant's assertion that the trial court abused its discretion in denying his request to poll the jury upon return of the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.
