State v. Askew


(14771)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


44 Conn. App. 280; 688 A.2d 1346; 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 50


December 9, 1996, Argued  
February 18, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was identified by his victim after she was brought to a police car in which he was sitting. Defendant contended that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress the victim's out-of-court and in-court identifications, that it improperly excluded impeachment evidence, and that it improperly refused to give a Simmons-Telfaire instruction to the jury. The court held that (1) the out-of-court and in-court identifications by the victim were reliable and were not the result of an improper procedure that was unnecessarily suggestive and conducive to irreparable misidentification; (2) the trial court instructed jurors as to the factors they had to consider in determining the reliability of the identification testimony at trial, the instructions were comprehensive enough to give adequate guidance to jurors and thus, the trial court did not err by failing to give a Telfaire instruction to the jury; and (3) because the trial court properly found that there was no unnecessary suggestiveness in the identification procedure, defendant's claim that the trial court improperly failed to give a Simmons instruction was meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Marsala


(14952)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number five (Connecticut), which found him guilty on 25 counts of harassment in the second degree, in violation of Conn. The statute was previously held to be constitutional and he failed to properly brief the issue for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on 25 counts of harassment in the second degree.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) of possession of narcotics with intent to sell, in violation of Conn. State v. Strickland


(14593)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


42 Conn. App. 768; 682 A.2d 521; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 449


March 18, 1996, Argued  
September 3, 1996, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Information charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Hadden, J.; judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) revoking his probation based on findings that he failed to report as directed to his probation officer, had been carrying a pistol or revolver without a permit, had obliterated the identification number on a pistol or revolver, and had been in criminal possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to multiple offenses and was sentenced to a prison sentence of 11 years, suspended after 4 and 1/2 years, and placed on probation for 3 years. He was released on probation upon the conditions that he comply with all criminal laws and report as directed to his probation officer. Subsequently, defendant's probation officer prepared an arrest warrant application for failure to report to him and for several charges arising out of a shooting incident. The trial court found by a preponderance of the evidence that defendant committed the violations and imposed the remainder of his sentence. On appeal, the judgment was affirmed. The trial court's findings as to the violations were not clearly erroneous. Defendant's unpreserved claim that the trial court improperly refused to disqualify himself was not subject to a plain error review. Neither Connecticut rules of practice nor due process required that he be given the opportunity personally to address the trial court in a probation revocation hearing. Neither Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-32 (b) nor Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. P. § 943 mandated that a presentence investigation report be provided prior to revocation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that revoked defendant's probation.

Town of Haddam v. LaPointe


(14637)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


42 Conn. App. 631; 680 A.2d 1010; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 440


April 24, 1996, Argued  
August 20, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from continuing to use a subsurface sewage disposal system on a year-round basis on certain of the defendant's real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, J. Walsh, J., denied the plaintiffs' application for a temporary injunction; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Hon. Daniel F. Spallone, state trial referee; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a town and its health director, filed an action against defendant property owner, seeking injunctive and other relief for the owner's alleged conversion of a summer cottage into to a year-round residence without meeting the requirements of the public health code, Conn. Agencies Regs. § 19-13-B100. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut) rendered judgment for the owner and plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The director sent the owner a notice of violation stating that she was in violation of § 19-13-B100, by her year-round use of public sewers, and notifying her that she could appeal the order by telephoning the agency within 48 hours and that a letter of appeal was required to be sent within seven days, under Conn. Agencies Regs. § 19-2a-34. The owner timely indicated her intent to appeal the order by telephoning the agency but, because she did not file a letter of appeal timely, her administrative appeal was dismissed. The director then filed the suit to enjoin the owners' year-round use of the sewers. In reversing the superior court's decision that denied plaintiffs' request for injunctive relief, the court agreed with plaintiffs' contention that the superior court improperly required the plaintiffs to prove a violation of the public health code even though the owner failed to exhaust her administrative remedies. The court reasoned that it would violate the exhaustion doctrine and its policy underpinnings to allow a defendant who did not exhaust administrative remedies to defeat an agency's injunction action on issues that could have been contested in the administrative process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Patrick


(15213)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


42 Conn. App. 640; 681 A.2d 380; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 438


June 3, 1996, Argued  
August 20, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of an elementary school, possession of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia in a drug factory situation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographically area number ten, and tried to the jury before Parker, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which convicted him upon a jury verdict of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who was not drug-dependent, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1,500 feet of an elementary school, possession of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia in a drug factory situation.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of several drug-related offenses. Defendant argued that his convictions violated his right not to be placed in double jeopardy, that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a)(b), which proscribed possession of a controlled substance within 1,500 feet of an elementary school, was unconstitutionally vague, and that he was not afforded effective assistance of counsel. The court reasoned that although defendant's convictions arose out of the same transaction, the convictions did not violate double jeopardy because there was adequate legislative intent that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a)(b) authorized cumulative punishment that could be imposed in addition to a sentence for violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b). Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a)(b) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant because a person of ordinary intelligence should have known that the prohibited activity of possessing cocaine with intent to sell would also be illegal within 1,500 feet of a school. Habeas corpus was the proper vehicle for review of defendant's ineffective assistance claims because of the opportunity for an evidentiary hearing afforded by a habeas corpus proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant upon a jury verdict of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who was not drug-dependent, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1,500 feet of an elementary school, possession of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia in a drug factory situation.

987 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nokes


(14355)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


42 Conn. App. 10; 678 A.2d 510; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 335


April 2, 1996, Argued  
July 2, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, and tried to the jury before Scheinblum, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Geographical Area Number 15 (Connecticut), of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(a).


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, in violation of § 14-227a(a). Defendant appealed contending that the trial court's jury instruction unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof from the state to defendant, and that because he had presented evidence to rebut the presumption, the jury should not have been instructed on the presumption at all. The court affirmed the conviction. The court found that the charge allowed the jury to make a permissive inference in that it could consider the test results and attach whatever weight it chose to them. The charge did not impermissibly allow the State to use an evidentiary presumption to relieve itself of its burden of persuasion beyond a reasonable doubt of every essential element of a crime. The jury was never instructed that the presumption or inference was mandatory, and the burden of persuasion never shifted. Further, nothing in § 14-227a(c) implied that the production of evidence to rebut the presumption eliminated the presumption if the jury chooses to believe the facts underlying the presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor.

Sherman v. Sherman


(14552)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


41 Conn. App. 803; 678 A.2d 9; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 313


February 28, 1996, Argued  
June 25, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Bassick, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief; thereafter, the matter was referred to Edmund H. Miller, family support magistrate, who denied the defendant's motion for modification of the child support award and ordered the defendant to make certain payments, and the defendant appealed to the Superior Court; thereafter, the court, Bassick, J., granted the attorney general's motion to dismiss the appeal and rendered judgment thereon, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband was ordered by a family support magistrate to pay weekly child support to plaintiff wife; an arrearage was found, and the husband was ordered to pay $ 1,500 on the arrearage. The husband appealed to the Superior Court (Connecticut), which dismissed the appeal based on a lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband filed an appeal form (JD-FM-111) within 14 days of the family support magistrate's order. The husband did not file a separate petition with the appeal form as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-231(n). Affirming the trial court's dismissal of the appeal, the court held that the husband had failed to comply with the strict statutory requirements. The appeal form itself stated that a petition was required to be filed with the form. The form was not itself the equivalent of a petition because it provided no place for the husband to give notice of his claims or challenges to the ruling of the magistrate. Because the husband lacked standing, the court lacked jurisdiction and properly dismissed the appeal. The court rejected the attorney general's contention that the appeal was moot based on the husband's payment of the $ 1,500 toward the arrearage because the appeal could have challenged more than the lump sum payment. The court rejected the husband's claim that § 46b-231(n) was unconstitutional because the husband had sought the benefits of the statute. Any relief arising from unconstitutionality could not be claimed in the present action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the husband's appeal.

 

989 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Korhn


(14345)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


41 Conn. App. 874; 678 A.2d 492; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 340


December 12, 1995, Argued  
June 25, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number ten, and tried to the jury before O'Keefe, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), geographical area number 10, which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of liquor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding and failed the field sobriety tests administered by two state troopers. Defendant was taken to the barracks where a breathalyzer test taken 90 minutes after he was stopped. He registered a blood alcohol content (BAC) of 0.169. A second breathalyzer test taken 41 minutes after the first one registered a BAC of 0.170. Defendant was subsequently convicted upon a jury verdict of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(a)(2). On appeal, the court affirmed and held that defendant had standing to challenge the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(c) as amended by 1993 Conn. Acts No. 93-371 (Reg. Sess.) only insofar as it applied to him. The rebuttable presumption in amended § 14-227a(c) that the BAC at the time defendant was stopped was the same as it was at the time of the first test without the need for an expert's extrapolation testimony was a permissive inference. That inference did not shift the burden of proof on and element of the offense to defendant because the trial court did not instruct the jury that the presumption was mandatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in all respects.

 

990 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jenkins


(12465)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


41 Conn. App. 604; 679 A.2d 3; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 283


November 7, 1995, Argued  
June 11, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of cocaine by a person who is not drug-dependent, sale of cocaine and possession of cocaine brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, and tried to the jury before Rittenband, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him after a jury trial of sale of cocaine by a person who was not drug-dependent in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b), sale of cocaine in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a), and possession of cocaine in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court violated his state and federal constitutional rights to a fair trial and to due process of law when it denied his motion to bifurcate the trial to consider separately the issue of drug dependency. The court upheld defendant's conviction and sentence. First, the court held that drug dependency was not an element of the offense, but was an exemption from liability. A person charged with sale of narcotics pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) was presumed not to have been drug-dependent, but could avoid liability under § 21a-278(b) by proving by a preponderance of the evidence that he was drug-dependent at the time of the offense. Second, the court concluded that the issue of drug dependency was not a sentencing factor, but was more akin to an affirmative defense. Thus, the court held that the defense of drug dependency did not require a bifurcated hearing. Third, the court held that a defendant's voluntary decision to maintain mutually inconsistent defenses did not result in a due process violation that required separate trials. Finally, the court held that the jury charge as a whole did not mislead the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Phidd


(13999)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


42 Conn. App. 17; 681 A.2d 310; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 337


November 27, 1995, Argued  
May 23, 1996 *, Officially Released


* May 23, 1996, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 3, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 1556.


PRIOR HISTORY: Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell and possession of marijuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before McGrath, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of marijuana with intent to sell, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Fairfield Judicial District Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted him of possession of marijuana with intent to sell under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21(a)-277(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another individual were arrested after an officer observed them engaging in drug activity. Initially, they were tried together with the same counsel, however, the State entered a nolle with respect to the individual. The jury was instructed not to concern itself with why the individual was taken out of their consideration. Defendant did not file an immediate appeal and, pursuant to a request, a habeas court restored defendant's appellate rights. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court determined that the habeas court had the power to restore defendant's appellate rights because the parties stipulated that defendant did not knowingly waive his rights to a direct appeal. Despite defendant's contention, the court found that the trial court did not err in failing to inform of a potential conflict of interest in the joint representation because the issue was not raised at trial, defendant did not establish a clear constitutional violation, and the trial court was not required to inquire into a possible conflict. The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to declare a mistrial on the basis of the alleged conflict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Rogers


(13685)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


41 Conn. App. 204; 674 A.2d 1364; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 207


October 23, 1995, Argued  
April 30, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction following a jury trial in the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction, claiming that the trial court improperly permitted the State to inject the issue of defendant's religious beliefs during his cross-examination. Noting that when defendant brought a Bible to the witness stand he presented himself as a religious person and opened the door to cross-examination concerning how his religious beliefs were consistent with his prior acts, the court declined to reach the merits of whether it was proper to allow the questioning because defendant failed to object at trial and the claim was not of constitutional magnitude. The court reversed the conviction on the ground that the trial court abused its discretion by allowing the State to ask defendant questions requiring defendant to assume that he was guilty. The court ruled that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant access to a witness's psychiatric records when the trial court had performed an in camera inspection of the records and determined that the records did not contain probative information. The court also ruled that the trial court did not improperly refuse to ask the witness to allow defendant access to the records.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Corbeil


(13990)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


41 Conn. App. 7; 674 A.2d 454; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 180


January 23, 1996, Argued  
April 9, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number twelve, and tried to the jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) for operating a motor vehicle on a public highway while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or any drug or both in violation of Con. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for driving under the influence of alcohol and contended that the superior court erred in admitting into evidence certain statements he made after he had been given Miranda warnings and while excluding statements made before he had been given those warnings. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and concluded that defendant's statement regarding him having been drinking beer at a club for approximately six hours was admissible. The court ruled that the statement, given after the Miranda warnings, was not tainted by the alleged illegal first confession during defendant's arrest. The court found that the initial first statement had been given voluntarily while in custody and without the Miranda warnings, and such statements did not automatically required the exclusion of other statements made after the Miranda warnings had been given. The court found that the actions and words of defendant were sufficient to allow the superior court to infer a waiver of his Miranda rights. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. §14-227a(f) was not unconstitutionally vague and the State was permitted to present evidence of defendant's refusal to submit to a breath test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment of conviction against defendant for operating a motor vehicle on a public highway while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or any drug or both.

State v. Carolina


(13885)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


40 Conn. App. 762; 673 A.2d 562; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 154


December 6, 1995, Argued  
March 26, 1996, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of cocaine and disregarding the signal of a police officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before Stodolink, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court in the District of Danbury (Connecticut) of possession of a narcotic substance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 21a-279(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by police for operating a motor vehicle without a license and was arrested for violating Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 14-36a. While defendant remained at the scene the officer searched defendant's car and found narcotics. Defendant was subsequently charged with possession of a narcotic substance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 21a-279(a). defendant was convicted and appealed. He argued that the search was illegal in that his custodial arrest was not permitted on a crime punishable solely by a fine. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 14-140(a) gave the officer discretion to arrest defendant, and that the arrest practice manual also gave the officer such discretion. The court held that because defendant was also arrested for disregarding the signal of a police officer, which was not punishable by mail, the arrest was proper. In affirming the conviction, the court held that because defendant was lawfully arrested and detained at the scene, his vehicle could be searched. The court held that the selection of defendant's venire from a subdivision of the district did not violate his right to have a jury selected from a fair cross section of the community.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant on the charge of possession of a narcotic substance.

 

995 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Van Snyder


(13785)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


40 Conn. App. 544; 672 A.2d 535; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 130


November 2, 1995, Argued  
March 12, 1996, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations charging the defendant with five counts of the crime of harassment in the second degree and five counts of the crime of disorderly conduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, where the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the court, Keller, J., granted the defendant's motions to dismiss the informations and rendered judgments thereon, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with five counts of harassment in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(2). The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) granted defendant's motion to dismiss the informations against him. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's supervisors suspended him from his job as a high school principal for one week. Thereafter, they began to receive unwanted magazine subscriptions and other mail order items. Defendant was charged with five counts of harassment in the second degree in violation of § 53a-183(a)(2). The trial court dismissed the charges. On appeal, the court held that a direct communication from a defendant to his victim was not required to establish a violation of that provision. Section 53a-183(a)(2) provided that a person was guilty of harassment in the second degree when, with the intent to harass, annoy, or alarm another, he communicated with a person by mail in a manner likely to cause annoyance or alarm. Thus, the plain language of the statute did not require a direct communication with the person targeted for harassment. Moreover, courts were not permitted to read into a statute provisions that were not clearly stated or to render its words and phrases mere surplusage. Therefore, the court concluded that a direct communication was not required under § 53a-183(a)(2).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of the charges against defendant for harassment in the second degree.

Bombero v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


(13780)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


40 Conn. App. 75; 669 A.2d 598; 1996 Conn. App. LEXIS 7


September 27, 1995, Argued  
January 9, 1996, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a judgment declaring null and void certain amendments to the defendant's zoning regulations, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Vertefeuille, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner challenged a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which found in favor of defendant zoning commission in plaintiff's action for a judgment declaring null and void certain amendments to defendant's zoning regulations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff challenged defendant's zoning regulations, claiming that they had an adverse and unconstitutional impact on plaintiff. The trial court found in favor of defendant and refused to grant declaratory relief. The court reversed the decision of the trial court and held plaintiff showed the requisite degree of uncertainty as to his rights as a property owner. Plaintiff had standing to bring a declaratory judgment action because he was adversely affected by the regulation. The fact that plaintiff owned subdividable property, which was clearly within the purview of the zoning regulation, coupled with his legislative attack on the regulation, based primarily on constitutional vagueness grounds, constituted sufficient grounds to seek declaratory relief. Defendant was not prejudiced by plaintiff's failure to allege that the disputed regulation caused plaintiff to be uncertain as to his rights as an owner of potentially subdividable property. As an owner of property that had the potential for subdivision, plaintiff was entitled to be able to ascertain with reasonable certainty the validity of the adopted regulation and its affect on his rights as a property owner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the suit challenging zoning regulations for further proceedings.

State v. Payne


(12993)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


40 Conn. App. 1; 669 A.2d 582; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 529


September 14, 1995, Argued  
December 26, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of risk of injury to a child and with two counts of the crime of coercion, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Ripley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of risk of injury to a child and one count of coercion, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of risk to injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, and of misdemeanor coercion in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-192.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court: (1) improperly denied his motions for judgment of acquittal and for judgment notwithstanding the verdict on the charge of risk of injury to a child, because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 was unconstitutionally vague and indefinite;, (2) incorrectly instructed the jury on the elements of § 53-21; and (3) improperly denied his motion for judgment of acquittal in which he claimed that there was insufficient evidence to support the convictions. On appeal, the court found that defendant's conduct created a situation inimical to the mental health of the minor child and that § 53-21 was not unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the trial court properly exercised its discretion in refusing to instruct the jury as defendant requested. The court determined that the cumulative effect of the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction of misdemeanor coercion beyond a reasonable doubt. In addition, the court determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to allow defendant's four relatives to testify, as to statements allegedly made by defendant, on the ground that the challenged evidence was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant.

CTB Ventures 55 v. Rubenstein


(14193)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


39 Conn. App. 684; 667 A.2d 1272; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 462


September 20, 1995, Argued  
November 14, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage on certain real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Hon. Donald W. Celotto, state trial referee, granted the plaintiff's motion for judgment of strict foreclosure and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court, Zoarski, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for a deficiency judgment and rendered judgment against the named defendant, from which the named defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, New Haven Judicial District (Connecticut), which awarded a deficiency judgment to appellee lender following the foreclosure sale of the home. The homeowner argued that he was entitled to a jury trial on the deficiency judgment proceeding and that trial court committed several errors as to procedure and the admission of evidence.


OVERVIEW: After it purchased the homeowner's house pursuant to a default foreclosure judgment, the lender sought a deficiency judgment as to the unsatisfied portion of the debt. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-14. The court addressed the homeowner's claims of error as follows. First, the homeowner did not ask for a jury trial at the hearing and thus that alleged error was not preserved for review; in any event, the court held that Conn. Const. art. 1, § 19 did not mandate a jury trial in a deficiency proceeding. Second, the lender erred in not disclosing an expert witness but again the homeowner did not object and the issue was not preserved. Third, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in reopening or continuing the hearing for additional testimony. Fourth, the homeowner could not challenge the underlying debt established in the default foreclosure judgment in the appeal on the deficiency judgment; that matter was closed. Fifth, there was sufficient evidence as to the value of the property and the lender did make a prima facie case. Sixth, the introduction of microfiche copies of checks rather than the originals was permitted under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-180(a), (c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's deficiency judgment on behalf of the lender and against the homeowner that was entered pursuant to an action in foreclosure.

Santiago v. Commissioner of Correction


(14219), (14220), 14221), (14223), (14224)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


39 Conn. App. 674; 667 A.2d 304; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 461


September 21, 1995, Argued  
November 14, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petitions for writs of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Sferrazza, J., granted the respondent's motions to quash and rendered judgments dismissing the petitions, from which the petitioners, on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals to this court.
Cubano v. Warden, 1994 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2661 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 24, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Judgment in the fourth appeal reversed, further proceedings; judgment in the other appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Five petitioners sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which granted respondent state commissioner of correction's motions to quash and dismissed the petitions for writs of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, inmates in state correctional facilities, were all designated as members of a security risk group pursuant to an administrative directive. Petitioners claimed that the labels were false and unconstitutional. Specifically, petitioners alleged that such designation violated their constitutional rights to due process under Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 10 and U.S. Const. amend. V, XIV. They also claimed the designation violated their constitutional right to be free from cruel and unusual punishment. The court found that all but one of the petitioners failed to allege sufficient facts to support a constitutional due process claim. However, one petitioner invoked the subject matter jurisdiction of the trial court in a habeas corpus proceeding by alleging that his failure to receive good time credits that would have shorted his time of commitment was arbitrarily abrogated by the designation. Petitioners failed to allege sufficient facts demonstrating an Eighth Amendment violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the motion to quash the petition filed by one inmate who alleged he lost good time credits based on his designation as a member of a security risk group. The court affirmed order that quashed the other four petitions.

 

1000 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lemoine


(11701)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


39 Conn. App. 657; 666 A.2d 825; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 458


September 7, 1995, Submitted  
November 7, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of sexual assault in the third degree, assault of a peace officer, attempt to commit assault in the first degree and reckless endangerment in the first degree, and with one count of the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, and tried to the jury before Stengel, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of assault of a peace officer and one count each of sexual assault in the third degree and risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial on the charges of which the defendant had been convicted, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Supreme Court, which reversed the judgment of this court and remanded the case to this court for further proceedings.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with third degree sexual assault, assault of a peace officer, attempt to commit first degree assault, first degree reckless endangerment, and risk of injury to a child. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) held him guilty of peace officer assault, sexual assault and risk of injury. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The only remaining claim in the appeal was defendant's claim that the superior court improperly instructed the jury on the crime of risk of injury to a child. The court was not persuaded that the instructions as to the crime were improper. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment of the superior court, which correctly set forth the elements of the crime, and which had not expanded the information by instructing the jury on a statutory or factual alternative not charged in the information. Therefore, an unconstitutional enlargement was not in issue. The instruction was not a kind that the court considered in the context of the test for enlargement to determine whether a constitutional violation existed that clearly deprived defendant of a fair trial. The court concluded that the court's jury instructions, when examined as a whole and in the context of the entire trial, achieved their purpose of assisting the jury in applying the law. The court also concluded that it was not reasonably possible that the jury was misled by the instructions and that no injustice to defendant resulted by reason of the instructions. Therefore, no due process violation existed under the constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
